Full turn-by-turn text loads with corrections highlighted.

TC-02

Play back a voice turn

Original audio plays inline.

TC-03

Open a session whose audio was deleted

Transcript text shows with an "audio unavailable" note.

TC-04

Open a crashed/partial session

Available turns show with an incomplete-session banner.

TC-05

Open transcript while offline

Loading/sync-pending state shows instead of a blank screen.



AIC-US-03: Proficiency-Level Adaptive Conversation Difficulty

STATUS: Proposed PRIORITY: High ACTOR: Learner

Intent: To automatically calibrate the AI's vocabulary complexity, sentence length, and pacing to match the learner's current Confidence Score, so every session stays appropriately challenging.

Happy Path Steps

Session Start: User begins any AI Conversation Practice topic.

Level Lookup: System retrieves the current Confidence Score / CEFR level from the Baseline Assessment engine.

Calibrated Opening: AI opens with vocabulary/complexity matched to that level.

Dynamic Adjustment: If the user's responses are notably more or less complex than expected, the AI adjusts its complexity within the same session.

Session End: Feedback notes the difficulty level the session was conducted at.

Acceptance Criteria

Initial calibration must automatically use the latest Confidence Score, without requiring manual selection.

Mid-session adjustment must change the level no more than once per session, to avoid jarring shifts.

Users must be able to manually override the auto-detected level via a settings toggle.

Exception Handling

E-01: No Baseline Score on File. A new user hasn't completed the Baseline Assessment. RESOLUTION: Default to a neutral "Intermediate" calibration and prompt the user to complete the Baseline Assessment.

E-02: Significantly Stale Score. The Confidence Score is more than 90 days old. RESOLUTION: Use the stale score but flag in-session: "Your level may have changed — consider retaking your Baseline Assessment."

E-03: Manual Override to a Mismatched Level. A beginner-level user manually selects "Advanced." RESOLUTION: Allow the override but show a one-time warning that content will be harder than their assessed level.

E-04: Level Oscillation Risk. The user's responses vary wildly within one session (e.g., pasting advanced text). RESOLUTION: Ignore single outlier turns; adjust the level only based on a rolling average of the last 3 turns.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-01

User with a known Confidence Score starts a session

AI's opening vocabulary automatically matches the stored level.

TC-02

New user with no baseline data

Session defaults to Intermediate and prompts a baseline assessment.

TC-03

User consistently answers above their level

AI raises complexity once, based on rolling average, not per turn.

TC-04

Manual override to a harder level

Override applies with a one-time difficulty warning.

TC-05

One outlier advanced response mid-session

AI doesn't overreact to the single outlier turn.



AIC-US-04: Real-Time Inline Grammar Correction Toggle

STATUS: Proposed PRIORITY: Medium ACTOR: Learner

Intent: To let the learner opt into lightweight, real-time grammar correction suggestions during chat, instead of waiting for the end-of-session summary, for learners who prefer immediate feedback.

Happy Path Steps

Settings: User enables "Show corrections during chat" in session settings.

Turn Submission: User sends a message containing a grammar error.

Inline Suggestion: A subtle correction chip appears beneath the user's message (e.g., "did → done").

Continued Flow: The AI's conversational reply proceeds normally, unaffected by the chip.

Session End: The full list of corrections is also included in the post-session review.

Acceptance Criteria

Real-time corrections must never block or delay the AI's conversational response.

The feature must be off by default to preserve the casual, no-dead-ends flow.

Corrections must apply only to grammar/spelling, never tone or content.

Exception Handling

E-01: Correction Contradicts a Regional English Variant. User writes valid British English (e.g., "colour," "whilst"). RESOLUTION: System checks the user's English-variant setting and suppresses the false-positive correction.

E-02: Correction Overload on a Heavily Broken Sentence. Message has 5+ errors. RESOLUTION: Cap the visible chip to the single highest-impact error.

E-03: Voice-Mode Correction Timing. User is in voice mode, where text chips would clutter the UI. RESOLUTION: Suppress inline chips in voice mode; corrections appear in the end-of-session summary.

E-04: Correction Service Latency. The grammar-checking service responds slower than the AI's reply. RESOLUTION: Show the AI's reply immediately; append the chip asynchronously once ready — never delay the conversation.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-01

Toggle enabled, minor grammar error sent

Correction chip appears without delaying the AI reply.

TC-02

Valid British English spelling used

No false-positive correction shown.

TC-03

Message with many errors sent

Only the single highest-impact correction shown.

TC-04

Feature used in voice mode

No inline chips appear; corrections surface only in the summary.

TC-05

Grammar service responds slowly

AI reply appears on time; chip appears later.



AIC-US-05: Session Interruption & Auto-Resume Handling

STATUS: Proposed PRIORITY: High ACTOR: Learner

Intent: To gracefully handle real-world interruptions (incoming calls, app backgrounding, connectivity loss) during an active session, so the learner can resume without losing progress.

Happy Path Steps

Active Session: User is mid-conversation in voice mode.

Interruption: An incoming call or app-switch event occurs.

Auto-Pause: App detects the interruption, pauses the timer, and saves state.

Return: User returns to the app.

Resume Prompt: App offers "Resume where you left off" or "Start a new session," continuing seamlessly if resumed.

Acceptance Criteria

Session state must persist for at least 30 minutes after an interruption.

Resuming must not repeat the AI's last question.

If the user declines to resume, the partial session must still be scored, not discarded.

Exception Handling

E-01: Interruption Exceeds the Timeout Window. User returns more than 30 minutes later. RESOLUTION: Session auto-submits using data up to the interruption point; a fresh session is required for further practice.

E-02: App Force-Closed During Interruption. OS kills the app entirely. RESOLUTION: On next launch, the app detects the orphaned session and offers the same resume prompt.

E-03: Network Loss Coincides with the Interruption. Connectivity drops at the same time. RESOLUTION: Cache unsent turns locally and sync once connectivity and foreground state are restored.

E-04: Multiple Interruptions in One Session. User is interrupted, resumes, then interrupted again. RESOLUTION: Each interruption independently re-arms the 30-minute timeout, with no fluency score penalty.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-01

Incoming call interrupts a voice session

Session pauses and resumes seamlessly on return.

TC-02

User returns after 45 minutes

Session auto-submits using data before the interruption.

TC-03

App is force-closed by the OS

Next launch detects and offers to resume the orphaned session.

TC-04

Connectivity drops during the interruption

Unsent turns sync automatically once back online and foregrounded.

TC-05

Two interruptions occur back-to-back

Timeout resets each time with no fluency score penalty.



AIC-US-06: Cross-Session Personalization Memory

STATUS: Proposed PRIORITY: Medium ACTOR: Learner

Intent: To have the AI remember durable personal facts (job, hobbies, goals) shared in past sessions and naturally reference them on different days, so conversations feel continuous.

Happy Path Steps

Fact Capture: During a session, the user mentions a durable fact (e.g., "I work as a nurse").

Memory Storage: System tags and stores the fact against the user's profile.

New Session, Later Day: User starts a new session on a different topic.

Contextual Callback: AI naturally references the stored fact (e.g., "As a nurse, do you find shift work makes it hard to practice regularly?").

Session End: New durable facts are added to the memory store.

Acceptance Criteria

Stored facts must be limited to conversation-relevant, non-sensitive categories (job, hobbies, interests, goals).

Users must be able to view/delete individual remembered facts from settings.

Callbacks must appear no more than once or twice per session.

Exception Handling

E-01: User Corrects a Previously Stored Fact. User says "Actually, I changed jobs." RESOLUTION: System updates the stored fact and discards the outdated version.

E-02: User Opts Out of Memory. User disables "Remember me across sessions." RESOLUTION: System stops storing new facts and purges existing facts within 24 hours.

E-03: Sensitive Fact Volunteered. User shares a health condition or financial detail. RESOLUTION: System does not persist sensitive-category facts to long-term memory, even when memory is enabled.

E-04: Conflicting Facts Across Sessions. User states contradictory facts (e.g., different job titles) without correction. RESOLUTION: System retains only the most recently stated fact, silently overwriting the older value.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-01

User mentions their job, chats again a week later

AI references the job naturally in the later session.

TC-02

User explicitly corrects a stored fact

Old fact is overwritten and no longer referenced.

TC-03

User disables cross-session memory

Facts are purged within 24 hours; no new facts stored.

TC-04

User shares a health condition

Fact is not added to long-term memory.

TC-05

User states two different job titles in separate sessions

Only the most recent title is retained and referenced.



AIC-US-07: Sensitive Personal Information (PII) Safety Handling

STATUS: Proposed PRIORITY: High ACTOR: Learner

Intent: To ensure the AI responds safely when a learner volunteers sensitive personal information during casual practice, protecting privacy and never encouraging further disclosure.

Happy Path Steps

Normal Interaction: User is engaged in casual conversation practice.

PII Detection: User volunteers a full home address, national ID, or card number.

Real-Time Redaction: System detects the PII pattern and prevents the raw value from being stored or forwarded, substituting a placeholder.

Safe Response: AI acknowledges the message without repeating the details, and gently reminds the user not to share sensitive data.

Session Continues: Conversation resumes on the original topic.

Acceptance Criteria

Detected PII must never be stored in transcripts or long-term memory, redacted or not.

The AI's reminder must appear at most once per session.

The AI must never ask a follow-up that invites further sensitive detail.

Exception Handling

E-01: Financial Information Shared. User shares a card/bank account number. RESOLUTION: System redacts the value immediately, AI responds generically ("Thanks for sharing, let's keep chatting!"), with a passive on-screen reminder.

E-02: Government ID Shared. User shares a national ID/passport number. RESOLUTION: Same redaction/reminder flow, logged as a privacy-safety event without exposing the actual value.

E-03: Third-Party PII Shared. User shares another person's private info (e.g., a friend's phone number). RESOLUTION: Third-party data is redacted identically to first-party PII.

E-04: Repeated PII Sharing After Warning. User shares sensitive data again after being reminded. RESOLUTION: AI repeats a brief, calm reminder without being punitive or ending the session.

E-05: False-Positive PII Detection. System misflags a normal number (e.g., a fictional role-play number) as PII. RESOLUTION: Redaction happens silently regardless of accuracy; conversation continues smoothly.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-01

User shares a credit card number

Value is redacted; AI gives a generic response + one-time reminder.

TC-02

User shares a national ID number

Same flow applies; event is logged for audit.

TC-03

User shares a friend's phone number

Third-party data is redacted the same as first-party PII.

TC-04

User shares PII again after the reminder

A calm repeat reminder is shown; session is not ended.

TC-05

A fictional number is misflagged as PII

Conversation continues smoothly with no visible disruption.



AIC-US-08: Conversation Input Abuse & Rate-Limiting Protection

STATUS: Proposed PRIORITY: Medium ACTOR: Learner

Intent: To protect the AI Conversation Practice experience and backend resources from spam, gibberish flooding, or automated abuse, ensuring genuine learners get a responsive experience.

Happy Path Steps

Normal Use: User exchanges messages at a typical human pace.

Rate Monitor: System silently tracks message frequency and patterns.

Threshold Check: All activity stays within normal human bounds.

Uninterrupted Practice: Session proceeds without throttling.

Session End: Session completes and is scored normally.

Acceptance Criteria

Normal conversational pacing must never trigger a rate limit.

Abuse detection must not degrade the experience for legitimate fast typists/voice responders.

Any throttling action must be logged for admin-side abuse analytics.

Exception Handling

E-01: Rapid-Fire Message Flooding. User sends 15+ messages within 10 seconds. RESOLUTION: Send button temporarily disables for a cooldown, displaying "Let's slow down a bit — take your time."

E-02: Repetitive Gibberish Input. User repeatedly sends nonsensical text to break the AI. RESOLUTION: AI clarifies a limited number of times, then ends the session early with a generic message if the pattern persists.

E-03: Prompt Injection Attempt. User tries to make the AI ignore its role or reveal system instructions. RESOLUTION: AI declines to comply, stays in persona, and continues the original topic.

E-04: Automated/Bot-Like Cadence Detected. Messages arrive at suspiciously uniform intervals. RESOLUTION: System flags the session for backend review and may present a human-verification challenge.

E-05: Legitimate Burst Misclassified. A voice note dictation results in several quick text fragments submitted together. RESOLUTION: System batches submissions arriving within a 2-second window into a single turn, rather than treating them as flooding.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-01

User sends messages at a normal human pace

No throttling occurs at any point.

TC-02

User sends 20 messages in 8 seconds

Send button cools down and a slow-down message is shown.

TC-03

User repeatedly sends gibberish text

AI clarifies a limited number of times, then session ends gracefully.

TC-04

User attempts a prompt injection

AI ignores the injected instruction and stays in persona.

TC-05

Voice note is split into rapid text fragments

Fragments are batched into one turn rather than flagged as flooding.



AIC-US-09: AI Conversation Practice

STATUS: In Development PRIORITY: Medium ACTOR: Learner

Intent: To practice conversational English with an AI on real-life topics to improve speaking ability without a human partner.

Happy Path Steps

Topic Selection: User selects a real-life topic (e.g., Daily Life, Travel, Work).

Interaction: User speaks or types a message to the AI.

AI Response: AI analyzes the input, simulates a natural response, and asks a follow-up to keep the conversation going.

Session End: User ends the chat, and the system logs the session duration.

Acceptance Criteria

Must support switching between text and voice input seamlessly mid- conversation.

AI responses must include a conversational hook/question to prevent dead ends.

Exception Handling

E-01: AI Transcription Failure. Speech-to-text service cannot decode the user's accent or pronunciation. RESOLUTION: AI responds, "I didn't quite catch that, could you say it one more time?"

E-02: Content Safety Trigger (Inappropriate Language). User uses profanity or explicit language. RESOLUTION: AI blocks the response, states, "Let's keep the conversation professional," and resets the turn.

E-03: LLM Generation Timeout. AI backend takes longer than 5 seconds to generate a response. RESOLUTION: Display typing indicator indefinitely until 10s timeout, then show "Connection slow, retrying..." banner.

E-04: Empty Submission. User clicks send without typing or recording. RESOLUTION: Disable send button until input length >

E-05: User Goes Completely Off-Topic. User ignores the chosen scenario (e.g., starts talking about sports in a "Travel" scenario). RESOLUTION: AI acknowledges the input briefly but gently steers the conversation back to the selected topic.

Validation Test Cases

 Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

 TC-0 01

Voice turn execution

AI accurately transcribes and responds in <3 seconds.

 TC-0 02

Switch mode mid-session

User types, then speaks next turn; system handles both.

 TC-0 03

Profanity input

Content blocked, AI issues a polite redirect warning.

 TC-0 04

Silence on voice recording

System detects 0s audio length and prompts user to retry.

 TC-0 05

Completing a 5-minute session

System logs time against the "Daily Challenge" metric.

AIC-US-10: AI Conversation Practice - Daily Life & Hobbies

STATUS: In Development PRIORITY: High ACTOR: Learner

Intent: To engage in casual, low-pressure English practice about daily routines, hobbies, and general interests to build foundational fluency.

Happy Path Steps

Topic Selection: User selects "Daily Life" from the AI Conversation Practice menu.

Initiation: AI asks an open-ended question (e.g., "What do you usually do on weekends?").

Interaction: User speaks about their hobbies or routine.

Dynamic Follow-up: AI picks up on a specific detail (e.g., "Oh, you like playing cricket? What's your favorite team?") to keep the chat going.

Session End: User finishes the 5-minute chat and receives a fluency score.

Acceptance Criteria

The AI must actively identify and ask follow-up questions based on specific nouns/verbs the user mentions.

The tone must remain casual and encouraging, distinctly different from the "Workplace" or "Interview" coaches.

Exception Handling

E-01: Single-Word Answers. User replies "Nothing" or "Yes" repeatedly. RESOLUTION: AI gently probes: "Sometimes quiet weekends are the best! Did you watch any movies or just relax?" to force a longer response.

E-02: Morbid/Depressing Topics. User starts talking about severe depression or self-harm in response to "How is your day?". RESOLUTION: AI breaks the casual persona, provides a supportive, empathetic statement, and offers a gentle pivot or standard helpline resources (Safety constraint).

E-03: Repetitive Topic Loop. User gives the exact same daily routine answer every day. RESOLUTION: AI memory detects the repetition and prompts a new angle: "You mentioned working out before. What's your favorite exercise?"

E-04: Extremely Long Monologue. User speaks for 5 uninterrupted minutes without letting the AI respond. RESOLUTION: The system allows the recording to finish, but feedback suggests practicing conversational back-and-forth rather than monologuing.

Validation Test Cases

 Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

 TC-0 01

Normal hobby discussion

AI asks contextual follow-up questions based on the hobby.

 TC-0 02

Single word answers

AI actively prompts user to expand their answers.

 TC-0 03

Repeated topics across days

AI references past chats to push the conversation in a new direction.

 TC-0 04

Long monologue

Feedback notes low "Active Dialogue" pacing.

 TC-0 05

Inappropriate/unsafe topic

AI halts casual chat and issues a safety protocol response.

Session End: User completes a 5-minute back-and-forth and receives their Fluency and Vocabulary scores.

Acceptance Criteria

The AI must utilize a general knowledge base to ask contextually accurate follow- ups about global destinations.

The conversation must prioritize descriptive language (adjectives and storytelling) over rigid transactional language.

Exception Handling

E-02: Lack of Travel Experience. User says "I have never traveled anywhere." RESOLUTION: AI gracefully pivots the prompt from past experience to future desires: "That's completely okay! Is there a city in your own country you'd love to visit?"

E-03: Safety/Political Trigger. User attempts to pivot the travel conversation into a highly sensitive geopolitical conflict zone. RESOLUTION: AI politely deflects, maintains neutrality, and steers the topic back to casual travel and culture.

Exception Handling

E-03: Overly Dense Technical Jargon. User is an engineer and starts discussing complex backend code architecture. RESOLUTION: AI maintains the conversation but reminds the user that the primary goal is assessing English fluency, not technical system design.

The AI must successfully parse common modern work terms (e.g., "hybrid," "Zoom fatigue," "commute").

E-02: Venting/Highly Negative Tone. User uses the prompt to aggressively complain about their real-life boss. RESOLUTION: AI maintains a neutral, supportive tone and steers the conversation toward constructive career goals rather than validating workplace hostility.

E-03: Confusion with "Interview Coach". User starts answering the casual question as if it were a formal HR interview (e.g., "My greatest weakness is..."). RESOLUTION: AI gently breaks the formal tone: "This isn't an interview, just a casual chat! Let's talk more about your day-to-day."

AIC-US-15: Seamless Voice-to-Text Mode Switching

STATUS: In Development PRIORITY: High ACTOR: Learner

Intent: To switch seamlessly between voice and text input modes during an active AI Conversation practice session if the user's physical environment changes (e.g., walking into a quiet public space).

Happy Path Steps

Active Session: User is actively engaged in a voice-based AI Conversation.

Mode Toggle: User taps the "Keyboard" icon to switch to text mode mid- conversation.

Input Context: The AI retains the full context of the preceding voice conversation.

Text Execution: User types their next response and hits send.

AI Adaptation: AI responds via text (with an option to play audio) and the conversation continues smoothly.

Acceptance Criteria

The switch between voice and text must not reset the conversation history or context.

The final session scorecard must accurately reflect the hybrid input modes (e.g., scoring pronunciation only for the voice segments).

Exception Handling

E-01: Network Drop During Toggle. User switches to text, but connection drops before the text is sent. RESOLUTION: Cache the typed text locally and display a "Waiting for connection..." banner.

E-02: Simultaneous Input Attempt. User begins typing text but accidentally holds the microphone button to record. RESOLUTION: UI locks text input while the microphone is active and clears the text field if the voice note is successfully sent.

E-03: Null Pronunciation Data. A user begins a session in voice mode but switches to text after only 1 second of audio. RESOLUTION: System drops the Pronunciation metric from the session entirely if the total audio sample size is too small to accurately score.

Validation Test Cases

 Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

 TC-0 01

Switch voice to text session

mid- Conversation continues seamlessly; history is retained.

 TC-0 02

Switch text to voice session

mid- AI accurately transcribes subsequent audio and responds.

 TC-0 03

Post-session scoring

Hybrid session calculates fluency based on both text speed and audio pacing.

 TC-0 04

Simultaneous input

lock Tapping microphone disables the software keyboard.

 TC-0 05

Short audio sample threshold

Pronunciation score is omitted if audio input < 5 seconds.

AIC-US-16: Text-to-Speech (TTS) Playback for AI Text Chat

STATUS: In Development PRIORITY: Low ACTOR: Learner

Intent: To listen to the AI's generated text responses spoken aloud during a text-mode session, allowing the user to practice listening comprehension and hear proper pronunciation.

Happy Path Steps

Execution: User sends a text message to the AI in an active Conversation Practice.

Response: AI generates and displays a text response on the screen.

Action: User taps the "Speaker" icon next to the AI's chat bubble.

Playback: The app's TTS engine reads the text aloud using a natural, human- sounding voice model.

Acceptance Criteria

TTS must utilize a natural-sounding neural voice model, not a robotic/legacy OS voice.

The audio playback must match the exact text displayed on the screen.

Exception Handling

E-01: Device on Silent Mode. The user taps the speaker icon but their hardware physical mute switch is on (iOS). RESOLUTION: App detects the hardware state and displays a brief toast: "Device is muted. Please turn on volume to hear audio."

E-02: External TTS API Failure. The cloud neural voice service times out. RESOLUTION: System gracefully falls back to the native iOS/Android local text-to-speech engine to ensure playback still occurs, albeit at lower quality.

E-03: Interrupted Playback. User taps the speaker icon, but then immediately types and sends their next message. RESOLUTION: Audio playback stops immediately to prevent overlapping with the next turn of the conversation.

E-04: Non-English Text Generation. The AI accidentally hallucinates a response containing foreign characters or code. RESOLUTION: The TTS engine skips unreadable characters or aborts playback for that specific string, logging an error.

Validation Test Cases

 Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

 TC-0 01

Tap speaker icon

Natural TTS engine reads the text aloud accurately.

 TC-0 02

Device hardware muted

UI alerts the user that their device volume is off.

 TC-0 03

Cloud TTS failure

App seamlessly falls back to native OS local voice synthesis.

 TC-0 04

Send message during playback

Active TTS audio stops instantly.

 TC-0 05

Re-play audio

User can tap the speaker icon multiple times to hear it again.

Interview Coach

INT-US-01: Resume/CV & Job-Description-Grounded Question Generation

STATUS: Proposed (Gap)   PRIORITY: High   ACTOR: Job Seeker

Intent: To generate interview questions directly from the user's uploaded resume/CV and/or a pasted job description, so practice reflects the user's real experience and the specific target role instead of generic prompts.

Happy Path Steps

1.      Resume/JD Upload: User uploads their CV (PDF/DOCX) and/or pastes a job description before starting a session.

2.      Parsing: System extracts key experience, skills, and role requirements from the supplied document(s).

3.      Tailored Question Generation: AI generates a blended question set referencing specific resume details (e.g., "You mention leading a team of 5 at X — walk me through that.") alongside JD requirements.

4.      Execution: Mock interview proceeds using the tailored question set.

5.      Feedback: Scorecard notes the alignment between the user's stated resume experience and the answers actually delivered.

Acceptance Criteria

●       At least 40% of generated questions must reference a specific resume detail or a specific JD requirement.

●       The system must never expose or read aloud sensitive personal data (address, phone number, national ID numbers) found on the resume.

Exception Handling

●       E-01: Unparsable/Scanned Resume. User uploads an image-only scanned PDF with no extractable text. RESOLUTION: System notifies the user that text extraction failed and falls back to the standard generic question bank, prompting the user to paste key experience manually.

●       E-02: Resume-JD Mismatch. The user's resume shows no relevant experience for the pasted JD (e.g., a barista resume against a Senior DevOps JD). RESOLUTION: AI proceeds but flags the mismatch and pivots questions toward transferable skills rather than assuming false expertise.

●       E-03: Sensitive Data Detected. Parser detects a CNIC/SSN, home address, or photo embedded in the resume. RESOLUTION: System automatically redacts these fields before they enter the LLM context and confirms redaction to the user.

●       E-04: Resume Upload Failure. The uploaded file exceeds the size limit or is corrupted. RESOLUTION: Display a clear error and allow the user to proceed with a generic interview instead of blocking the session entirely.

●       E-05: Wrong Resume Version Selected. User has multiple saved resumes and selects an outdated one for a role. RESOLUTION: A confirmation step displays the resume filename and last-modified date before the session starts.

●       E-06: Overly Long Job Description Pasted. User pastes an entire multi-page careers-page listing, including benefits and legal boilerplate. RESOLUTION: System truncates to the Responsibilities/Requirements section using keyword extraction before generating questions.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-01

Upload valid PDF resume

Questions reference specific past roles or projects from the resume.

TC-02

Paste JD only, no resume

Questions align tightly to the stated JD requirements.

TC-03

Upload a scanned/image-only PDF

System falls back gracefully to the generic question bank with a notice.

TC-04

Resume contains a phone number/CNIC

Field is redacted and never referenced by the AI.

TC-05

Resume unrelated to the pasted JD

AI flags the mismatch and pivots to transferable-skills questions.

 

INT-US-02: Panel / Group Interview Simulation

STATUS: Proposed (Gap)   PRIORITY: Medium   ACTOR: Job Seeker

Intent: To simulate multi-interviewer panel or group interviews, which are common in HR loops and university admissions, so the user learns to address multiple personas and manage divided attention in a single session.

Happy Path Steps

6.      Panel Setup: User selects "Panel Interview" and chooses 2-3 interviewer personas (e.g., Hiring Manager, HR Representative, Technical Lead).

7.      Introduction: Each AI persona introduces itself with a distinct voice and tone.

8.      Rotating Questioning: Personas take turns asking questions in-character, occasionally interjecting or building on one another's questions.

9.      Address Management: User must direct answers appropriately (e.g., more technical depth toward the Technical Lead).

10.   Feedback: Scorecard breaks down performance per persona rather than a single aggregate score.

Acceptance Criteria

●       The system must maintain clearly distinguishable voices and tones for each concurrent persona.

●       Feedback must be segmented per interviewer, not delivered only as an aggregate score.

Exception Handling

●       E-01: Persona Voice Overlap. Two TTS voices attempt to play simultaneously due to a timing bug. RESOLUTION: System enforces a strict speaking queue so only one persona voice plays at a time.

●       E-02: User Directs Answer to the Wrong Persona. User answers a technical question using purely soft-skills language. RESOLUTION: The Technical Lead persona follows up in-character, requesting more technical specificity.

●       E-03: Panel Fatigue / User Confusion. User loses track of which persona asked what after a long session. RESOLUTION: UI displays a persistent name/role tag identifying the currently "speaking" persona.

●       E-04: One Persona Dominates. Randomized turn logic causes a single persona to ask the large majority of questions. RESOLUTION: Turn-allocation logic enforces a balanced rotation across all selected personas.

●       E-05: Session Drop Mid-Panel. A connectivity issue interrupts a 3-persona session. RESOLUTION: On reconnect, the system resumes with the same persona that was mid-question, preserving full panel state.

●       E-06: Persona Count Misconfiguration. User attempts to select more than 3 personas for a single panel. RESOLUTION: UI caps selection at 3 personas with a tooltip explaining the realistic panel-size limit.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-01

Select a 3-persona panel

Each persona has a distinct voice and questioning style.

TC-02

Technical question answered vaguely

Technical Lead persona probes for further depth.

TC-03

Network drops mid-session

Session resumes with the correct persona and question state.

TC-04

End of panel session

Feedback report is segmented by individual persona.

TC-05

Attempt to add a 4th persona

UI blocks selection beyond the configured cap.

 

INT-US-03: Salary & Offer Negotiation Practice

STATUS: Proposed (Gap)   PRIORITY: High   ACTOR: Job Seeker

Intent: To let users rehearse the negotiation conversation that follows a job offer, since interview preparation currently stops before this critical, anxiety-inducing conversation.

Happy Path Steps

11.   Scenario Selection: User selects "Salary Negotiation" and inputs context (current offer, target range, competing offer if any).

12.   Persona Setup: AI adopts the persona of a hiring manager or recruiter delivering the offer.

13.   Negotiation Dialogue: User practices countering, justifying their ask, and responding to pushback.

14.   Outcome Branching: AI simulates realistic outcomes (partial increase, sign-on bonus offered instead, or a firm decline).

15.   Feedback: Scorecard rates assertiveness, use of market data, and tone (collaborative versus confrontational).

Acceptance Criteria

●       AI must not always concede; the negotiation must include realistic pushback and at least one "no movement" branch.

●       Feedback must reference concrete negotiation techniques (anchoring, framing, strategic pausing) the user did or did not use.

Exception Handling

●       E-01: Unrealistic Ask. User demands an extreme, unjustifiable salary increase. RESOLUTION: AI persona pushes back firmly, and feedback flags the anchor as unrealistic while suggesting market-based ranges.

●       E-02: User Immediately Accepts First Offer. User caves without attempting any counter. RESOLUTION: Post-session feedback specifically flags the missed negotiation opportunity and offers a sample counter-script.

●       E-03: Emotional/Confrontational Tone. User becomes visibly frustrated or aggressive in tone. RESOLUTION: AI persona de-escalates in-character as a professional recruiter would, while feedback separately flags the tone risk.

●       E-04: No Competing Offer Provided. User has no leverage data to input. RESOLUTION: System proceeds using non-monetary leverage points (skills, market demand) rather than blocking the scenario.

●       E-05: Silence Used as a Tactic. User goes silent after receiving a counteroffer, using it deliberately as a pause tactic. RESOLUTION: AI waits an appropriate real-world pause before continuing rather than immediately re-engaging.

●       E-06: Currency/Region Mismatch. User inputs a salary figure in the wrong currency for their stated region. RESOLUTION: System detects the mismatch and asks the user to confirm the currency before proceeding.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-01

User counters with market-backed data

AI persona concedes a partial increase.

TC-02

User accepts the first offer immediately

Feedback flags the missed negotiation opportunity.

TC-03

Unrealistic demand entered

AI firmly declines; feedback notes anchor miscalibration.

TC-04

Aggressive tone used by user

AI stays professional; feedback flags the tone.

TC-05

End of session

Scorecard lists specific negotiation techniques used or missed.

 

INT-US-04: Case Study, Consulting & Brainteaser Interview Simulation

STATUS: Proposed (Gap)   PRIORITY: Medium   ACTOR: Job Seeker

Intent: To prepare users for consulting, product, and strategy interviews involving market-sizing (guesstimates), case frameworks, and brainteasers — a distinct format from coding or behavioral interviews.

Happy Path Steps

16.   Scenario Selection: User selects "Case Study Interview" and chooses a sub-type (Market Sizing, Business Case, or Brainteaser).

17.   Case Delivery: AI presents an open-ended prompt (e.g., estimating a niche local market size).

18.   Structured Reasoning: User thinks aloud while the AI interjects with clarifying data or constraints as a real case interviewer would.

19.   Framework Evaluation: AI evaluates structure (segmentation, stated assumptions, logical math) rather than only the exact numeric answer.

20.   Feedback: Scorecard rates structure, numeracy, and communication of assumptions.

Acceptance Criteria

●       AI must evaluate reasoning structure and assumption clarity, not just the final numeric answer.

●       AI must be capable of injecting realistic follow-up constraints mid-case.

Exception Handling

●       E-01: User Jumps to a Guessed Number. User states a final number with no visible reasoning. RESOLUTION: AI pauses the case and requires the user to walk back through the segmentation logic before the answer is accepted.

●       E-02: Math Error Mid-Calculation. User makes an arithmetic mistake while reasoning aloud. RESOLUTION: AI notes that the structure was sound and scores "approach" separately from "arithmetic accuracy" in the feedback.

●       E-03: Prolonged Silence During Framework-Building. User pauses for an extended period while structuring the case. RESOLUTION: AI offers a mild scaffolding hint rather than remaining silent indefinitely.

●       E-04: Off-Framework Rambling. User discusses unrelated tangents instead of building a structure. RESOLUTION: AI redirects the user back to structuring the problem.

●       E-05: Case Difficulty Mismatch. User selects a difficulty level but struggles significantly or finishes trivially fast. RESOLUTION: System offers to recalibrate the difficulty for the next case in the session.

●       E-06: Ambiguous Clarifying Question from User. User asks a clarifying question the AI has no pre-scripted constraint for. RESOLUTION: AI improvises a reasonable constraint on the fly and keeps it fixed for the rest of that case to avoid contradictions.

INT-US-05: Multi-Round "Interview Day" Simulation

STATUS: Proposed (Gap)   PRIORITY: Medium   ACTOR: Job Seeker

Intent: To simulate a full onsite or virtual interview loop of 2-4 consecutive rounds (e.g., HR Screen, then Technical, then Hiring Manager) with short breaks, mirroring the format changes and fatigue of a real interview day.

Happy Path Steps

21.   Loop Setup: User selects "Full Interview Day" and configures the sequence of round types.

22.   Round Execution: Each round runs using the relevant existing interview-type logic (HR, Technical, etc.).

23.   Inter-Round Break: System inserts a short timed break between rounds, simulating real transition time.

24.   Continuity: Persona context carries forward where realistic (e.g., a later-round persona references what an earlier round noted).

25.   Consolidated Feedback: A single end-of-day report aggregates performance across all rounds, plus a consistency trend across the day.

Acceptance Criteria

●       Each round must retain its own distinct interviewer persona and question style.

●       The consolidated report must show whether performance declined, held steady, or improved across successive rounds.

Exception Handling

●       E-01: User Abandons Mid-Loop. User exits after the first round of a planned three-round loop. RESOLUTION: System saves partial progress and offers to resume the remaining rounds later rather than discarding completed results.

●       E-02: Break Skipped. User immediately proceeds without taking the inter-round break. RESOLUTION: System allows skipping but flags in the report that no recovery break was taken, for the user's own awareness.

●       E-03: Contradictory Answers Across Rounds. User gives conflicting details between rounds (e.g., different reasons for leaving a past job). RESOLUTION: A later-round persona references the discrepancy naturally, as a real interview panel debrief might.

●       E-04: Round Count Misconfiguration. User attempts to configure more than four back-to-back rounds. RESOLUTION: UI caps the loop at four rounds with guidance that real interview days rarely exceed this.

●       E-05: Session Timeout Mid-Loop. Long total session duration triggers an application timeout. RESOLUTION: System auto-saves round-level checkpoints so no completed round's data is lost.

●       E-06: Round Type Duplication. User selects the same interview type twice within one loop. RESOLUTION: System allows it but varies the specific question set between the two instances to avoid repetition.

Validation Test Cases

Scenario

Expected Result

Progress is saved; resume option offered later.

TC-04

Give conflicting answers across rounds

Later persona references the discrepancy.

TC-05

Complete the full loop

Consolidated report shows the performance trend across rounds.

Intent: To let users share a completed mock-interview transcript or recording with a trusted mentor, career counselor, or peer for human feedback, since current feedback is entirely AI-contained.

28.   Access Control: User sets an expiry window and whether the recipient sees audio/video or a transcript-only view.

29.   Recipient Review: The mentor opens the link without needing an account and can leave time-stamped comments.

30.   Consolidated View: User sees mentor comments alongside the AI-generated feedback in one unified view.

Acceptance Criteria

●       Mentor comments must be visually distinguished from AI-generated feedback in the UI.

Exception Handling

●       E-04: Simultaneous Mentor Comments. Two recipients comment on the same timestamp at the same time. RESOLUTION: Both comments are preserved and displayed in submission order rather than overwritten.

●       E-05: Early Access Revocation. User decides to revoke a previously shared link before its expiry. RESOLUTION: A "Revoke Access" control immediately invalidates the link for all future visits.

●       E-06: Inappropriate Mentor Comment. A recipient leaves an abusive or harassing comment. RESOLUTION: User can report or hide the specific comment; repeated abuse from a recipient blocks that link's future comment ability.

INT-US-14: Standard HR Behavioral Interview (STAR Method Focus)

STATUS: In Development PRIORITY: High ACTOR: Job Seeker

Intent: To master standard behavioral HR questions ("Tell me about a time when...") using clear, structured storytelling frameworks.

Happy Path Steps

Scenario Selection: User selects "HR Interview" from the Skill Enhancement module.

Execution: AI asks a standard behavioral question (e.g., "Tell me about a time you overcame a challenge at work.").

Delivery: User answers the question via voice.

Analysis: AI evaluates the response specifically looking for a logical structure: Situation, Task, Action, and Result (STAR).

Feedback: Scorecard highlights which parts of the STAR method the user successfully utilized and which were missing.

Acceptance Criteria

AI must be prompted to evaluate answers against standard HR behavioral frameworks (STAR).

Follow-up questions must probe for missing information (e.g., if the user forgets the 'Result', the AI must ask, "What was the final outcome of that action?").

Exception Handling

E-01: Hypothetical Instead of Past Action. AI asks for a past example, but the user answers hypothetically ("If that happened, I would...").

RESOLUTION: AI interrupts and clarifies: "That's a good approach, but could you give me a specific real-world example from your past experience?"

E-02: Complaining/Negative Tone. User uses the "challenge" question to heavily insult a former boss. RESOLUTION: AI feedback severely penalizes "Professional Tone" and provides actionable advice on how to reframe negative experiences professionally.

E-03: Rambling "Situation" Phase. User spends 3 minutes explaining the background without getting to their actions. RESOLUTION: AI interrupts to keep the interview pacing realistic: "I understand the background now. What specific actions did you take to resolve it?"

Workplace English Coaching

WEC-US-01: Text-Mode Code-Switch Detection

STATUS: Not Started (Gap)   PRIORITY: High   ACTOR: Learner (South Asian Market)

Intent: To detect and correct code-switched local-language words typed during text-mode AI Conversation Practice or written scenarios, extending the existing audio-only detection (CSC-US-01) to typed input.

Happy Path Steps

Input: User types a message mixing English and a local-language word in Roman/transliterated script (e.g., "Please send the file jaldi").

Detection: System's text-based language model scans the typed input token-by-token for non-English words, including transliterated local-language spellings.

Feedback: System highlights the flagged word inline and suggests the pure English equivalent, consistent with the audio-mode feedback style.

Logging: The flagged word is added to the user's Code-Switch Word List (CSC-US-02), tagged "source: text" for tracking.

Acceptance Criteria

Detection must work on both Roman-script transliteration and native-script (e.g., Urdu script) typed words.

Flagging must not break or reject the rest of the message; only the flagged token is isolated.

Must apply the same NER proper-noun exclusion logic used in audio mode (CSC-US-01 E-01).

Exception Handling

E-01: Proper Noun False Positive in Text. User types a local name or location (e.g., "I visited Lahore"). RESOLUTION: Run the same NER check against typed tokens and skip flagging recognized proper nouns.

E-02: Ambiguous Transliteration Spelling Variants. The local word is typed with inconsistent spelling (e.g., "jaldi" vs. "jaldy" vs. "jaldee"). RESOLUTION: Use fuzzy/phonetic matching against the code-switch lexicon rather than exact string matching.

E-03: Auto-Correct Interference. The device's native keyboard auto-correct silently changes the local word into an unrelated English word before submission. RESOLUTION: Score based on the submitted text only; if the resulting word creates a high-confidence contextual mismatch, flag it for the user's review rather than guessing the original intent.

E-04: Mixed Native-Script and Latin-Script in One Message. User types some words in Urdu script and some in English within a single message. RESOLUTION: Process the message as mixed-encoding, scanning native-script tokens directly against the native-script lexicon and skipping English tokens.

E-05: Copy-Pasted Foreign-Language Sentence. User pastes an entire sentence in the local language rather than code-switching a few words. RESOLUTION: Route to the same "complete local-language sentence" handling as audio mode (CSC-US-01 E-02), prompting the user to write the whole sentence in English rather than flagging word-by-word.

E-06: Obfuscated Code-Switch Word. User combines a flagged word with emoji, numbers, or stylized characters (e.g., "j@ldi🙏"). RESOLUTION: Normalize text — strip non-alphanumeric decorations — before lexicon matching, so obfuscated code-switch words are still detected.

E-07: Extremely Short Message. User's entire message is a single ambiguous word that could be either English or a local word (e.g., "na"). RESOLUTION: Require conversational context from the surrounding turns before flagging single-token ambiguous messages, rather than judging them in isolation.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-001

Type a message with one Roman-script local word

Word is isolated, flagged inline, and an English equivalent is suggested.

TC-002

Type a message containing a proper noun

Sentence is accepted without flagging the proper noun.

TC-003

Type the same local word with inconsistent spelling

Fuzzy matching still flags the word correctly.

TC-004

Type a message mixing Urdu script and English words

Native-script tokens are checked against the native lexicon; English tokens are skipped.

TC-005

Paste a full local-language sentence

System prompts the user to rewrite the whole sentence in English.

TC-006

Type a flagged word disguised with emoji/numbers

Normalization still detects and flags the underlying word.



WEC-US-02: Multi-Language / Configurable Mother-Tongue Code-Switch Detection

STATUS: Not Started (Gap)   PRIORITY: High   ACTOR: Learner (South Asian Market) / System

Intent: To allow the Code-Switch Coaching engine to detect mixing from the learner's actual native language(s) — Hindi, Bengali, Punjabi, Tamil, Sindhi, etc. — rather than assuming Urdu for every user, based on a language profile configured at onboarding.

Happy Path Steps

Setup: During onboarding, learner selects their native/regional language(s) from a supported list; multiple selections are allowed.

Configuration: System loads the corresponding code-switch lexicon(s) for the selected language(s) into the user's detection profile.

Detection: During practice, AI cross-references spoken or typed non-English words against the user's configured lexicon(s) rather than a single default language.

Feedback & Logging: Flagged words are corrected and logged exactly as in CSC-US-01/CSC-US-02, tagged with the specific source language for reference.

Acceptance Criteria

Must support, at minimum, the top regional languages relevant to the South Asian market (e.g., Hindi, Urdu, Bengali, Punjabi, Tamil) as selectable onboarding options.

A learner selecting multiple native languages must have all selected lexicons active simultaneously during detection.

Must allow the learner to update their language profile later from account settings without losing prior word list history.

Exception Handling

E-01: Learner Skips Language Selection. User skips the onboarding language-selection step. RESOLUTION: Default to a general "South Asian code-switch" lexicon covering common cross-language loanwords, with a prompt to refine the setting later for higher accuracy.

E-02: Overlapping Vocabulary Across Languages. A word exists in more than one selected language with different English equivalents (e.g., a Hindi/Urdu cognate). RESOLUTION: Use conversational context to disambiguate; if ambiguity remains, present both possible equivalents and let the user confirm which fits.

E-03: Unsupported Language Selected. The learner's native language is not yet in the supported lexicon list (e.g., a regional dialect). RESOLUTION: Disable word-level detection for that language, keep the general non-English-sentence detection (CSC-US-01 E-02) active, and log the request to prioritize adding that language.

E-04: Mid-Program Language Profile Change. Learner updates their native language selection after months of practice. RESOLUTION: Apply the new lexicon only to future sessions; historical word list entries remain tagged with the language that was active when they were logged.

E-05: Code-Mixing Across Two Local Languages With No English. Learner mixes two regional languages together with no English at all (e.g., Punjabi and Urdu in the same sentence). RESOLUTION: Treat the entire utterance as non-English per CSC-US-01 E-02, since the goal is English fluency, not cross-regional-language correction.

E-06: False Detection From Lexicon/English Overlap. A local-language word is spelled identically to a common English word (e.g., a short Romanized token). RESOLUTION: Require a minimum confidence threshold combining phonetic and contextual signals before flagging, to avoid over-flagging legitimate English usage.

E-07: Conflicting Selections at Scale. An enterprise bulk-imports learners without individual language profiles set. RESOLUTION: Default all such learners to the general multi-region lexicon (per E-01) until each completes their own onboarding language selection.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-001

Select Hindi and Punjabi at onboarding

Both lexicons are active; words from either language are detected.

TC-002

Skip language selection entirely

General South Asian lexicon is used by default; refine-later prompt appears.

TC-003

Speak a word ambiguous between two selected languages

AI presents both possible English equivalents for confirmation.

TC-004

Select a currently unsupported dialect

Word-level detection is disabled for that language; sentence-level detection remains active.

TC-005

Change language profile mid-program

New lexicon applies going forward; historical entries retain original language tags.



WEC-US-03: Context-Sensitive Code-Switch Tolerance Across Features

STATUS: Not Started (Gap)   PRIORITY: Medium   ACTOR: Learner / System

Intent: To adjust how strictly code-switching is flagged depending on the practice context — treating a casual roleplay differently from a formal Interview Coach or Workplace Email scenario — and to ensure Code-Switch Coaching applies consistently across every feature involving spoken or written English, not only the core AI Conversation module.

Happy Path Steps

Session Start: Learner begins a session in any English-practice feature (AI Conversation, Interview Coach, Workplace English Coaching, Public Speaking Coach, Scenario-Based Learning).

Context Tagging: System reads the session's formality tag (Casual, Professional, Formal/High-Stakes).

Detection & Threshold: Code-switch detection runs uniformly, but flagging strictness and feedback tone adjust to the formality tag (e.g., a gentle inline note in Casual mode vs. an explicit flag with required correction in Interview Coach).

Consistent Logging: Regardless of source feature, flagged words are logged to the single, unified Code-Switch Word List (CSC-US-02).

Acceptance Criteria

Code-switch detection must be active in every spoken/written practice feature, not only the core AI Conversation module.

Formality-based flagging strictness must reuse the same context tiers already defined for grammar tone adjustment (BAS-US-11), for consistency across the app.

All flags, regardless of source feature, must funnel into the same personal word list rather than fragmenting into feature-specific lists.

Exception Handling

E-01: Feature With No Formality Tag. A newly added practice feature has not yet been tagged with a formality tier. RESOLUTION: Default to "Professional" strictness until explicitly configured, erring toward the stricter standard.

E-02: Casual Roleplay Requiring Local Flavor. A cultural roleplay scenario (e.g., ordering street food) intentionally allows local terms for authenticity. RESOLUTION: Scenario metadata can explicitly whitelist specific local words as "intentional" and exempt them from flagging in that scenario only.

E-03: Mid-Session Formality Shift. A Scenario-Based Learning session shifts from casual small talk to a formal negotiation partway through. RESOLUTION: Re-evaluate the formality tier at each scripted scenario beat rather than locking it for the entire session.

E-04: Conflicting Feature-Level Feedback. Interview Coach's own scoring logic and Code-Switch Coaching both attempt to evaluate the same utterance differently. RESOLUTION: Surface Code-Switch flags as a distinct, clearly labeled feedback category so they never overwrite or conflict with a feature's separate evaluation criteria.

E-05: User Disputes Strictness in High-Stakes Mode. Learner code-switches once during an Interview Coach mock session and feels the flag was too harsh for a single instance. RESOLUTION: Single-instance flags in high-stakes contexts are noted in feedback but do not tank the session's overall score; only repeated instances affect scoring.

E-06: Feature Without Text or Audio Utterances. A feature like a passive video lesson has no learner speech/text to evaluate. RESOLUTION: Skip Code-Switch detection entirely for non-interactive content rather than forcing an inapplicable check.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-001

Code-switch during Casual scenario

Gentle inline note appears; session flow is not interrupted.

TC-002

Code-switch during Interview Coach mock session

Explicit flag with required correction appears.

TC-003

Local word whitelisted in a cultural roleplay

Word is not flagged in that specific scenario.

TC-004

Scenario shifts from casual to formal mid-session

Strictness updates at the formality transition point.

TC-005

Single code-switch instance in a scored mock interview

Flag is logged but does not significantly lower the overall score.



WEC-US-04: Untranslatable / No-Direct-Equivalent Cultural Term Handling

STATUS: Not Started (Gap)   PRIORITY: Medium   ACTOR: Learner / System

Intent: To gracefully handle local-language words that have no single, direct English equivalent (e.g., culturally specific terms), instead of forcing an inaccurate one-word translation.

Happy Path Steps

Detection: AI flags a local-language word as in the standard flow.

Lookup: System checks whether the word exists in a "no direct equivalent" cultural-term dictionary rather than the standard word-swap lexicon.

Adapted Feedback: AI offers the closest descriptive English phrase, or explains the term is an accepted loanword in professional English if that is standard practice (e.g., "chai" in business contexts).

Logging: The term is logged separately under a "Cultural Terms" category rather than the standard target-word category, since it is not necessarily something to eliminate.

Acceptance Criteria

The system must maintain a distinct dictionary of untranslatable/cultural terms, separate from the standard direct-swap lexicon.

Feedback for cultural terms must never present a forced, inaccurate one-word "English equivalent."

Cultural-term entries must be visually distinguished in the Word List UI from words the learner should actively eliminate.

Exception Handling

E-01: Ambiguous Classification. A word could reasonably be treated as either a standard code-switch or a cultural term depending on context (e.g., "jugaad"). RESOLUTION: Default to cultural-term classification when confidence in a direct-swap equivalent is low, erring toward not over-correcting.

E-02: Regionally Accepted Loanword in Business English. The term is already standard in South Asian professional English (e.g., certain food, clothing, or family terms). RESOLUTION: AI explicitly reassures the learner the term is acceptable as-is and does not require replacement.

E-03: Learner Requests Reclassification. Learner disagrees with a term being marked "cultural" and wants it flagged for elimination anyway (e.g., preparing for a non-regional international audience). RESOLUTION: Allow the learner to manually move a term from "Cultural Terms" into the active target-word list.

E-04: New/Unrecognized Cultural Term. AI encounters a local word not yet present in either lexicon. RESOLUTION: Flag it as "Unclassified," offer the closest descriptive phrase as a best-effort suggestion, and queue the term for lexicon review rather than guessing definitively.

E-05: Term Has Multiple Regional Meanings. The same word means different things across the learner's multiple selected native languages (per GAP-02). RESOLUTION: Use active conversation context to select the most likely regional meaning, and note the alternate meaning if confidence is low.

E-06: Cultural Term Used Excessively as a Crutch. Learner repeatedly relies on the loanword exemption to avoid attempting English phrasing at all. RESOLUTION: If a cultural term is used far more frequently than typical for that concept, gently suggest an English descriptive alternative anyway, without contradicting the earlier "acceptable as-is" guidance for occasional use.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-001

Use a term with no direct English equivalent

AI offers a descriptive phrase instead of an inaccurate single-word swap.

TC-002

Use a regionally accepted business loanword

AI confirms the term is acceptable and does not suggest replacement.

TC-003

Learner manually reclassifies a cultural term as a target word

Term moves into the active target-word list.

TC-004

Use an unrecognized local term

Term is flagged "Unclassified" with a best-effort descriptive suggestion.

TC-005

Use a term with 2 regional meanings from different selected languages

AI selects the contextually likely meaning and flags low-confidence cases.



WEC-US-05: Immediate In-Session Retry & Reinforcement Drill

STATUS: Not Started (Gap)   PRIORITY: Medium   ACTOR: Learner

Intent: To let the learner immediately practice the corrected English word right after a code-switch is flagged, reinforcing the correction in the moment rather than only queuing it for a later dashboard drill.

Happy Path Steps

Flag: AI detects and flags a code-switched word mid-conversation, as in CSC-US-01.

Prompt: AI immediately asks the learner to restate the sentence, or just the phrase, using the suggested English word.

Retry: Learner repeats the corrected sentence.

Reinforcement Confirmation: AI confirms correct usage and the conversation resumes naturally from where it left off.

Acceptance Criteria

The retry prompt must not fully interrupt conversational flow in Casual/low-stakes sessions; it should be optional and dismissible in Casual mode (per GAP-03 tiers) and default-on in Professional/Formal modes.

A successful immediate retry must be recorded distinctly (e.g., "corrected on first retry") in the Word List history, separate from words never retried.

Retry prompting must not repeat more than once per flagged instance, to avoid derailing the conversation.

Exception Handling

E-01: Learner Declines the Retry. Learner dismisses or ignores the retry prompt and continues the conversation. RESOLUTION: Log the word normally per CSC-US-02 without the "corrected on retry" tag, and do not force the retry.

E-02: Learner Retries Incorrectly. Learner attempts the retry but uses the wrong word or makes a different mistake. RESOLUTION: AI gives one gentle re-prompt restating the correct word, then moves on regardless of the outcome, to avoid a frustrating loop.

E-03: Retry Requested During Casual Mode. Session is tagged Casual, where retries are optional. RESOLUTION: Show the retry prompt as a subtle, dismissible inline suggestion rather than a blocking interruption.

E-04: Repeated Flags in Rapid Succession. Learner code-switches multiple different words within the same short exchange. RESOLUTION: Batch the corrections into a single consolidated retry prompt covering all flagged words, rather than issuing sequential interruptions for each one.

E-05: Retry Prompt During Timed Assessment Context. The flagged utterance occurs during a scored, time-boxed exercise (e.g., Interview Coach mock timing). RESOLUTION: Suppress the interactive retry prompt during the timed portion; log the flag for post-session review instead so timing is not disrupted.

E-06: Learner Repeatedly Declines Across Many Sessions. Learner consistently ignores retry prompts session after session. RESOLUTION: Reduce prompt frequency automatically for that learner and surface a one-time settings suggestion pointing to the sensitivity controls (GAP-07) instead of continuing to interrupt.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-001

Code-switch flagged in Professional mode

Retry prompt appears by default and blocks brief continuation until addressed.

TC-002

Learner successfully retries with correct word

Word list logs the entry as "corrected on first retry."

TC-003

Learner dismisses the retry prompt

Word is logged normally without the retry tag; conversation continues.

TC-004

3 words flagged within one exchange

A single consolidated retry prompt covers all 3 words.

TC-005

Flag occurs during timed Interview Coach segment

Retry prompt is suppressed; flag is queued for post-session review.



WEC-US-06: Code-Switch Word Mastery & List Archiving

STATUS: Not Started (Gap)   PRIORITY: Low   ACTOR: Learner / System

Intent: To recognize when a learner has consistently stopped code-switching a specific word over time and automatically move it out of the active target list, so the list reflects current problem areas rather than growing indefinitely.

Happy Path Steps

Tracking: System tracks each active target word's usage across subsequent sessions after it was first flagged.

Mastery Check: After the learner correctly uses the English equivalent instead of code-switching across a defined number of consecutive relevant opportunities, the system marks the word "Mastered."

Archiving: The mastered word moves from the active "My Target Words" list into an "Achievements/Mastered Words" section.

Notification: Learner receives a small positive notification celebrating the mastered word.

Acceptance Criteria

A word must only be eligible for mastery evaluation after appearing in at least one flagged instance and subsequently having genuine opportunities to be code-switched again.

Mastered words must remain visible in an archived/history view, not deleted outright.

Mastery status must be reversible if the learner code-switches the same word again after being marked mastered.

Exception Handling

E-01: Relapse After Mastery. A learner marked as having "mastered" a word code-switches it again weeks later. RESOLUTION: Automatically move the word back to the active target list and reset its mastery progress, without shaming messaging.

E-02: Insufficient Opportunities to Prove Mastery. A flagged word is rare in typical conversation, so the learner never gets enough natural chances to demonstrate they have stopped using it. RESOLUTION: After a defined inactivity period with no relapse, allow a lower-confidence "Likely Mastered" status rather than requiring an exact opportunity count.

E-03: User Manually Marks a Word Mastered. Learner believes they have corrected a word and wants to archive it early. RESOLUTION: Allow a manual "Mark as practiced" action, labeled distinctly from system-verified mastery until the system independently confirms it over subsequent sessions.

E-04: Bulk Mastery Edge Case. Multiple words reach mastery criteria in the same session, all at once. RESOLUTION: Batch the celebratory notification into a single summary rather than firing multiple separate pop-ups.

E-05: Mastery Achieved Immediately After Sensitivity Was Off. Coaching was turned Off (per GAP-07) for a period, then re-enabled, and the word appears not to have relapsed simply because it was not being tracked. RESOLUTION: Exclude any period where coaching was Off from the opportunity count used to evaluate mastery.

E-06: Word List Migrated After Language Profile Change. A word's source language changes after a profile update (per GAP-02 E-04). RESOLUTION: Preserve mastery progress already made on the word; do not reset progress purely due to a language-tag change.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-001

Learner correctly uses a target word across required opportunities

Word is marked "Mastered" and moved to the archive with a notification.

TC-002

Learner relapses on a mastered word

Word returns to the active target list and mastery progress resets.

TC-003

Rarely-used flagged word with a long inactivity period

Word receives a "Likely Mastered" status after the defined inactivity window.

TC-004

Learner manually marks a word as practiced

Word is labeled as manually marked, distinct from system-verified mastery.

TC-005

5 words reach mastery in one session

A single consolidated celebration notification is shown.



WEC-US-07: Code-Switch Coaching Sensitivity Settings (Opt-Out / Adjust)

STATUS: Not Started (Gap)   PRIORITY: Low   ACTOR: Learner

Intent: To give the learner control over how actively Code-Switch Coaching intervenes, since some learners may find the correction frequency intrusive at their current comfort level, or may be preparing specifically for international audiences with no local-language mixing habits.

Happy Path Steps

Access: Learner navigates to Settings > Coaching Preferences > Code-Switch Coaching.

Options: Learner selects a sensitivity level: Off, Light (flag only clear/frequent offenders), Standard (default behavior), or Strict (flag even borderline slang per CSC-US-01 E-03).

Confirmation: System applies the selected sensitivity to all future sessions immediately.

Persistent Setting: Selection persists across sessions until changed again.

Acceptance Criteria

Turning coaching "Off" must stop new detection and logging but must not delete the learner's existing Word List history.

The setting must apply uniformly across all features per the context tiers in GAP-03, not just the core AI Conversation module.

Changing sensitivity mid-program must not retroactively alter previously logged words or scores.

Exception Handling

E-01: Learner Turns Coaching Off Then Re-Enables Later. RESOLUTION: Resume detection going forward using the existing Word List and Language Profile (GAP-02) without requiring re-onboarding.

E-02: Enterprise-Mandated Sensitivity. Learner belongs to an organization that requires Code-Switch Coaching to remain on at or above "Standard" sensitivity for compliance/training purposes. RESOLUTION: Lock the sensitivity control at the org-mandated minimum and disable the "Off" option for that learner.

E-03: Sensitivity Conflicts With High-Stakes Context. Learner has set sensitivity to "Off" but enters a Formal/High-Stakes session (e.g., Interview Coach). RESOLUTION: Temporarily restore at least "Light" sensitivity for that session only, informing the learner why, since high-stakes practice benefits from the feedback even for otherwise opted-out learners.

E-04: Setting Not Yet Configured (New User). Learner has never visited the sensitivity setting. RESOLUTION: Default to "Standard" sensitivity, matching the currently documented CSC-US-01 behavior.

E-05: Setting Changed Mid-Session. Learner adjusts sensitivity while a practice session is already in progress. RESOLUTION: Apply the new sensitivity starting with the next utterance in that same session, rather than requiring a session restart.

E-06: Conflicting Device Settings. Learner has different sensitivity settings saved on two devices due to an offline sync delay. RESOLUTION: Treat the most recently confirmed change (by timestamp) as authoritative once connectivity is restored, and surface a brief notice if a conflict was resolved.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-001

Set sensitivity to Off

Detection and logging stop; existing Word List remains intact.

TC-002

Enterprise learner attempts to set sensitivity to Off

Option is disabled/locked at the org-mandated minimum.

TC-003

Sensitivity is Off, learner enters Interview Coach

"Light" sensitivity is temporarily restored for that session with an explanation.

TC-004

New user opens the setting for the first time

Sensitivity defaults to "Standard."

TC-005

Change sensitivity mid-session

New sensitivity applies starting with the next utterance in that session.



WEC-US-08: Workplace English Practice

STATUS: In Development PRIORITY: Medium ACTOR: Working Professional

Intent: To practice scenario-based professional communication (emails, meetings, presentations) to improve workplace effectiveness.

Happy Path Steps

Select Task: User selects a workplace scenario (e.g., Email Writing, Client Communication).

Execution: User drafts an email text or records an audio message for a meeting.

Analysis: AI evaluates the submission against workplace norms.

Feedback: AI delivers feedback focused on professional tone, clarity, and effectiveness, not just basic grammar.

Acceptance Criteria

Feedback must explicitly grade "Professional Tone" as a core metric.

The AI must flag casual language or slang that is inappropriate for corporate settings.

Exception Handling

E-01: Tone Mismatch Detected. User uses highly informal text speak (e.g., "thx bro") in a client email scenario. RESOLUTION: AI flags the specific phrase, explains why it's unprofessional, and suggests a corporate alternative.

E-02: Code-Switching Detected. User mixes Urdu/local language words with English (e.g., "Please jaldi reply"). RESOLUTION: AI flags the code-switched word and provides the exact English equivalent to use in professional settings.

E-03: Empty Subject Line (Email Scenario). User submits an email without a subject. RESOLUTION: System prompts, "A professional email needs a clear subject line. Please add one."

E-04: Plagiarized/Template Input. User copies and pastes a standard corporate boilerplate. RESOLUTION: AI detects unnatural perfection/standard templates and asks the user to rewrite it in their own original words.

Analysis: AI evaluates the draft specifically looking at workplace tone and professionalism, not just grammar.

Feedback: AI presents a polished version of the email and highlights areas where clarity or tone can be improved.

Acceptance Criteria

The AI must flag language that is grammatically correct but culturally inappropriate for a professional setting.

E-04: Boilerplate Copy-Paste. User pastes a generic corporate template instead of writing originally. RESOLUTION: AI detects the lack of personalization and asks the user to adapt it specifically to the prompt.

WEC-US-11: Workplace English - Meeting Communication Coach

Happy Path Steps

Feedback: AI evaluates the user on timing, professional phrasing, and clarity of the proposal.

Acceptance Criteria

The AI must simulate multiple "voices" or a continuous discussion that the user must actively step into.

Feedback must specifically grade "Polite Interruption" and "Idea Clarity".

Exception Handling

E-02: Abrupt Interruption. User yells or cuts off the AI mid-sentence abruptly. RESOLUTION: Feedback highlights the interruption as too aggressive and provides standard corporate transition phrases (e.g., "If I could just jump in here...").

WEC-US-12: Workplace English - Presentation Preparation Coach

STATUS: In Development PRIORITY: High ACTOR: Working Professional

Intent: To practice the verbal delivery, slide transitions, and professional framing needed for corporate presentations before delivering them to real colleagues.

Happy Path Steps

Module Selection: User selects "Presentation Preparation" from the Workplace English menu.

Context Setup: User inputs the topic of their presentation (e.g., "Q3 Marketing Results").

Execution: User speaks their presentation aloud, treating the AI as the audience.

Analysis: AI evaluates the clarity of the core message, transition phrases between "slides," and overall professional tone.

Feedback: AI provides actionable tips on how to sound more authoritative and clear.

Acceptance Criteria

The AI must be trained to recognize and grade "transition phrasing" (e.g., "Moving on to the next slide," "As you can see on this graph").

Feedback must prioritize "Professional Tone" over casual conversational fluency.

Exception Handling

E-01: Skipping the Agenda/Intro. User jumps straight into raw data without setting the context. RESOLUTION: Feedback flags "Missing Introduction/Agenda" and suggests opening phrases like "Today I'd like to cover..."

E-02: Casual Language in Corporate Setting. User uses terms like "So yeah, that's pretty much it" to conclude. RESOLUTION: AI flags the informal conclusion and suggests a strong corporate closing: "To summarize our main takeaways..."

E-03: Long Pauses (Simulating Slide Clicks). User pauses for 5 seconds between thoughts. RESOLUTION: AI recognizes this as a potential slide transition pause and does not penalize fluency, provided appropriate transition words bracket the pause.

E-04: Audio Mute During Prep. User accidentally mutes their device mid- presentation. RESOLUTION: App detects 0db input for 15 seconds while the app is active and shows a toast: "Microphone seems quiet. Still practicing?"

Extended slide-click pause

System accepts a 5-second silence without a fluency penalty.

WEC-US-14: Workplace English - Meeting Preparation Feedback UI

Acceptance Criteria

The UI must visually decouple tone feedback from basic grammar feedback.

Suggested alternatives must align with standard corporate meeting terminology.

Exception Handling

E-03: Micro-Audio Snippet Submission. User submits a 2-second audio clip saying "Okay." RESOLUTION: AI cannot evaluate tone on a single word. Scorecard flags "Insufficient Data for Tone Analysis" and asks for full sentences next time.
