Pronunciation Coaching

PRN-US-01: Microphone Access & Device Readiness Check

STATUS: Proposed (Gap)   PRIORITY: High   ACTOR: Learner

Intent: To be guided through microphone permission and hardware readiness before a Pronunciation Coaching session begins, so that a session never starts on audio that cannot be captured.

Happy Path Steps

1. Entry: User taps into the Pronunciation Coach for the first time on a device.

2. Permission Prompt: System requests microphone access via the OS-level permission dialog.

3. Readiness Check: System runs a 2-second silent calibration to confirm signal is being received and sets an input gain baseline.

4. Confirmation: UI shows a green mic icon and "Ready to record" before the first target sentence appears.

5. Proceed: User begins the standard read-aloud flow once readiness is confirmed.

Acceptance Criteria

• The system must never present a target sentence for recording until microphone access is confirmed as granted and functional.

• A visible mic-status indicator (ready / blocked / no input) must be shown at all times during the session.

• The calibration check must complete in under 3 seconds on a stable connection.

Exception Handling

• E-01: Permission Denied. User denies microphone access at the OS prompt. RESOLUTION: System blocks entry to the exercise and displays step-by-step instructions to enable the mic from device settings, with a "Try Again" button that re-triggers the permission check without restarting the app.

• E-02: Permission Revoked Mid-Session. User (or the OS) revokes mic access while a session is already open, e.g. via a privacy toggle. RESOLUTION: System immediately pauses the current sentence, preserves the in-progress score, and shows a non-destructive "Microphone access lost - reconnect to continue" banner.

• E-03: No Microphone Hardware Detected. Device has no functioning microphone (e.g. desktop browser without an input device, or a hardware fault). RESOLUTION: System detects the absence of an audio input track and offers to switch to a connected Bluetooth/external mic if one exists, or gracefully routes the user to a non-voice practice mode.

• E-04: Multiple Input Devices Available. User has both a phone mic and a paired Bluetooth headset active simultaneously. RESOLUTION: System defaults to the highest-priority/most recently connected input and exposes a device picker so the user can confirm or switch before recording.

• E-05: Calibration Timeout. The silent calibration step receives no signal at all (e.g. muted hardware switch). RESOLUTION: After 5 seconds with zero signal, system surfaces "We're not picking up any sound - check your mute switch or mic settings" rather than failing silently.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-001

First-time mic permission grant

Calibration runs automatically; session unlocks and first sentence loads.

TC-002

Mic permission denied

Entry blocked; settings walkthrough shown with a retry action.

TC-003

Permission revoked mid-sentence

Session pauses without losing prior sentence scores; reconnect banner appears.

TC-004

No mic hardware present

System offers external device pairing or routes to non-voice mode.

TC-005

Muted hardware switch active

Timeout message about missing audio input is shown within 5 seconds.

PRN-US-02: Pre-Attempt Reference Audio Playback (Listen First)

STATUS: Proposed (Gap)   PRIORITY: Medium   ACTOR: Learner

Intent: To hear a native-quality model reading of the full target sentence before attempting it, so pronunciation errors can be pre-empted rather than only corrected after the fact.

Happy Path Steps

6. Prompt: AI presents a target English sentence on screen alongside a "Listen" button.

7. Playback: User taps "Listen" and hears the full reference sentence at natural speed.

8. Optional Slow Playback: User taps a speed toggle to hear the same sentence at 0.6x speed, syllable emphasis intact.

9. Attempt: User taps "Record" and reads the sentence aloud.

10. Evaluation: AI scores the attempt using the standard word-level highlighting flow.

Acceptance Criteria

• Reference audio must be available on-demand, unlimited times, before the first recording attempt.

• A slow-speed (0.6x) playback option must be available without pitch distortion (time-stretch, not simple slowdown).

• Listening to the reference audio must never count as, or affect the score of, a recording attempt.

Exception Handling

• E-01: Reference Audio File Missing. The TTS/reference clip for a specific sentence fails to generate or load. RESOLUTION: System falls back to a generic TTS engine for that sentence and logs the missing asset for content-team follow-up, rather than disabling the Listen button silently.

• E-02: Repeated Listen Without Attempting. User replays the reference audio more than 5 times without recording. RESOLUTION: System gently nudges with "Ready to give it a try?" without blocking further listens.

• E-03: Playback Interrupted by Incoming Notification/Call. Audio playback is cut off by a system-level interruption. RESOLUTION: Playback auto-resumes from the beginning (not mid-word) once the interruption ends.

• E-04: Slow-Speed Toggle Left On Across Sentences. User enables 0.6x playback and moves to the next sentence. RESOLUTION: The speed preference persists for the session but never silently changes the speed of the user's own recording or scoring criteria.

• E-05: Low Bandwidth / Audio Fails to Buffer. Reference audio stream stalls on a poor connection. RESOLUTION: System caches the next 2-3 sentences' reference audio proactively during idle time and shows a lightweight loading state rather than a hard error.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-001

Tap Listen before first attempt

Reference audio plays at natural speed with no impact on score.

TC-002

Tap slow-speed toggle

Audio plays at 0.6x speed with pitch preserved (no chipmunk/robotic distortion).

TC-003

Reference audio missing for a sentence

Fallback TTS voice plays; Listen button remains functional.

TC-004

Call interrupts playback

Playback restarts cleanly from the beginning after the call ends.

TC-005

Poor network during playback

Buffering indicator shown; cached upcoming sentence audio plays without delay.

PRN-US-03: Adaptive Sentence Selection Based on Weak Phonemes

STATUS: Proposed (Gap)   PRIORITY: High   ACTOR: Learner

Intent: To automatically receive the next practice sentence chosen based on previously mispronounced sounds, so practice targets real weaknesses instead of a fixed, generic sentence list.

Happy Path Steps

11. Session Start: User completes a sentence in the Pronunciation Coach; the system logs which phonemes/words were red or orange.

12. Analysis: AI aggregates the error pattern (e.g. recurring difficulty with the "th" sound) across the session.

13. Selection: System selects the next sentence from the content bank specifically containing that phoneme in a new context.

14. Presentation: The next sentence is shown with a subtle tag, e.g. "Practicing: TH sound".

15. Continuation: The cycle repeats, gradually rotating through the user's top 3 weak sounds rather than repeating just one.

Acceptance Criteria

• After any session with 2 or more flagged word errors sharing a phoneme, the next sentence offered must target that phoneme.

• The system must rotate across a user's top weak phonemes rather than fixating on a single one indefinitely.

• The targeting tag/rationale must be visible to the user so the adaptivity is transparent, not a black box.

Exception Handling

• E-01: Insufficient Error History. A brand-new user has no prior session data to base selection on. RESOLUTION: System falls back to a difficulty-ordered default sentence set until at least one full session of data exists.

• E-02: No Matching Content Available. AI identifies a weak phoneme but the content bank has no more unused sentences containing it. RESOLUTION: System reuses a previously seen sentence rather than skipping the targeted practice, and flags the content gap for the content team.

• E-03: Over-Fixation Risk. The same single phoneme would be selected for more than 3 consecutive sentences. RESOLUTION: System caps consecutive same-phoneme targeting at 3 sentences, then rotates to the next weak phoneme or a general sentence to avoid learner fatigue/frustration.

• E-04: Conflicting Signals from Retry Loop. A word was mispronounced initially but corrected during the retry loop (PRN-US-11) within the same sentence. RESOLUTION: Only the final, post-retry articulation is counted toward the weak-phoneme profile, not the initial failed attempt.

• E-05: User Manually Overrides Adaptive Suggestion. User taps "Skip to a different topic" instead of the suggested targeted sentence. RESOLUTION: System honors the override immediately and de-prioritizes (not deletes) that phoneme target for the remainder of the session.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-001

Two consecutive errors on the same phoneme

Next sentence contains that phoneme with a visible practice tag.

TC-002

New user, zero history

Default difficulty-ordered sentence is served; no crash or blank state.

TC-003

Content bank exhausted for a phoneme

A previously used sentence is reused rather than an empty state.

TC-004

Same phoneme targeted 4 times in a row

System rotates to a different weak phoneme on the 4th sentence.

TC-005

User taps 'Skip to different topic'

Adaptive suggestion is dropped for the session without error.

PRN-US-04: Silent / No-Speech Full-Duration Recording

STATUS: Proposed (Gap)   PRIORITY: Medium   ACTOR: Learner

Intent: To be clearly informed when a full-length recording was captured but contains no detectable speech, so the user is not left confused by a stalled or blank evaluation.

Happy Path Steps

16. Execution: User taps Record and the full expected duration for the sentence elapses.

17. Capture: System captures a complete audio clip matching the expected sentence length.

18. Analysis: AI attempts to transcribe the clip and detects no speech energy above the silence threshold for the entire duration.

19. Feedback: System distinguishes this from a mispronunciation and informs the user no speech was detected.

20. Retry: User is prompted to try again with a visual audio-level meter shown live this time.

Acceptance Criteria

• A full-duration silent recording must never be scored as mispronounced words; it must be classified as "No Speech Detected".

• The system must not deduct from or affect any existing score when this occurs.

• A live input-level meter must be offered on retry to help the user confirm they are being heard.

Exception Handling

• E-01: Whispered/Very Low Volume Speech. User speaks but at a volume too low for reliable phoneme analysis. RESOLUTION: System distinguishes 'too quiet to score' from 'no speech at all' and prompts "Try speaking a little louder" rather than a generic error.

• E-02: Partial Silence (Speech Starts Late). User pauses several seconds before starting to speak, then reads normally. RESOLUTION: System trims leading/trailing silence before scoring rather than penalizing for the initial delay.

• E-03: Repeated Silent Attempts. User submits 3 consecutive silent recordings. RESOLUTION: System proactively surfaces the microphone troubleshooting flow (see GAP-PC-01) instead of repeating the same generic prompt.

• E-04: Silence Due to Muted Mic Mid-Recording. Speech is captured for part of the clip, then the mic is muted (e.g. hardware mute button) for the rest. RESOLUTION: System scores only the words captured before the mute point and marks the remainder as 'Unscorable', distinct from a mispronunciation.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-001

Full-duration recording with zero speech

"No Speech Detected" message shown; no score impact; retry offered.

TC-002

Whispered attempt below scoring threshold

System asks user to speak louder rather than flagging errors.

TC-003

Speech starts 3 seconds late

Leading silence trimmed automatically; sentence scored normally.

TC-004

Three silent attempts in a row

Microphone troubleshooting flow is triggered automatically.

TC-005

Mic muted mid-recording

Words before mute are scored; remainder marked Unscorable, not wrong.

PRN-US-05: Off-Script / Wrong-Language Speech Detection

STATUS: Proposed (Gap)   PRIORITY: Medium   ACTOR: Learner

Intent: To receive a clear, non-punitive correction when the recorded speech does not match the target English sentence at all, so the user understands the mismatch instead of seeing a wall of red errors.

Happy Path Steps

21. Execution: User reads a target sentence, but instead speaks an unrelated sentence, a translation, or thinks aloud in another language.

22. Transcription: AI transcribes the audio and runs a similarity check against the target sentence.

23. Detection: System detects that overall word/phoneme overlap falls far below the threshold for a genuine attempt.

24. Feedback: System flags the attempt as "Off-Script" rather than scoring every word as mispronounced.

25. Retry: User is shown the original target sentence again with a reminder to read it aloud as written.

Acceptance Criteria

• An off-script or wrong-language recording must never be rendered as a sentence full of red mispronunciation highlights.

• The similarity threshold that triggers "Off-Script" classification must be configurable/tunable, not hard-coded per sentence.

• The user's overall pronunciation score must be unaffected by an off-script attempt.

Exception Handling

• E-01: Heavy Accent Misclassified as Off-Script. A very heavy but genuine attempt at the correct sentence triggers a false 'Off-Script' flag. RESOLUTION: System requires both low word-overlap AND low phoneme-overlap before classifying as off-script, so accented-but-correct attempts are never mistaken for wrong-language speech.

• E-02: Code-Switching Mid-Sentence. User reads most of the sentence in English but slips into their native language for one word. RESOLUTION: System scores the recognizably English portion normally and marks only the non-English segment as 'Unrecognized', not off-script for the whole sentence.

• E-03: User Reads a Different Valid English Sentence. User accidentally reads the sentence from a previous screen. RESOLUTION: System still classifies as Off-Script (since it doesn't match the current target) but surfaces the specific mismatch: "That didn't match today's sentence - here it is again."

• E-04: Repeated Off-Script Attempts. User submits off-script audio 3 times in a row, suggesting confusion about the task. RESOLUTION: System offers to replay the reference audio (GAP-PC-02) and simplifies the instruction text before the next attempt.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-001

User speaks an entirely unrelated sentence

Attempt flagged Off-Script; no red word highlights; score unaffected.

TC-002

Heavy accent, correct sentence content

Attempt scored normally, not misclassified as off-script.

TC-003

One word spoken in native language mid-sentence

Rest of sentence scored normally; only that word marked Unrecognized.

TC-004

User reads the previous sentence by mistake

System shows the correct target sentence again with a clear reminder.

TC-005

Three off-script attempts in a row

Reference audio replay and simplified instructions are surfaced.

PRN-US-06: Pronunciation Engine Outage & Timeout Fallback

STATUS: Proposed (Gap)   PRIORITY: High   ACTOR: Learner

Intent: To have a predictable, honest experience when the backend speech-analysis service is slow, down, or errors out, rather than an app that appears frozen or silently loses a recording.

Happy Path Steps

26. Execution: User completes a recording and taps submit for evaluation.

27. Processing: App uploads the audio and awaits a scoring response from the pronunciation-analysis service.

28. Timeout Check: If no response is received within the expected window, system escalates to a retry/backoff state.

29. Fallback Messaging: If the service remains unavailable, system informs the user clearly rather than spinning indefinitely.

30. Recovery: Once the service responds (or comes back online), the queued attempt is scored and the result is delivered, or the user is offered to re-record.

Acceptance Criteria

• The UI must never show an indefinite loading spinner beyond a defined timeout (e.g. 10 seconds) without user-facing status.

• A user's recorded audio must never be silently discarded on a backend failure without the user being told.

• The system must distinguish between a slow response (retry automatically) and a hard failure (inform and offer manual retry).

Exception Handling

• E-01: Transient Timeout. The scoring service takes longer than expected but is not fully down. RESOLUTION: System automatically retries the request up to 2 times with backoff before surfacing any message to the user.

• E-02: Full Service Outage. The pronunciation-analysis service is completely unreachable. RESOLUTION: System preserves the recorded audio locally, shows "We're having trouble scoring this right now - we'll save your attempt and retry shortly," and queues it for background retry.

• E-03: Partial Response (Corrupted/Incomplete Score). The service returns a malformed or partial scoring payload. RESOLUTION: System discards the corrupted result, does not display a false score, and prompts the user to re-record rather than showing broken UI.

• E-04: Outage During an Active Retry-Loop Streak. Service goes down mid-way through a multi-attempt retry loop (PRN-US-11) where earlier attempts were already scored. RESOLUTION: Previously scored words/results remain visible and intact; only the pending attempt is affected.

• E-05: User Navigates Away During Processing. User exits the Pronunciation Coach while a submission is still processing. RESOLUTION: System completes scoring in the background and surfaces the result via a notification/badge when the user returns, rather than silently dropping it.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-001

Scoring response delayed by 4 seconds

Automatic retry occurs silently; user sees only a brief loading state.

TC-002

Backend fully unreachable

Audio preserved locally; clear message shown; background retry queued.

TC-003

Malformed scoring payload returned

No score displayed; user prompted to re-record.

TC-004

Outage occurs mid retry-loop

Earlier correctly-scored words remain visible and unaffected.

TC-005

User exits app while processing

Result delivered via notification when user returns to the app.

PRN-US-07: Cross-Session Trouble Words Bank & Spaced Repetition

STATUS: Proposed (Gap)   PRIORITY: Medium   ACTOR: Learner

Intent: To have specific words that were repeatedly mispronounced across different sessions automatically collected into a personal review list, so problem words are revisited over time instead of being forgotten after one session ends.

Happy Path Steps

31. Logging: Each time a word is scored red (mispronounced) or gray (omitted), the system logs it against the user's profile.

32. Aggregation: After a session ends, AI checks whether any word has been mislogged in 2 or more separate sessions.

33. Bank Update: Qualifying words are added to the user's persistent "Trouble Words" list, visible from the Pronunciation Coach home screen.

34. Spaced Review: At a suitable interval, the system inserts a short sentence containing a trouble-bank word into a future session.

35. Graduation: When a trouble word is pronounced correctly 3 times across separate sessions, it is marked "Mastered" and removed from active rotation.

Acceptance Criteria

• A word must appear in the Trouble Words bank only after failing in at least 2 distinct sessions, not a single session's retries.

• The Trouble Words list must be viewable on demand by the user, independent of any single session.

• A word must be automatically retired from the active bank once the mastery criterion (3 correct, separate-session reads) is met.

Exception Handling

• E-01: Word Mastered Then Regresses. A previously 'Mastered' word is mispronounced again in a later session. RESOLUTION: System re-adds it to the active Trouble Words bank rather than treating it as permanently graduated, and resets its mastery counter.

• E-02: Trouble Bank Grows Unbounded. User accumulates more than 50 trouble words over months of use. RESOLUTION: System caps active spaced-repetition rotation to the top 15 most-recent/most-frequent words, while the full historical list remains viewable in an archive view.

• E-03: Word Flagged Due to Non-Pronunciation Cause. A word was marked red due to background noise or a service glitch (per GAP-PC-06/PRN-US-10 E-04), not a genuine articulation error. RESOLUTION: Only words scored red/gray under normal, unflagged conditions count toward the Trouble Words bank; noise-affected or unscorable attempts are excluded.

• E-04: Duplicate Word Forms. The same root word appears in different inflections (e.g. "specific" vs "specifically"). RESOLUTION: System tracks trouble entries at the phoneme-pattern level so related word forms sharing the same problem sound are grouped, not duplicated as unrelated entries.

• E-05: User Requests Manual Removal. User wants to remove a word from the bank they feel is already resolved. RESOLUTION: System allows manual dismissal, but logs the override so if the word fails again later it can re-enter the bank normally.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-001

Word mispronounced in 2 separate sessions

Word appears in the Trouble Words bank.

TC-002

Word mispronounced twice within the same session's retries only

Word does NOT yet appear in the persistent bank.

TC-003

Mastered word mispronounced again later

Word re-enters active bank; mastery counter resets.

TC-004

Bank exceeds 50 historical entries

Active rotation limited to top 15; full list still viewable in archive.

TC-005

User manually dismisses a trouble word

Word is removed from rotation but can re-enter if it fails again.

PRN-US-08: Accessibility Safeguard for Genuine Speech Disorders

STATUS: Proposed (Gap)   PRIORITY: High   ACTOR: Learner (with a diagnosed or self-identified speech disorder)

Intent: To practice pronunciation without being repeatedly and inaccurately flagged for a disability-related speech pattern (e.g. a genuine stutter) as if it were a correctable pronunciation error, preserving motivation and dignity.

Happy Path Steps

36. Opt-In: During setup, user optionally indicates a speech-related condition (e.g. stutter, apraxia) in accessibility settings.

37. Adjusted Scoring: Pronunciation Coach applies an accessibility-aware scoring profile that separates fluency/disfluency from articulation accuracy.

38. Execution: User reads the target sentence at their own pace, including any natural repetitions or blocks.

39. Feedback: System scores the articulation of words rather than penalizing pace or repetition patterns tied to the disclosed condition.

40. Encouraging Framing: Feedback language avoids implying that a disclosed disorder trait is an 'error' to be fixed.

Acceptance Criteria

• When an accessibility profile is active, disfluency patterns consistent with the disclosed condition must not lower the pronunciation or fluency score.

• The system must still accurately flag genuine phoneme-level articulation errors unrelated to the disclosed condition.

• Opting in or out of the accessibility profile must be available at any time from settings, not just at onboarding.

Exception Handling

• E-01: Undisclosed Disorder Pattern Detected. System observes a highly consistent disfluency pattern across many sessions from a user who has not opted into an accessibility profile. RESOLUTION: System never diagnoses or labels the user; it may gently surface the optional accessibility setting once, without repeating the suggestion if declined.

• E-02: Standard 'Frustration Loop' Logic Conflicts With Accessibility Mode. The 5-fail frustration-loop trigger from PRN-US-11 (E-01) risks repeatedly interrupting a user whose natural speech includes more than 5 repetitions. RESOLUTION: When the accessibility profile is active, the frustration-loop threshold and syllable-breakdown intervention are disabled for disfluency-pattern triggers, while remaining active for genuine phoneme-level mispronunciation.

• E-03: Profile Misapplied to Casual Disfluency. A user without a disclosed condition stutters occasionally due to nerves, not a disorder. RESOLUTION: Standard casual-stutter handling (PRN-US-10 E-03 / PRN-US-12 E-02) continues to apply unchanged; the accessibility profile only alters behavior for users who have explicitly opted in.

• E-04: Score Comparability Concerns. User wants to know if their score is 'lower' because of the adjusted profile. RESOLUTION: System clearly labels sessions run under the accessibility profile so progress trends are compared like-for-like, never silently mixed with standard-profile scores.

• E-05: User Wants to Temporarily Disable for a Specific Drill. User wants standard (unadjusted) scoring for one exercise. RESOLUTION: A per-session toggle allows temporarily using the standard profile without changing the persistent accessibility setting.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-001

User opts into accessibility profile, reads with natural repetitions

Articulation scored fairly; repetition pattern does not lower fluency score.

TC-002

Genuine mispronunciation occurs under accessibility profile

Word is still correctly flagged as an articulation error.

TC-003

5+ repetitions trigger under accessibility profile

Standard frustration-loop interruption is suppressed.

TC-004

User without opt-in stutters occasionally

Standard casual-disfluency handling applies unchanged.

TC-005

User toggles standard scoring for one drill

That session uses unadjusted scoring; persistent setting unchanged.

PRN-US-09: Session Interruption Recovery (Calls, Backgrounding, Connectivity Loss)

STATUS: Proposed (Gap)   PRIORITY: Medium   ACTOR: Learner

Intent: To resume a Pronunciation Coaching session exactly where it left off after being interrupted by a phone call, app backgrounding, or a dropped connection, without losing progress already scored.

Happy Path Steps

41. Interruption: User is mid-sentence in the Pronunciation Coach when an incoming call, OS backgrounding event, or connectivity drop occurs.

42. State Preservation: App immediately saves the current sentence index, already-scored words, and session progress to local storage.

43. Return: User returns to the app after the interruption ends.

44. Resume Prompt: App shows "Pick up where you left off?" referencing the exact sentence that was interrupted.

45. Continuation: User resumes at the same sentence with prior in-session scores intact.

Acceptance Criteria

• No previously scored word or sentence within the interrupted session may be lost due to an interruption.

• The resume prompt must reference the specific interrupted sentence, not just restart the session from the beginning.

• State must be preserved locally so resume works even if connectivity has not yet been restored.

Exception Handling

• E-01: Interruption During Active Recording. The call/backgrounding event occurs while audio is actively being captured, before submission. RESOLUTION: The partial, unsubmitted recording is discarded (not scored), and the user is asked to re-record that specific sentence on return - previously completed sentences remain untouched.

• E-02: Extended Absence. User does not return to the app for more than 24 hours after an interruption. RESOLUTION: System still preserves in-session progress but relabels the resume prompt as "Continue your previous session?" and offers a fresh-start alternative in case content is now stale.

• E-03: App Force-Closed by OS/User. The app is killed entirely rather than backgrounded. RESOLUTION: Local session state is periodically checkpointed (not only on interruption events) so recovery still works after a hard close.

• E-04: Connectivity Lost After Recording But Before Scoring. Audio was captured successfully but the network dropped before the scoring request completed. RESOLUTION: The recording is queued locally and automatically submitted once connectivity returns, without requiring the user to re-record (ties in with GAP-PC-06).

• E-05: Conflicting Session on a Second Device. User starts a new Pronunciation Coach session on a different device while an interrupted session is still pending resume on the first. RESOLUTION: System treats the most recently active session as current and archives the abandoned one, avoiding a conflicting duplicate-progress state.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-001

Incoming call mid-sentence, user returns within a minute

Resume prompt shows the exact interrupted sentence; prior scores intact.

TC-002

Interruption during active recording capture

Only the in-progress recording is discarded; earlier sentences unaffected.

TC-003

User returns after 2 days

Resume prompt offers both 'continue' and 'start fresh' options.

TC-004

App force-closed by OS

Session state still recoverable via periodic local checkpoints.

TC-005

Recording captured, network drops before scoring

Recording auto-submits once connectivity returns; no re-record needed.

 

PRN-US-10: Pronunciation Coach

STATUS: In Development PRIORITY: High ACTOR: Learner

Intent: To read sentences aloud and receive precise, word-level feedback to fix pronunciation errors.

Happy Path Steps

Prompt: AI presents a target English sentence on screen.

Execution: User reads the sentence aloud.

Evaluation: AI processes the audio and highlights specific mispronounced words in red/orange.

Retry: User selects a mispronounced word to hear the correct pronunciation, then repeats the sentence.

Acceptance Criteria

Feedback must be at the word level, visually highlighting errors.

Users must be able to retry the exact same sentence multiple times.

Exception Handling

E-01: Word Omission. User skips a word in the sentence entirely. RESOLUTION: System highlights the skipped word in a specific color (e.g., gray) indicating "Missed Word."

E-02: Local Accent False-Positive. User speaks clearly but with a strong regional accent (e.g., Pakistani English), which a generic AI might flag as incorrect. RESOLUTION: AI utilizes the "Local Accent Calibration" model to accept correct regional stress patterns without penalizing.

E-03: Heavy Stuttering / Disfluency. User stutters on a word multiple times. RESOLUTION: AI identifies the stutter, grades the final articulation of the word, but provides a gentle tip on pacing.

E-04: Background Speech Interference. Someone else speaks in the background while the user is reading. RESOLUTION: System detects multiple voice vectors and prompts: "Multiple voices detected. Try again in a quiet place."

Validation Test Cases

 Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

 TC-0 01

Perfect pronunciation read

All words highlighted green; high score given.

 TC-0 02

Mispronounce single word

Specific word highlighted red; audio playback of correct pronunciation available.

 TC-0 03

Skip word entirely

Skipped word marked as omitted; score adjusted.

 TC-0 04

Retry sentence

System re-evaluates the same sentence and updates the previous score.

 TC-0 05

Valid local accent

System accepts culturally standard pronunciations (e.g., Pakistani English traits) if Local Accent mode is active.

PRN-US-11: Pronunciation Retry Loop Mechanic

STATUS: In Development PRIORITY: High ACTOR: Learner

Intent: To repeatedly practice the exact same problematic sentence, receiving dynamic, updating feedback until the mispronounced word is mastered.

Happy Path Steps

Execution: User reads a sentence in the Pronunciation Coach.

Feedback: AI highlights the word "specifically" in red (mispronounced).

Retry Action: User taps the "Retry Sentence" button.

Re-Execution: User records the exact same sentence again, focusing on the highlighted word.

Dynamic Update: The AI re-evaluates. The word "specifically" turns green, and a success chime plays.

Acceptance Criteria

The system must allow infinite retries of the same sentence.

The UI must visibly transition a word from red/orange to green upon successful correction.

Exception Handling

E-01: Successive Failures (Frustration Loop). User fails to pronounce the target word correctly after 5 consecutive retries. RESOLUTION: System temporarily pauses the loop and offers an audio breakdown: "Let's listen to this word slowly syllable by syllable."

E-02: New Errors on Retry. User fixes the target word, but mispronounces a different word they had previously gotten right. RESOLUTION: System turns the new error red, but keeps the fixed word green, displaying: "Great job fixing 'specifically', but watch out for 'always'."

E-03: Accidental Early Submission. User clicks retry but accidentally hits stop before speaking. RESOLUTION: Discard the 0-second audio clip without penalizing the score and prompt: "Audio too short. Try again."

E-04: Audio Caching Bloat. User retries a sentence 20 times, filling local cache. RESOLUTION: App automatically flushes the temporary audio files of failed attempts once a successful attempt is logged.

Validation Test Cases

 Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

 TC-0 01

Successful retry

Highlighted word updates from red to green dynamically.

 TC-0 02

Fail 5 times in a row

UI interrupts with a slower, syllable-based audio example.

 TC-0 03

Fix one word, break another

UI accurately updates colors for both words independently.

 TC-0 04

Empty audio submission

System rejects input without lowering the previous score.

 TC-0 05

Local cache cleanup

System purges the .wav files of the failed attempts.

PRN-US-12: Pronunciation Coach - Word-Level Visual Highlighting

STATUS: In Development PRIORITY: High ACTOR: Learner

Intent: To receive precise, word-level visual feedback on a spoken sentence so the user knows exactly which specific phonemes to fix, rather than getting a vague overall score.

Happy Path Steps

Execution: User reads a target sentence aloud in the Pronunciation Coach.

Analysis: The AI transcribes the audio and compares the phonemes against the target sentence.

Display: The UI renders the full sentence on the screen.

Highlighting: Perfectly pronounced words turn green. Mispronounced words turn red. Words spoken clearly but with slight stress errors turn orange.

Action: User visually identifies the exact point of failure and taps "Retry" to focus on the red words.

Acceptance Criteria

Feedback must be mapped specifically to individual words in the UI, not just a global 0-100 score.

The system must distinguish between a minor stress error (orange) and a complete mispronunciation (red).

Exception Handling

E-01: Word Omission (Skipped Word). User reads the sentence but skips a word entirely. RESOLUTION: The skipped word is highlighted in gray and tagged with a strikethrough to indicate it was missed, not mispronounced.

E-02: Stuttering / Word Repetition. User says a word three times before getting it right. RESOLUTION: The AI evaluates the final, complete articulation of the word for the color code, but lowers the overarching "Fluency" score for the sentence.

E-03: Local Accent Calibration On. A Pakistani user speaks with heavy regional consonant stress while the "Local Accent" model is toggled on. RESOLUTION: System accepts valid regional variations (e.g., rolling an R) and highlights the word green, whereas the generic model might have flagged it red.

E-04: Background Noise Override. A loud noise interrupts the middle of the sentence. RESOLUTION: System marks the interrupted words as "Unscorable" rather than "Mispronounced" and prompts a retry.

ACC-US-01: Live Speech Verification (Anti-Playback / Anti-Cheat)

STATUS: Proposed   PRIORITY: High   ACTOR: Learner

Intent: To ensure the audio submitted for assessment is genuine live speech from the user, not a pre-recorded or replayed file, protecting the integrity of the accent profile and interview-readiness score.

Happy Path Steps

1. Prompt Generation: System generates a randomized passage/sentence at runtime (not a static, reusable file).

2. Live Capture: User reads the prompt aloud in real time via microphone.

3. Liveness Check: AI cross-checks ambient audio signature, timing jitter, and background noise consistency to confirm live capture (not a played-back file).

4. Acceptance: If liveness checks pass, audio proceeds to normal scoring pipeline.

Acceptance Criteria

●       System must randomize passage content per session so pre-recorded submissions cannot match the prompt.

●       System must flag audio with signal characteristics consistent with file playback (e.g., no ambient noise floor, compression artifacts).

Exception Handling

●       E-01: Detected Playback Audio. System identifies signal artifacts typical of a played-back recording. RESOLUTION: Reject submission, display "Live reading required — please read the passage directly into your microphone," and do not update the accent profile.

●       E-02: False Positive on Liveness Check (e.g., very clean studio mic). RESOLUTION: Allow user to appeal via a secondary short live-repeat prompt before permanently flagging the account.

●       E-03: Repeated Flags on Same Account. User is flagged for suspected playback 3+ times. RESOLUTION: Temporarily suspend accent-assessment access and route to support review.

●       E-04: Static/Cached Prompt Reuse. Client attempts to reuse a previously cached passage. RESOLUTION: Server rejects stale prompt IDs and forces a fresh passage fetch.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-01

Genuine live reading

Passes liveness check, scoring proceeds normally.

TC-02

Played-back audio file submitted

Submission rejected, profile not updated.

TC-03

Reused prompt ID

Server rejects, forces new passage.

TC-04

Repeated flags

Account routed to manual review after 3rd flag.

 

ACC-US-02: Voice Data Consent & Privacy Disclosure

STATUS: Proposed   PRIORITY: High   ACTOR: Learner

Intent: To obtain explicit, informed consent before recording and storing a user's voice data for accent analysis, and to give the user control over retention/deletion.

Happy Path Steps

1. First-Time Trigger: User attempts to start their first Accent Assessment.

2. Consent Screen: System displays a plain-language disclosure covering what is recorded, how long it is stored, and how it is used (AI scoring, profile generation).

3. Explicit Opt-In: User taps "I Agree" before microphone access is requested.

4. Ongoing Control: User can later view/delete stored voice samples from account settings.

Acceptance Criteria

●       System must block microphone access and assessment start until explicit consent is recorded.

●       User must be able to delete stored voice recordings at any time without losing their derived text-based accent profile scores.

Exception Handling

●       E-01: Consent Declined. User declines the disclosure. RESOLUTION: Block access to Accent Assessment module, explain the feature is unavailable without consent, and offer link to non-voice modules.

●       E-02: Consent Withdrawn Mid-Use. User revokes consent after months of use. RESOLUTION: Immediately stop new recordings, purge stored raw audio, and retain only aggregate scores unless user requests full deletion.

●       E-03: Regional Legal Requirement (e.g., data residency). RESOLUTION: Route storage to the compliant regional server before allowing recording to proceed.

●       E-04: Minor User Detected. Age-gate flags the account as a minor. RESOLUTION: Require parental/guardian consent flow before enabling voice recording.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-01

First-time consent accepted

Mic access granted, assessment proceeds.

TC-02

Consent declined

Module locked, no mic access requested.

TC-03

Consent withdrawn later

Raw audio purged, aggregate scores retained.

TC-04

Minor account detected

Parental consent flow triggered before recording.

 

ACC-US-03: Target Accent / English Variant Selection

STATUS: Proposed   PRIORITY: Medium   ACTOR: Learner

Intent: To let the user choose a target reference accent (e.g., General American, British RP, Neutral International) against which pronunciation and intonation are scored, since "clarity" targets differ by variant.

Happy Path Steps

1. Settings Navigation: User goes to "Accent Model Preference" and selects a Target Accent (separate from the existing Local Calibration toggle).

2. Confirmation: System explains how scoring will shift (e.g., vowel-length expectations differ for American vs British targets).

3. Recalibration: Future assessments and exercises score against the newly selected target variant.

4. Execution: User completes a reading passage scored against the chosen target.

Acceptance Criteria

●       System must support at least two distinct target-accent references at launch (e.g., General American, British RP).

●       Switching target accent must not overwrite or delete prior historical scores; it must be logged as a model-context change.

Exception Handling

●       E-01: Mid-History Switch. User switches target accent after 3 months of tracked progress. RESOLUTION: Visually annotate the progress tracker with a marker noting "Target accent changed on [date]" so trend lines aren't misread as regression.

●       E-02: Conflicting Selection with Local Calibration (overlaps US-017 E-02). RESOLUTION: Display combined guidance clarifying Local Calibration governs acceptable regional variance, Target Accent governs the pronunciation reference point; both can be active together.

●       E-03: Unsupported Target Requested. User requests a target accent not yet modeled (e.g., Australian English). RESOLUTION: Display "Coming soon" and default to closest supported variant, without silently applying it.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-01

Select British RP target

Future scoring uses British reference phonemes.

TC-02

Switch target mid-history

Tracker annotates the switch, no data loss.

TC-03

Unsupported target selected

System shows "coming soon," no silent fallback.

 

ACC-US-04: Score Dispute & Manual Feedback Loop

STATUS: Proposed   PRIORITY: Medium   ACTOR: Learner

Intent: To allow a user who believes an AI score was inaccurate to flag it for review, building trust in the scoring system and generating labeled data for model improvement.

Happy Path Steps

1. Score Review: User views a completed assessment or drill result.

2. Dispute Action: User taps "This score seems wrong" on a specific metric.

3. Reason Capture: User selects a short reason (e.g., "background noise," "misheard word," "unfair penalty").

4. Submission: System logs the dispute with the associated audio clip for review; user is notified once a response is available.

Acceptance Criteria

●       Dispute action must be available on every scored metric, not just the overall score.

●       System must not auto-correct the score without either an automated re-scoring pass or human/model review.

Exception Handling

●       E-01: High Volume of Disputes on Same Drill. Many users dispute the same phoneme/drill. RESOLUTION: Auto-flag the drill for content-team review of possible scoring-model bias.

●       E-02: Repeated Frivolous Disputes by Single User. RESOLUTION: Rate-limit disputes per user per day and display remaining allowance.

●       E-03: Dispute on Deleted Audio. User disputes a score after the underlying recording was auto-purged per retention policy. RESOLUTION: Inform user the raw audio is no longer available and offer a fresh re-assessment instead.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-01

Valid dispute submitted

Logged with audio, user notified of outcome.

TC-02

Dispute rate limit reached

Further disputes blocked until next day, message shown.

TC-03

Dispute on purged audio

User offered re-assessment instead of review.

 

ACC-US-05: Accent Profile Staleness & Re-Baseline Prompt

STATUS: Proposed   PRIORITY: Low   ACTOR: Learner

Intent: To keep the accent profile relevant by prompting re-assessment after long inactivity, since speech patterns and skill level can drift.

Happy Path Steps

1. Inactivity Detection: System detects no completed accent drills for 60+ days.

2. Re-Baseline Prompt: On next login, system suggests "Your accent profile is X days old — retake a quick baseline?"

3. User Choice: User accepts or dismisses.

4. Update: If accepted, a fresh baseline is generated; old data remains visible as history, not overwritten.

Acceptance Criteria

●       System must timestamp every baseline and display profile age to the user.

●       Re-baseline must never silently overwrite historical trend data.

Exception Handling

●       E-01: User Dismisses Repeatedly. RESOLUTION: Reduce prompt frequency (e.g., from every login to weekly) to avoid nagging.

●       E-02: Re-Baseline Requested Too Soon (e.g., next day). RESOLUTION: Allow it, but label it a "manual refresh" rather than a scheduled re-baseline to avoid skewing monthly comparisons.

●       E-03: Inactivity Exceeds 1 Year. RESOLUTION: Treat next assessment as a brand-new baseline (Month 1 reset) rather than continuing an outdated trend line, with a clear notice to the user.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-01

60-day inactivity

Re-baseline prompt shown on next login.

TC-02

Prompt dismissed 3x

Prompt frequency reduced.

TC-03

1-year+ inactivity

New baseline started, old data archived separately.

 

ACC-US-06: Microphone Permission & Device Compatibility Check

STATUS: Proposed   PRIORITY: High   ACTOR: Learner

Intent: To detect and gracefully handle missing or denied microphone permissions and incompatible devices before a user attempts an assessment, avoiding a broken/confusing experience.

Happy Path Steps

1. Pre-Check: On entering the Accent Assessment module, system checks mic permission status and basic input-level responsiveness.

2. Permission Request: If not yet granted, system requests OS-level mic permission with a clear rationale.

3. Input Test: A short "say a word to test your mic" step confirms audio is being captured before the real assessment starts.

4. Proceed: Once confirmed, user proceeds to the actual reading passage.

Acceptance Criteria

●       System must never start a scored assessment without first confirming a live, working audio input.

●       Permission-denial messaging must include a path to fix it (link to device settings instructions).

Exception Handling

●       E-01: Permission Denied by OS. RESOLUTION: Show blocking message with step-by-step instructions to enable mic access in device settings; do not proceed to assessment.

●       E-02: Permission Granted but No Audio Detected (e.g., muted hardware switch, faulty mic). RESOLUTION: Show "We can't hear you — check your microphone" with a retry button before allowing assessment start.

●       E-03: Unsupported Browser/Device. RESOLUTION: Display compatibility notice and suggest a supported browser/app version.

●       E-04: Permission Revoked Mid-Session. User revokes mic permission while an assessment is in progress. RESOLUTION: Pause assessment, discard the partial recording, and prompt to re-grant before resuming.

Validation Test Cases

Expected Result

TC-03

Mic muted at hardware level

ACC-US-07: Adaptive Difficulty Progression for Targeted Exercises

STATUS: Proposed   PRIORITY: Medium   ACTOR: Learner

Intent: To scale exercise difficulty as the user improves, preventing plateauing on drills that are now too easy and keeping practice meaningfully challenging.

Happy Path Steps

1. Performance Tracking: System tracks per-phoneme/per-metric success rate across sessions (builds on ACC-US-13).

2. Threshold Check: When a specific weak point is consistently scored above a mastery threshold (e.g., 3 consecutive high scores), system marks it "improved."

3. Difficulty Escalation: AI generates harder variants (longer words, faster pacing, embedded in full sentences) for that point instead of repeating basic drills.

4. Rebalancing: Newly surfaced weak points from the harder drills feed back into the exercise queue.

Acceptance Criteria

●       System must not keep serving mastered drills at the original difficulty once the mastery threshold is met.

●       Difficulty escalation must be traceable in the user's session history (so progress is explainable, not opaque).

Exception Handling

●       E-01: Mastery Then Regression. User masters a phoneme, then later fails harder variants. RESOLUTION: Down-shift difficulty one level rather than sending the user back to the original baseline drill.

●       E-02: Uneven Mastery Across Metrics. User masters Pronunciation but not Intonation. RESOLUTION: Escalate difficulty independently per metric rather than gating on overall improvement.

●       E-03: Gaming the Threshold. User repeats an easy phrase they already know well to trigger fast escalation. RESOLUTION: Require variety across distinct drill items (not repeats of the same phrase) to count toward the mastery threshold.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-01

3 consecutive high scores

Harder variant drill generated next.

TC-02

Regression on harder drill

Difficulty steps down one level, not full reset.

TC-03

Mastery on one metric only

Only that metric's difficulty escalates.

 

ACC-US-08: Multi-Speaker / Background Voice Interference Detection

STATUS: Proposed   PRIORITY: Medium   ACTOR: Learner

Intent: To distinguish between generic background noise (already handled in ACC-US-14 E-03) and interference from a second human voice, which can corrupt phoneme-level scoring in a different way than white noise.

Happy Path Steps

1. Capture: User records the passage as normal.

2. Voice-Isolation Check: AI detects whether a secondary distinct voice is present in the recording.

3. Isolation: If a secondary voice is faint/separable, system isolates the primary speaker and proceeds.

4. Scoring: Assessment proceeds using only the isolated primary-speaker audio.

Acceptance Criteria

●       System must differentiate "background noise" (already handled) from "competing human speech" and apply distinct resolutions.

●       Isolated audio used for scoring must be flagged internally as "processed" for QA/audit purposes.

Exception Handling

●       E-01: Second Voice Too Prominent to Isolate. RESOLUTION: Reject the recording with message: "We detected another person speaking — please record in a quiet space alone," distinct from the generic noise message in ACC-US-14.

●       E-02: Overlapping Speech During Multisyllabic Words. RESOLUTION: Flag only the affected words as "unscored due to interference" rather than failing the entire passage.

●       E-03: False Positive (e.g., TV/radio in background mistaken for scorable speech). RESOLUTION: Same rejection path as E-01, since the AI cannot reliably distinguish source at low confidence.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-01

Faint second voice, isolable

Primary speaker isolated, scoring proceeds.

TC-02

Prominent second voice

Recording rejected with specific messaging.

TC-03

Partial word overlap

Only affected words marked unscored.

 

ACC-US-09: Sub-Dialect Granularity Within Local Accent Calibration

STATUS: Proposed   PRIORITY: Low   ACTOR: Learner (South Asian / Pakistani)

Intent: To refine the single "South Asian / Pakistani English" model (US-017) into recognizable sub-dialect influences (e.g., Punjabi-, Sindhi-, Pashto-influenced English), since regional stress-pattern variance within Pakistan itself is significant.

Happy Path Steps

1. Extended Settings: Under "Local Accent Calibration," user optionally selects a sub-region influence in addition to the base toggle.

2. Recalibration: System narrows the accepted phonetic-shift range to the selected sub-dialect rather than the broad national model.

3. Execution: User reads a practice sentence.

4. Evaluation: AI scores using the narrower sub-dialect tolerance, improving precision over the generic regional model.

Acceptance Criteria

●       Sub-dialect selection must remain optional; users who skip it default to the existing broad "South Asian/Pakistani" model (no regression to current behavior).

●       System must clearly state this is a beta/best-effort refinement if confidence data is limited for a given sub-dialect.

Exception Handling

●       E-01: Low-Confidence Sub-Model. Selected sub-dialect has insufficient training data. RESOLUTION: Display "Limited data for this dialect — using broader regional model for now" and fall back automatically.

●       E-02: Mixed-Dialect Household/Speaker. User's speech doesn't cleanly match one sub-dialect. RESOLUTION: Allow reverting to the broad model at any time without losing prior scores.

●       E-03: Sub-Dialect Misclassification Complaint. User disputes their assigned sub-dialect tolerance (ties into GAP-04 dispute flow). RESOLUTION: Route to the same score-dispute mechanism.

Validation Test Cases

Scenario

Expected Result

Narrower tolerance applied, scoring proceeds.

TC-02

Sub-dialect selected, low data

Falls back to broad model with notice.

TC-03

Revert to broad model

Historical scores preserved unchanged.

ACC-US-11: Local Accent Calibration Model Activation

STATUS: In Development PRIORITY: High (Market Differentiator) ACTOR: Learner (South Asian / Pakistani)

Intent: To receive accurate, culturally relevant pronunciation scoring that accounts for regional stress patterns rather than being unfairly penalized by a generic Western accent model.

Happy Path Steps

Settings Navigation: User navigates to profile settings and selects "Accent Model Preference".

Model Selection: User toggles on "South Asian / Pakistani English" calibration.

Recalibration: System updates the user's acoustic evaluation profile.

Execution: User reads a practice sentence.

Evaluation: AI scores the audio, accepting valid regional stress patterns and consonant substitutions without flagging them as errors.

Acceptance Criteria

The system must offer a clear toggle between "Generic Global" and "Local Accent" models.

The calibration must correctly ignore common regional phonetic shifts (e.g., typical Urdu-influenced English stress patterns) while still catching genuine mispronunciations.

Exception Handling

E-01: Extreme Dialect Distortion. User speaks with a dialect so heavy it breaks the Speech-to-Text transcriber entirely. RESOLUTION: AI falls back to phonetic clarity scoring and prompts the user to speak slightly slower.

E-02: Conflicting Model Usage. User attempts to practice a strict "Western Accent Improvement" drill while the Local Calibration toggle is on.

RESOLUTION: System displays a prompt advising the user to temporarily disable Local Calibration for this specific drill.

E-03: Model Loading Failure. The local acoustic model fails to load from the server. RESOLUTION: System defaults to the generic global model and displays a minor warning: "Using standard pronunciation model due to network latency."

Validation Test Cases

 TC-0 02

Toggle model off

Same audio file is re-scored lower against the strict Western baseline.

Genuine mispronunciation

Word is highlighted in red regardless of the active model.

 TC-0 04

Extreme distortion

 TC-0 05

Review: User views the positive trend lines reinforcing their practice efforts.

Acceptance Criteria

The tracker must break down progress into exactly four sub-metrics: Pronunciation, Word Stress, Intonation, and Clarity.

The UI must support a month-over-month view (e.g., Month 1 vs Month 3).

Exception Handling

E-01: Insufficient Historical Data. User opens the tracker during their first week of app usage. RESOLUTION: Display current baseline scores with locked "Future Month" columns, stating: "Keep practicing! Check back next month to see your trend."

E-02: Score Regression. A user's Month 3 score is lower than their Month 1 score. RESOLUTION: Visually highlight the drop without extreme negative colors (avoid red), and offer a quick CTA: "Let's review some targeted exercises to boost this back up!"

ACC-US-13: Accent Improvement Targeted Exercises

PSC-US-01: Public Speaking Coach

Happy Path Steps

Selection: User selects speech format (e.g., pitch, TED-style talk).

Analysis: AI evaluates confidence, speech structure, pacing, voice clarity, tone variation, filler words, and audience engagement.

Feedback: AI generates a comprehensive delivery scorecard.

Acceptance Criteria

Must support video recording and extract both audio and visual data.

AI must specifically count and flag filler words (um, ah, like).

Exception Handling

E-01: File Size / Duration Exceeded. User attempts to record/upload a video longer than the server limits. RESOLUTION: Stop recording at the max time limit automatically (e.g., 5 mins) and display a warning.

E-02: No Face Detected in Video. Camera is pointed at a wall or lighting is too dark. RESOLUTION: System warns "Face not detected. Eye contact and body language cannot be scored." and falls back to audio-only scoring.

E-03: Out of Frame Movement. User paces out of the camera's view mid- speech. RESOLUTION: Flag "Wandering/Out of Frame" on the feedback scorecard under physical presence.

E-04: Excessive Filler Words. User says "um" between every word, breaking transcription logic. RESOLUTION: Cap filler word count at 50+ and issue a primary alert focusing solely on pausing instead of speaking.

E-05: Audio/Video Desync. Device latency causes video to lag behind audio. RESOLUTION: Process evaluation based primarily on the audio track while warning the user about device performance.

PSC-US-08: Filler Word Tracking & Visualization

STATUS: In Development PRIORITY: Medium ACTOR: Learner

Intent: To view a precise breakdown of filler words (um, ah, like, you know) used during an audio/video session to identify and eliminate nervous verbal tics.

Categorization: System lists the specific words used and their frequency (e.g., "Um: 12 times", "Like: 5 times").

Acceptance Criteria

AI transcription must explicitly capture and tag filler words, rather than silently filtering them out as standard Speech-to-Text models often do.

The scorecard must provide an actionable tip on using silence (pausing) instead of filler words.

Exception Handling

E-01: "Like" as a Valid Word. User uses the word "like" in a grammatically correct context (e.g., "I like this project"). RESOLUTION: AI utilizes NLP context mapping to differentiate between "like" as a verb/preposition and "like" as a syntactic filler, ignoring the valid usage.

E-02: Heavy Breathing / Mic Pops. The microphone picks up heavy breathing and the STT model misinterprets it as an "ah." RESOLUTION: Implement an acoustic confidence threshold; discard suspected filler words that match breathing decibel patterns.

E-03: Zero Filler Words (Perfect Score). User uses no filler words in a 5-minute speech. RESOLUTION: Celebrate the achievement heavily on the UI, displaying a "Flawless Delivery" badge.

Validation Test Cases

 Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

 TC-0 02

Differentiating "like"

System ignores "I like apples" but tags "It was, like, bad".

 TC-0 03

Audio jumps to the exact timestamp where the filler word occurred.

 TC-0 04

Zero filler words

System awards maximum score and a specific achievement badge.

 TC-0 05

PSC-US-10: Low-Bandwidth Video-to-Audio Fallback

STATUS: In Development PRIORITY: High ACTOR: Learner (South Asian Market)

Intent: To ensure users can still submit Public Speaking practice sessions even if they are on a poor mobile data connection that cannot handle large video uploads.

Happy Path Steps

Execution: User records a 5-minute video for the Business Pitch scenario.

Upload Attempt: App initiates the video upload to the AI processing server.

Bandwidth Check: System detects an extremely slow upload speed (e.g., <500 kbps) or a connection timeout.

Fallback Prompt: App pauses upload and prompts: "Connection is slow. Convert to audio-only to save data and process faster?"

Conversion: User accepts; the app locally strips the video track, uploads only the lightweight MP3/WAV, and scores the speech based on audio metrics.

Acceptance Criteria

The conversion from video to audio must happen client-side (on the phone) to immediately relieve the bandwidth bottleneck.

The resulting scorecard must gracefully hide the "Eye Contact" and "Physical Presence" metrics, marking them as N/A.

Exception Handling

E-01: User Rejects Fallback. User insists on uploading the full video despite the slow connection warning. RESOLUTION: Move the upload to a background service, allow the user to continue using other app features, and send a push notification when processing finally completes.

E-02: Device Storage Full During Conversion. The local device lacks the storage space to safely execute the MP4 to MP3 extraction. RESOLUTION:

Abort extraction, display a "Storage Full" error, and ask the user to clear space or retry when on Wi-Fi.

E-03: Complete Network Loss. Connection drops entirely during the audio fallback upload. RESOLUTION: Cache the audio file securely and auto-resume the upload silently when the connection is restored.

Validation Test Cases

 Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

 TC-0 01

Detect slow bandwidth

System triggers the fallback prompt after a calculated timeout.

 TC-0 02

Accept fallback

App strips video, uploads audio only, generates partial scorecard.

 TC-0 03

Reject fallback

App moves heavy video upload to a background background job.

 TC-0 04

UI scorecard adjustment

Eye contact metric is cleanly hidden when audio-only is processed.

 TC-0 05

Complete network drop

File caches locally; upload resumes on network reconnect.

PSC-US-11: Public Speaking Coach - Speaking Pace Analytics

STATUS: In Development PRIORITY: Medium ACTOR: Learner / Student / Professional

Intent: To deliver a speech and receive precise AI analysis on speaking pace to ensure the presentation is neither rushed nor sluggish.

Happy Path Steps

Selection: User selects the Public Speaking Coach and begins a speech (e.g., Presentation or Business Pitch).

Delivery: User records the speech via voice or video.

Pace Analysis: AI extracts the audio track and calculates the Words Per Minute (WPM).

Scoring: AI maps the WPM against standard ideal pacing for public speaking (typically 130-160 WPM).

Feedback: AI delivers a detailed scorecard that includes actionable advice on "Speaking Pace".

Acceptance Criteria

The system must dynamically measure WPM and identify distinct sections of the speech that were rushed vs. appropriately paced.

Must support processing from both pure audio and extracted video files.

Exception Handling

E-01: Severe Stuttering/Disfluency. User stutters heavily, drastically lowering the raw WPM. RESOLUTION: Acoustic model separates stuttering from deliberate pacing, penalizing 'Fluency' instead of artificially dropping the 'Pace' score.

E-02: Silent Pausing. User uses deliberate 3-5 second pauses for dramatic effect. RESOLUTION: AI identifies these as intentional rhetorical pauses rather than a slow speaking pace, rewarding the "Tone Variation" metric.

E-03: Hyper-Fast Rushing (Nerves). User speaks at >180 WPM. RESOLUTION: Feedback explicitly flags the speech as "Rushed," noting that the audience may struggle to comprehend the information.

E-04: Non-Standard Accents Skewing STT. A strong local accent causes the Speech-to-Text engine to miss words, falsely lowering the WPM count.

RESOLUTION: System relies on Local Accent Calibration to correctly detect syllables and calculate pace regardless of STT exact word matches.

Validation Test Cases

 Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

 TC-0 01

Speech at 145 WPM

AI scores speaking pace as optimal.

 TC-0 02

Speech at 190 WPM

System flags pace as rushed and suggests slowing down.

 TC-0 03

Intentional 5-second pause

AI does not penalize pace; rewards tone variation.

 TC-0 04

Heavy stuttering

System flags fluency error rather than general pace error.

 TC-0 05

AI correctly extracts audio to calculate the pacing metrics.

PSC-US-12: Public Speaking Coach - Audience Q&A Simulation

STATUS: In Development PRIORITY: Medium ACTOR: Professional / Student

Intent: To practice handling impromptu follow-up questions from the audience immediately after delivering a structured presentation or pitch.

Happy Path Steps

Delivery: User successfully completes recording a "Business Pitch" or "Classroom Presentation".

Prompt: Instead of immediately ending, the AI simulates an audience member: "Great presentation. I have one question..."

Execution: The AI asks a dynamically generated question based specifically on the content of the user's speech.

Impromptu Response: User must answer the unexpected question via voice within a set time limit (e.g., 60 seconds).

Feedback: Scorecard evaluates the original presentation, but adds a section grading "Q&A Handling" (Composure, Relevance).

Acceptance Criteria

The AI must synthesize the user's transcript in near real-time to generate a logically relevant follow-up question.

The Q&A phase must test impromptu speaking mechanics (limiting filler words under pressure).

Exception Handling

E-01: Nonsense/Empty Presentation. User uploads a presentation consisting of just counting to 10. RESOLUTION: AI cannot generate a relevant question; it skips the Q&A phase entirely and immediately provides a failing presentation scorecard.

E-02: User Freezes (Silence). User panics at the unexpected question and remains silent. RESOLUTION: AI provides a supportive tip in the feedback about buying time during Q&A (e.g., "That's a great question, let me think about that for a second...").

E-03: Defensive/Aggressive Answer. User argues angrily with the AI's question. RESOLUTION: Feedback penalizes "Professional Tone" and highlights the importance of accepting audience feedback gracefully.

Validation Test Cases

 Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

 TC-0 01

Valid presentation

AI generates a highly specific question based on the speech content.

 TC-0 02

Answer Q&A confidently

Scorecard awards high marks for Composure and Relevance.

 TC-0 03

User freezes

Feedback explicitly addresses hesitation in Q&A settings.

 TC-0 04

Empty/Nonsense speech

AI correctly bypasses Q&A simulation due to lack of context.

 TC-0 05

Aggressive response

System flags tone as unprofessional for a speaker.

PSC-US-13: AI Audio/Video Feedback - Eye Contact & Presence Scoring

STATUS: In Development PRIORITY: High ACTOR: Learner / Professional

Intent: To record a video presentation so the AI can evaluate non-verbal communication, specifically eye contact and overall physical presence, mimicking a real audience.

Happy Path Steps

Execution: User initiates a Public Speaking or Mock Interview session and grants camera permissions.

Recording: User records their response while looking at their device camera.

Processing: The system extracts the video track and runs a computer-vision algorithm to map facial orientation.

Analysis: The AI calculates the percentage of time the user maintained direct eye contact versus looking away/reading notes.

Feedback: The scorecard visually separates "Audio Delivery" from "Physical Presence," displaying the Eye Contact percentage with actionable tips.

Acceptance Criteria

The system must track gaze direction and calculate a discrete "Eye Contact" score separate from vocal metrics.

The app must prompt the user to position their face within a designated on- screen frame before recording begins.

Exception Handling

E-01: Poor Lighting / Silhouette. The user is backlit (e.g., sitting in front of a bright window) and facial features cannot be mapped. RESOLUTION: The recording screen displays a real-time warning before recording: "Lighting is too dark to track eye contact. Please adjust your lighting."

E-02: Out of Frame. The user wanders out of the camera's view during a 5- minute presentation. RESOLUTION: The AI penalizes the "Overall Presentation" score and marks the exact timestamps where the user left the frame.

E-03: Multiple Faces Detected. The camera detects the user and another person in the background. RESOLUTION: System locks onto the primary (closest) face for eye-contact metrics and ignores background figures.

E-04: Reading Off-Screen Script. User constantly looks down and to the left to read a script. RESOLUTION: Scorecard highlights "Low Eye Contact," explicitly suggesting the user is reading and advising them to use bullet points instead.

Validation Test Cases

 Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

 TC-0 01

Steady eye contact maintained

System awards >90% Eye Contact score.

 TC-0 02

Looking down frequently

Scorecard accurately reflects low eye contact and flags script-reading.

 TC-0 03

Backlit environment

UI blocks recording start until lighting improves or user switches to audio-only.

 TC-0 04

Subject walks out of frame

Time out of frame is calculated and lowers overall presence score.

 TC-0 05

Two faces in camera view

System accurately tracks the primary speaker's gaze.

PSC-US-14: Public Speaking Coach - Voice Clarity & Projection Analysis

STATUS: In Development PRIORITY: Medium ACTOR: Learner / Student / Professional

Intent: To evaluate the physical projection and clarity of the user's voice during a speech to ensure they can be understood clearly in a large room (e.g., Classroom Presentation).

Happy Path Steps

Execution: User begins recording a "Classroom Presentation" via the Public Speaking Coach.

Audio Capture: The system captures the raw audio input, specifically measuring decibel (dB) variance and phonetic sharpness.

Analysis: The AI evaluates "Voice Clarity"—checking for mumbling, trailing off at the end of sentences, or insufficient volume.

Feedback: The post-session scorecard highlights specific timestamps where the user's voice dropped or mumbled, providing tips on diaphragmatic breathing.

Acceptance Criteria

The acoustic model must specifically track volume consistency (projection) separate from basic pronunciation correctness.

The feedback must distinguish between hardware issues (bad mic) and human delivery issues (mumbling).

Exception Handling

E-01: Consistent Low Volume (Hardware Issue). The entire recording is at 10% volume, indicating the user's microphone gain is set too low. RESOLUTION: The system drops the "Projection" penalty and instead displays a hardware warning: "Your microphone volume is very low. Please check device settings."

E-02: Sudden Screaming. User shouts loudly into the microphone, causing extreme audio clipping. RESOLUTION: The AI heavily penalizes Voice Clarity for distortion and provides a tip on proper microphone distance.

E-03: Trailing Off Detection. User speaks clearly at the start of a sentence but mumbles the final words. RESOLUTION: The AI flags this specific behavioral pattern in the scorecard, noting: "Try to maintain your energy through the end of your sentences."

Validation Test Cases

 Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

 TC-0 01

Clear, well-projected speech

High Voice Clarity score awarded.

 TC-0 02

Sentence trailing off

Scorecard specifically identifies the drop in volume at sentence endings.

 TC-0 03

Microphone gain too

Hardware warning triggered; projection penalty low bypassed.

 TC-0 04

Screaming/Clipping

Distorted audio penalized under Voice Clarity.

 TC-0 05

Mumbling detection

System detects slurred phonemes and flags them as clarity errors.

Scenario-Based Learning

SBL-US-01: Scenario-Based Learning Contexts

STATUS: In Development PRIORITY: Medium ACTOR: Learner

Intent: To practice conversational English in highly specific, realistic daily scenarios (e.g., Restaurant, Airport, Customer Support) to build practical vocabulary.

Happy Path Steps

Selection: User navigates to the Scenario library and selects "Restaurant - Ordering Food".

Context Delivery: System presents the expected vocabulary and context for the scene.

Roleplay: AI adopts the persona (e.g., Waiter) and opens the conversation.

Feedback: After completion, AI specifically grades the user on how well they applied the expected contextual vocabulary.

Acceptance Criteria

Each scenario must load a distinct pre-defined list of expected vocabulary words.

AI feedback must highlight which expected words were successfully used and which were missed.

Exception Handling

E-01: Off-Topic User Input. In a restaurant scenario, the user starts talking about fixing a car. RESOLUTION: AI (in character as the waiter) responds confused: "I'm sorry, we don't have cars on the menu. Would you like to hear today's specials?"

E-02: Vocabulary Bypass. User completes the scenario using extremely basic words, avoiding all targeted vocabulary. RESOLUTION: System grades the session as grammatically correct but flags a low "Scenario Vocabulary" score.

E-03: Silent Roleplay. User enters the scenario but doesn't speak. RESOLUTION: AI prompts twice, then gently auto-closes the scenario saving progress.

SBL-US-06: Scenario-Based Learning - Custom Scenario Expansion (Admin)

STATUS: In Development PRIORITY: Low ACTOR: Administrator

Intent: To quickly spin up a highly specific, niche scenario (e.g., "Negotiating a Salary Raise") and add it to the Scenario- Based Learning library to address user requests or market trends.

Happy Path Steps

Navigation: Admin opens Content Management.

Creation: Admin clicks "Create Custom Scenario" and assigns it to the "Workplace" category.

Definition: Admin defines the AI persona ("Strict Manager"), the scenario goal ("User must ask for a 10% raise"), and 5 target vocabulary words (e.g., "compensation, value, market rate").

Deployment: Admin publishes the new scenario.

Access: The new "Salary Negotiation" scenario immediately appears for all learners without an app update.

Acceptance Criteria

The custom scenario builder must allow the definition of an AI persona, a user goal, and expected vocabulary.

Deployment must bypass App Store updates by utilizing a cloud-based JSON configuration fetch.

Exception Handling

E-01: Unachievable Scenario Goal. The Admin sets a goal that the AI prompt logic naturally prevents (e.g., "Convince the strict manager to double your salary immediately"). RESOLUTION: The AI will realistically reject the user's requests. If the user complains, the Admin can use the Sandbox tester (US-081) to recalibrate the strictness of the prompt.

E-02: Missing Vocabulary Definitions. Admin creates the scenario but forgets to assign target vocabulary. RESOLUTION: Validation blocks deployment; scenarios require a minimum of 3 target words to drive the scoring engine.

E-03: Scenario Name Collision. Admin tries to name the scenario "Client Meeting," which already exists. RESOLUTION: System requires unique scenario titles and prompts the Admin to rename it (e.g., "Client Meeting - Escalation").

Validation Test Cases

Scenario

Expected Result

User completes custom scenario

System accurately grades the user against the newly defined target words.

 TC-0 05

Code-Switch Coaching

CSC-US-01: Code-Switch Coaching & Correction

STATUS: In Development PRIORITY: High (Market Differentiator) ACTOR: Learner (South Asian Market)

Intent: To identify when the user mixes local languages (e.g., Urdu) with English and provide direct English equivalents to improve professional fluency.

Happy Path Steps

Execution: User speaks a sentence mixing English and a local word (e.g., "Please process this jaldi").

Detection: AI processes the audio and flags the code-switched word.

Feedback: AI suggests the pure English equivalent (e.g., "quickly" or "urgently").

Logging: System adds the word to the user's personalized "common code- switch words" list for future targeted practice.

Acceptance Criteria

The AI must specifically isolate the non-English word without failing the entire transcription.

The feedback must explicitly explain why the word is inappropriate for professional settings and offer alternatives.

Exception Handling

E-01: Proper Noun False Positive. User says a local name or location (e.g., "I visited Lahore"). RESOLUTION: AI cross-references a Named Entity Recognition (NER) list and skips flagging recognized proper nouns.

E-02: Transcription Complete Failure. The mix of languages completely breaks the Speech-to-Text model. RESOLUTION: AI prompts: "I had trouble understanding that mix of words. Can you try saying the whole sentence in English?"

E-03: Local Slang vs Code Switch. User uses an English slang word heavily used locally (e.g., "prepone"). RESOLUTION: AI handles this under "Professional Tone" rather than strict Code-Switching, suggesting standard corporate alternatives (e.g., "bring forward").

Validation Test Cases

 Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

 TC-0 01

Valid code-switch input

AI isolates word, suggests English translation.

 TC-0 02

Proper noun usage

AI accepts sentence without flagging code-switching.

 TC-0 03

Add to personal list

Successfully flagged word appears in user's practice tracker.

 TC-0 04

Complete local language sentence

AI prompts user to switch entirely to English.

 TC-0 05

Slang detection

AI suggests standard English equivalent (Tone adjustment).

CSC-US-02: Code-Switch Personal Word List Management

STATUS: In Development PRIORITY: Medium (Market Differentiator) ACTOR: Learner (South Asian Market)

Intent: To track and review a personalized list of non-English/Urdu words the user frequently mixes into their English sentences so they can target them for elimination in professional settings.

Happy Path Steps

Detection: User accidentally code-switches (e.g., uses an Urdu word) during an AI Conversation.

Logging: The AI flags the word, provides the English equivalent, and automatically adds it to the user's "Code-Switch Word List".

Navigation: User opens the Progress Dashboard and clicks on "My Target Words".

Review: System displays the list of local words alongside their professional English equivalents.

Practice: User can tap a word to initiate a mini-drill focusing on utilizing the correct English term in a sentence.

Acceptance Criteria

The list must be automatically populated by the AI during conversational practice; no manual entry required.

Words must be paired with their exact contextual English translation.

Exception Handling

E-01: False Positive Removal. The AI incorrectly flagged a proper noun (e.g., a local city name) as a code-switched word. RESOLUTION: User swipes left on the word in their list and clicks "Remove/Ignore," training the local model to ignore it in the future.

E-02: Extreme List Bloat. The user has code-switched 500 unique times. RESOLUTION: The UI categorizes the list by "Frequency of Use," pushing the most commonly used local words to the top for priority practice.

E-03: Empty List State. The user checks the list but has never code-switched during practice. RESOLUTION: Show an empty state: "Great job maintaining pure English! Words will appear here if you accidentally mix languages."

E-04: Multiple Context Translations. An Urdu word has different English meanings depending on the context. RESOLUTION: The list saves the specific sentence the user spoke to show exactly which English equivalent was required in that moment.
