PSA-US-03: Post-Session Actionable Script - Advanced Vocabulary Injection

STATUS: In Development PRIORITY: High (Market Differentiator) ACTOR: Learner

Intent: To view a polished rewrite of their spoken answer that specifically replaces basic words with advanced, professional vocabulary, helping them level up their language skills.

Happy Path Steps

Execution: User answers an Interview Coach question using basic vocabulary (e.g., "I made the project better").

Analysis: AI processes the transcript and identifies opportunities to elevate the language.

Rewrite Generation: AI generates the Post-Session Actionable Script, substituting basic verbs/nouns for professional equivalents (e.g., "I optimized the project to enhance performance").

Display: The UI presents the Before/After comparison, explicitly highlighting the newly injected advanced words in bold or a distinct color.

Learning Loop: User reads the new script and absorbs the contextual use of the advanced vocabulary.

Acceptance Criteria

The rewrite algorithm must not alter the factual truth of the user's answer; it must only elevate the phrasing.

Injected vocabulary must match the context of the scenario (e.g., technical jargon for tech interviews, formal phrasing for Visa interviews).

Exception Handling

E-01: User Already Uses Advanced Vocabulary. The user provides a flawless, highly articulate answer using excellent vocabulary. RESOLUTION: The AI recognizes the high level and does not force arbitrary changes. The feedback states: "Excellent phrasing! Here is a slightly more concise alternative," rather than a heavy rewrite.

E-02: Factual Hallucination. The AI attempts to sound professional and accidentally adds a skill the user didn't mention (e.g., rewriting "I fixed the bug" to "I utilized Python to debug the system"). RESOLUTION: Strict LLM system prompts block the addition of any nouns or specific skills not present in the original transcript.

E-03: Overly Complex Jargon. The AI rewrite is so dense it sounds unnatural (e.g., "I elucidated the paradigm"). RESOLUTION: System prompts cap the reading-level complexity of the rewrite to "Professional Conversational," avoiding archaic or robotic vocabulary.

Validation Test Cases

 Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

 TC-0 01

Basic input provided

AI rewrites the sentence injecting contextual, professional verbs.

 TC-0 02

Flawless input provided

AI praises the vocabulary and offers a minor structural alternative.

 TC-0 03

UI highlighting

Newly injected advanced words are visually distinct in the 'After' text.

 TC-0 04

Hallucination block

Rewrite strictly maintains the user's original facts without adding new skills.

 TC-0 05

Tone matching

Rewrite for a Startup HR interview uses modern professional terms, not archaic language.

WhatsApp-Based Practice Mode



WAP-US-01: WhatsApp Account Linking Verification (OTP Security)

STATUS: Proposed   PRIORITY: High   ACTOR: Learner / Casual User

Intent: To securely verify ownership before linking a WhatsApp number to a Speeky-AI account, since the current flow (WAP-US-12 E-01) links accounts by simply asking for an email with no proof of ownership, exposing accounts to takeover.

Happy Path Steps

1. Trigger: User messages from an unrecognized number and replies with their Speeky-AI email to link accounts.

2. OTP Dispatch: System sends a one-time verification code to the email on file (not to WhatsApp) or to the previously-linked number if one exists.

3. Confirmation: User enters the OTP back into the WhatsApp chat within a set window.

4. Link Established: System binds the new WhatsApp number to the account and confirms via message.

Acceptance Criteria

●       System must never link a WhatsApp number to an account on the basis of an email address alone.

●       OTP must expire after a defined short window (e.g., 10 minutes) and be single-use.

Exception Handling

●       E-01: Incorrect OTP Entered. User mistypes the verification code. RESOLUTION: Allow up to 3 attempts, then invalidate the code and require the user to restart the linking flow.

●       E-02: OTP Expired. User replies with the code after the expiry window. RESOLUTION: Reject the code and prompt the user to request a new one.

●       E-03: Email Not Found in System. User provides an email that has no matching Speeky-AI account. RESOLUTION: Reply: "We couldn't find an account with that email — check for typos or sign up in the app first."

●       E-04: Account Already Linked to Another Number. The target account already has a different WhatsApp number linked. RESOLUTION: Require confirmation via the existing linked number or app login before allowing the switch, and notify the old number of the change.

●       E-05: Repeated Failed Linking Attempts. Same WhatsApp number fails linking verification 5+ times. RESOLUTION: Temporarily cool down further linking attempts from that number for security.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-01

Valid OTP entered in time

Account linked, confirmation message sent.

TC-02

Wrong OTP entered 3x

Linking flow invalidated, restart required.

TC-03

Expired OTP submitted

Code rejected, new code offered.

TC-04

Relinking an already-linked account

Old number notified, confirmation required before switch.

 

WAP-US-02: 24-Hour Messaging Window & Re-Engagement Template Compliance

STATUS: Proposed   PRIORITY: High   ACTOR: Learner / Casual User

Intent: To comply with WhatsApp Business API policy, which restricts free-form bot replies to within 24 hours of the user's last message, and requires pre-approved template messages for any re-engagement outside that window (e.g., Daily Challenge nudges in WAP-US-12).

Happy Path Steps

1. Window Tracking: System timestamps each inbound user message to track the active 24-hour session.

2. In-Window Reply: Bot replies freely with conversational content while inside the window.

3. Window Expiry: System detects the 24-hour window has closed since the user's last message.

4. Template Send: For re-engagement (e.g., daily challenge prompt), system sends a pre-approved WhatsApp template message instead of a free-form message.

Acceptance Criteria

●       System must never attempt a free-form message outside the 24-hour customer-service window.

●       All proactive/re-engagement messages (daily challenge triggers, streak reminders) must use Meta-approved templates.

Exception Handling

●       E-01: Template Message Rejected by Meta. A submitted template fails approval or is later disabled. RESOLUTION: Fall back to a generic approved template and flag the content team to resubmit.

●       E-02: User Replies After Template Send. User responds to a re-engagement template, reopening the 24-hour window. RESOLUTION: Resume free-form conversational replies immediately.

●       E-03: Daily Challenge Trigger Lands Mid-Window. The scheduled daily challenge time falls while the user is already inside an open free-form window. RESOLUTION: Send the challenge as a normal free-form message instead of a template, to avoid unnecessary template cost/friction.

●       E-04: Template Rate Limits Hit. Meta's messaging tier limits are reached for the day. RESOLUTION: Queue remaining re-engagement messages for the next available sending window and log the deferral.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-01

Message sent inside 24h window

Free-form reply delivered normally.

TC-02

Re-engagement after window closes

Approved template used, not free-form text.

TC-03

User replies to template

Window reopens, free-form chat resumes.

TC-04

Daily tier limit reached

Excess messages queued for next window.

 

WAP-US-03: Recycled / Reassigned Phone Number Handling

STATUS: Proposed   PRIORITY: Medium   ACTOR: Learner / Casual User

Intent: To prevent a new owner of a previously-used phone number from inheriting the prior owner's linked Speeky-AI account, streaks, and conversation history — a known risk in markets with frequent SIM recycling.

Happy Path Steps

1. New Message: An unrecognized-behavior message arrives from a number that is on file as linked to an existing account.

2. Anomaly Check: System checks for a break in usage pattern (e.g., long dormancy, different linguistic/voice signature) before assuming continuity.

3. Re-Verification Prompt: If anomaly is detected, bot asks a light identity check (e.g., "Is this still [name]? Reply YES or relink your account.").

4. Confirmation: User confirms identity or is routed to the account-linking flow (GAP-01) as a new user.

Acceptance Criteria

●       System must not silently expose a prior user's practice history/streak/name to a new speaker on a recycled number.

●       Anomaly detection must trigger a re-verification prompt rather than blocking the number outright.

Exception Handling

●       E-01: False Positive Anomaly Detection. The original user simply changed devices or speaking context. RESOLUTION: Allow a simple "YES, it's me" confirmation to resume normal access without re-linking.

●       E-02: Confirmed New Owner. The number's new holder confirms they are not the original user. RESOLUTION: Unlink the number from the old account, purge cached personal greeting/name for that number, and offer fresh onboarding.

●       E-03: No Response to Verification Prompt. User ignores the identity check for 48+ hours. RESOLUTION: Default to treating the number as unverified; withhold personal data (name, streak) until confirmed.

●       E-04: Dormancy Threshold Not Met. Number has been inactive less than the anomaly threshold (e.g., 2 weeks). RESOLUTION: Skip the re-verification step and resume normal continuity, since short gaps are expected.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-01

Long-dormant number resumes activity

Identity check prompt sent before resuming continuity.

TC-02

Original user confirms identity

Normal access resumes, no data loss.

TC-03

New owner denies identity

Number unlinked, old data purged from that number's context.

TC-04

Short dormancy gap

No verification prompt triggered.

 

WAP-US-04: Conversation Context Continuity & Session Timeout

STATUS: Proposed   PRIORITY: Medium   ACTOR: Learner / Casual User

Intent: To maintain coherent conversational context across a user's WhatsApp exchange, and to gracefully reset context after a natural break, so replies don't reference a stale topic from hours or days earlier.

Happy Path Steps

1. Active Exchange: User and bot exchange several messages on a topic within a short time span.

2. Context Retention: System retains the topic/thread state for follow-up replies within the active session.

3. Idle Detection: System detects no reply from the user for a defined idle period (e.g., 30+ minutes).

4. Session Reset: On the next user message, bot treats it as a fresh topic rather than forcing continuity with the stale thread.

Acceptance Criteria

●       System must define and apply a consistent idle threshold for resetting conversational context.

●       Bot must not reference a topic from a prior, clearly-closed session as if it were still active.

Exception Handling

●       E-01: User Resumes Old Topic Explicitly. User's new message directly references the earlier topic (e.g., "like I said about my trip"). RESOLUTION: Attempt topic re-identification from message content rather than rigidly forcing a reset.

●       E-02: Mid-Message Idle Timeout. User starts replying, pauses over 30 minutes, then sends a second fragment of the same thought. RESOLUTION: Treat the fragments as a fresh message rather than silently concatenating them, and ask a lightweight clarifying question if needed.

●       E-03: Multiple Rapid Topic Switches. User jumps between unrelated topics within one active session. RESOLUTION: Track the most recent topic only; do not attempt to interleave multiple simultaneous threads.

●       E-04: Idle Timeout Coincides with 24h Window Expiry. Session reset and the WhatsApp messaging window (GAP-02) close at the same time. RESOLUTION: Apply the template-message rule from GAP-02 for the first message back, using generic re-engagement copy rather than stale context.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-01

Rapid back-and-forth exchange

Context retained correctly across replies.

TC-02

30+ minute idle gap then new message

Bot starts a fresh topic, no stale reference.

TC-03

User explicitly references old topic

Bot re-identifies and responds coherently.

TC-04

Idle reset overlaps window expiry

Template-based re-engagement used correctly.

 

WAP-US-05: Unsolicited Addition of Bot to Group Chats

STATUS: Proposed   PRIORITY: Medium   ACTOR: Learner / Casual User / Group Member

Intent: To handle cases where the Speeky-AI WhatsApp number is added directly into a group chat (as opposed to a 1:1 referral flow in WAP-US-11), preventing unwanted behavior, privacy leakage, or spam within the group.

Happy Path Steps

1. Group Add Event: Speeky-AI bot number is added to a WhatsApp group by any member.

2. Passive Detection: System detects the group-add event via the WhatsApp Business API.

3. Opt-In Prompt: Bot sends a single introductory message to the group explaining it only responds to direct/tagged messages, with an option for an admin to remove it.

4. Passive Mode: Bot remains silent in the group unless explicitly tagged or messaged directly by a member.

Acceptance Criteria

●       Bot must never proactively broadcast a user's personal practice data (scores, streaks) inside a group context.

●       Bot must not respond to general group chatter unless directly addressed.

Exception Handling

●       E-01: Bot Tagged in Group. A member @-mentions the bot with a question. RESOLUTION: Respond only to that specific message, without surfacing any other member's personal data.

●       E-02: Repeated Unwanted Group Adds. The bot is added, removed, and re-added repeatedly (spam/harassment pattern). RESOLUTION: Rate-limit re-joining behavior and flag the group for review after repeated cycles.

●       E-03: Group Exceeds Business API Group Limits. WhatsApp Business API restrictions prevent normal bot participation in large groups. RESOLUTION: Bot sends a message noting it cannot function in this group size/type and exits gracefully.

●       E-04: Admin Requests Full Removal. A group admin explicitly asks the bot to leave. RESOLUTION: Bot exits the group and does not retain that group's conversation content beyond standard retention policy.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-01

Bot added to a group

Sends one intro message, then stays passive.

TC-02

Bot tagged with a question

Responds only to that message, no other data exposed.

TC-03

Admin asks bot to leave

Bot exits, no further group interaction.

TC-04

Repeated add/remove cycling

Rejoin behavior rate-limited, group flagged.

 

WAP-US-06: Roman Urdu / Non-English Input Handling

STATUS: Proposed   PRIORITY: High   ACTOR: Learner / Casual User

Intent: To gracefully handle users who message the bot in Roman Urdu, Urdu script, or mixed-language text/voice, since the target market (Pakistan) commonly code-switches, and the bot's core purpose is English coaching.

Happy Path Steps

1. Input Received: User sends a message or Voice Note substantially in Roman Urdu or Urdu script rather than English.

2. Language Detection: System detects the input is not primarily English.

3. Gentle Redirect: Bot acknowledges the message content where possible and gently encourages an English attempt, offering a simplified prompt.

4. Continued Engagement: User responds in English (even imperfectly), and normal practice flow resumes.

Acceptance Criteria

●       System must detect non-English input with reasonable accuracy for both text and transcribed voice notes.

●       Bot must never simply reject or ignore non-English input; it must respond with an encouraging, English-practice-oriented redirect.

Exception Handling

●       E-01: Fully Urdu-Script Message. User writes entirely in Urdu script (not Roman Urdu). RESOLUTION: Bot replies in simple English with an invitation to try again in English, avoiding a flat error message.

●       E-02: Mixed-Language Voice Note. User's Voice Note code-switches between Urdu and English mid-sentence. RESOLUTION: Score and respond to the English portions; do not penalize the Urdu portions as pronunciation errors.

●       E-03: User Persists in Urdu Repeatedly. User continues in Urdu across 3+ consecutive messages despite redirects. RESOLUTION: Reduce redirect frequency and offer a lighter bilingual prompt option rather than repeatedly blocking engagement.

●       E-04: Language Detection Failure. System cannot confidently classify the input language. RESOLUTION: Default to a neutral, language-agnostic encouraging reply rather than guessing incorrectly.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-01

Roman Urdu text sent

Bot detects, encourages English attempt.

TC-02

Urdu-script message sent

Bot replies in simple English, invites retry.

TC-03

Mixed Urdu/English voice note

Only English portion scored, Urdu portion ignored.

TC-04

Repeated Urdu across sessions

Redirect frequency reduced, bilingual option offered.

 

WAP-US-07: Concurrent Message / Race Condition Handling

STATUS: Proposed   PRIORITY: Medium   ACTOR: Learner / Casual User

Intent: To handle cases where a user sends a new message while a prior Voice Note is still being processed, preventing out-of-order replies, duplicate processing, or dropped messages.

Happy Path Steps

1. First Message: User sends a Voice Note; system begins processing.

2. Second Message Arrives: User sends a follow-up text message before processing of the first completes.

3. Queueing: System queues the second message and finishes processing the first in order.

4. Sequential Reply: Bot replies to both messages in the order received, clearly referencing each.

Acceptance Criteria

●       System must process a given user's messages in strict received order; no message may be silently dropped.

●       Bot must not blend two unrelated inputs into a single confused reply.

Exception Handling

●       E-01: Second Message Supersedes First. User sends a correction (e.g., "ignore that, here's my real answer") while the first is still processing. RESOLUTION: Detect override language where possible and prioritize the correction; otherwise process both and let the user clarify.

●       E-02: Processing Backlog Builds Up. User sends 5+ messages faster than the bot can process them. RESOLUTION: Apply the existing rate-limiting behavior (WAP-US-10 E-03) and inform the user replies are catching up.

●       E-03: First Message Processing Fails. The queued first Voice Note fails transcription mid-way. RESOLUTION: Skip to the next queued message, notify the user the earlier note failed and ask them to resend it.

●       E-04: Duplicate Message Sent (Network Retry). WhatsApp client retries delivery, sending the same message twice. RESOLUTION: De-duplicate via WhatsApp's message ID before processing, so it is only answered once.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-01

Voice note + quick text follow-up

Both processed in order, no dropped message.

TC-02

5 rapid messages sent

Rate limit applied, catch-up message shown.

TC-03

First voice note fails mid-processing

User notified, asked to resend, queue continues.

TC-04

Duplicate message ID received

Only processed once.

 

WAP-US-08: WhatsApp Business API Outage / Service Degradation Fallback

STATUS: Proposed   PRIORITY: Medium   ACTOR: Learner / Casual User

Intent: To handle periods when the WhatsApp Business API (Meta infrastructure) is degraded or unavailable, so users aren't left with silent failures and streaks/practice logging aren't corrupted.

Happy Path Steps

1. Outage Detection: System's monitoring detects elevated error rates or downtime from the WhatsApp Business API.

2. Internal Alerting: Engineering/on-call is notified automatically.

3. Graceful Degradation: Any messages that do get through receive a short apology/status note if replies are delayed.

4. Recovery Sync: Once the API recovers, queued inbound messages are processed and streak/practice data is reconciled without duplication.

Acceptance Criteria

●       System must never silently lose an inbound message during an outage; it must be queued for retry once service resumes.

●       Daily Streak logic (WAP-US-12) must not penalize a user for a missed day caused by a confirmed platform-side outage.

Exception Handling

●       E-01: Partial Outage (Some Messages Delivered). Only a subset of regions/numbers are affected. RESOLUTION: Apply fallback handling only to affected traffic; unaffected users continue normally.

●       E-02: Extended Outage Spans a Streak Deadline. Outage lasts through a user's daily streak cutoff. RESOLUTION: Automatically grant a streak grace day for affected users rather than breaking their streak.

●       E-03: Message Lost Despite Queueing (Meta-Side Failure). A message is acknowledged by Meta but never delivered to Speeky-AI's webhook. RESOLUTION: Rely on WhatsApp's own delivery-retry guarantees where possible; if data is unrecoverable, notify the user to resend once service is confirmed restored.

●       E-04: Users Attempt Contact via Alternate Channel During Outage. Users try the native app instead during a WhatsApp outage. RESOLUTION: Ensure native app functions independently and is unaffected by the WhatsApp-specific outage.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-01

Simulated full API outage

Messages queued, no silent loss, alert triggered.

TC-02

Outage spans streak deadline

Affected users granted automatic grace day.

TC-03

Partial regional outage

Only affected traffic falls back; others unaffected.

TC-04

Recovery after outage

Queued messages processed without duplication.

 

WAP-US-09: Opt-Out, Block & Re-Engagement Compliance

STATUS: Proposed   PRIORITY: Medium   ACTOR: Learner / Casual User

Intent: To respect user opt-outs and blocks, and to comply with WhatsApp policy around not attempting to circumvent a block or spam a user who has requested to stop receiving messages.

Happy Path Steps

1. Opt-Out Request: User sends a message like "stop" or "unsubscribe," or blocks the bot number.

2. Immediate Compliance: System immediately halts all proactive/template messages (daily challenge nudges, referral notifications) to that number.

3. Confirmation: If the user texted "stop" (not a hard block), bot sends one final confirmation message and then goes silent.

4. Re-Opt-In Path: If the user later messages the bot again voluntarily, proactive messaging resumes.

Acceptance Criteria

●       System must maintain a persistent opt-out list checked before every proactive/template send.

●       A hard block (detected via delivery failure) must be treated identically to an explicit opt-out for suppression purposes.

Exception Handling

●       E-01: User Blocks Without Explicit "Stop" Message. Delivery failures indicate a block rather than a stated request. RESOLUTION: Treat as an implicit opt-out; suppress all further template sends immediately, log for internal analytics only.

●       E-02: User Re-Engages After Opting Out. A previously opted-out user sends a new message voluntarily. RESOLUTION: Resume normal service and, if desired, re-confirm consent for future proactive nudges.

●       E-03: Accidental Opt-Out. User sends "stop" during casual conversation, not intending to unsubscribe. RESOLUTION: Send one clarifying confirmation before fully suppressing ("You've been unsubscribed from reminders — reply START anytime to turn them back on").

●       E-04: Opt-Out on Linked Account Affects Referrer. An opted-out user was also a referral source (WAP-US-11). RESOLUTION: Referral tracking/credit continues to function independently of messaging opt-out status.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-01

User texts "stop"

Confirmation sent, all future template sends suppressed.

TC-02

Delivery failure indicates block

Treated as opt-out, sends suppressed silently.

TC-03

Opted-out user re-engages

Normal service resumes.

TC-04

Opted-out referrer still gets referral credit

Referral credit unaffected by messaging suppression.

 















WAP-US-10: WhatsApp-Based Practice Mode

STATUS: In Development PRIORITY: Medium ACTOR: Learner / Casual User

Intent: To practice conversational English directly over WhatsApp without needing to download the full app, lowering the barrier to entry.

Happy Path Steps

Initiation: User sends a WhatsApp message (text or Voice Note) to the Speeky-AI business number.

Context Setting: AI responds with a casual, lightweight topic prompt.

Interaction: User replies via a WhatsApp Voice Note.

Feedback: AI processes the audio, replies contextually to keep the chat going, and offers brief, lightweight feedback on their response.

Acceptance Criteria

Must support both WhatsApp Text and Voice Note (audio) payloads.

AI responses must be formatted for chat (short, concise, utilizing standard emojis).

Must function entirely without requiring the user to authenticate into the web or native app first.

Exception Handling

E-01: Unsupported Media Upload. User sends an image or video instead of text/audio. RESOLUTION: AI replies: "I can only process text and voice notes right now. Send me a voice note to practice!"

E-02: Audio Exceeds Limits. User sends a 10-minute Voice Note. RESOLUTION: System truncates processing at the 2-minute mark and replies: "That was a lot of great detail! For this chat, let's try to keep responses under 2 minutes."

E-03: Spam/Rate Limiting. User spams the bot with 50 messages in one minute. RESOLUTION: Implement WhatsApp API rate limiting; bot pauses responses and sends a cooldown message.

E-04: WhatsApp API Timeout. The LLM takes too long to process the Voice Note. RESOLUTION: Bot instantly sends a "Typing/Processing..." status to manage user expectations while generating the response.

WAP-US-11: WhatsApp Mode - Viral Sharing & Acquisition

STATUS: In Development PRIORITY: High ACTOR: Learner / Casual User

Intent: To share a practice session result or invite a friend directly via WhatsApp, driving organic acquisition and leveraging local market behavior.

Happy Path Steps

Completion: User completes a Daily Challenge or WhatsApp-based practice session.

Prompt: The bot sends a dynamic image/card of their Confidence Score and a call-to-action: "Challenge a friend to beat your score!"

Share Action: User forwards the message (which includes a unique referral link) to a WhatsApp contact or group.

Onboarding: The receiving friend clicks the link, which instantly opens a chat with the Speeky-AI WhatsApp bot, bypassing an app download.

Reward: Original user receives a notification acknowledging the successful referral.

Acceptance Criteria

The shareable artifact must be an image/card (not just text) to increase visual engagement.

Referral links must append a unique tracking ID to attribute the acquisition to the original user.

Exception Handling

E-01: Referral Link Expiration. A user clicks a referral link that is older than 30 days. RESOLUTION: Link redirects to the standard Speeky-AI bot greeting rather than a specific challenge match.

E-02: Self-Referral Attempt. User attempts to click their own referral link to farm rewards. RESOLUTION: System detects matching phone numbers/device IDs and ignores the referral trigger.

E-03: Bot Blocked by Recipient. The referred user clicks the link but has previously blocked the Speeky-AI business number. RESOLUTION: WhatsApp natively prevents the message; system logs a "Failed Delivery" for the referral attempt.

E-04: API Rate Limiting on Viral Share. A user shares the link in a massive group, causing 500 simultaneous clicks. RESOLUTION: WhatsApp bot queues the incoming requests and delays onboarding messages by 1-2 seconds to prevent API suspension.

Acceptance Criteria

Practice sessions conducted on WhatsApp must count identically to sessions completed in the native app.

Exception Handling

E-01: Unlinked Phone Number. User messages the bot from a new number not associated with an account. RESOLUTION: Bot replies: "I don't recognize this number! Reply with your Speeky-AI email to link your account, or let's just chat for fun!"

E-02: Audio > 5 Minutes Sent. User sends a massive 10-minute Voice Note. RESOLUTION: Bot truncates processing at the maximum context limit (e.g., 2 minutes) to save API costs and replies: "That's a lot of detail! I listened to the first two minutes..."

E-03: Bot API Timeout. The LLM backend takes >15 seconds to process the voice note. RESOLUTION: Bot sends a standard WhatsApp "Typing..." indicator or a quick text: "Listening to your answer..." to manage user expectations.

E-04: Non-Text/Audio Media. User sends a sticker or a PDF. RESOLUTION: Bot gracefully handles the error: "I can only understand text and voice messages right now!"

PDG-US-01: Streak Freeze / Vacation Mode

STATUS: Proposed   PRIORITY: High   ACTOR: Learner

Intent: To let a user protect an earned streak during a planned absence (travel, illness, exams) using a limited number of "freeze" tokens, rather than losing weeks of progress to one missed day.

Happy Path Steps

1. Settings Access: User navigates to Streak settings and sees their available Streak Freeze tokens (e.g., earned 1 per 7-day milestone).

2. Activation: User activates a freeze before a day they expect to miss, or the system auto-applies one retroactively when a miss is detected.

3. Day Protection: On the missed day, the system consumes one freeze token and preserves the streak count instead of resetting it.

4. Confirmation: Dashboard shows a small "frozen" icon on that calendar day, distinct from a completed day.

Acceptance Criteria

●       Freeze tokens must be finite and earned (e.g., tied to milestones), not unlimited, to preserve habit-forming intent.

●       A frozen day must be visually distinguishable from a genuinely completed practice day on the streak calendar.

Exception Handling

●       E-01: No Freeze Tokens Available. User misses a day with zero tokens in reserve. RESOLUTION: Streak resets as normal, but system offers a one-time "Watch a tip / complete a 2-minute makeup drill" option to partially restore it, capped to once per month.

●       E-02: Multiple Consecutive Missed Days. User misses 3 days in a row with only 1 token available. RESOLUTION: Apply the single token to the first missed day only; streak breaks on the second missed day as normal.

●       E-03: Freeze Activated but User Actually Practices. User pre-activates a freeze then completes the Daily Challenge anyway. RESOLUTION: Refund the unused freeze token back to the user's balance.

●       E-04: Freeze Token Expiry. Tokens are earned but go unused for 6+ months. RESOLUTION: Tokens do not expire; system avoids punitive expiry to keep the mechanic goodwill-oriented.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-01

Activate freeze before missed day

Streak preserved, token consumed, frozen icon shown.

TC-02

Miss a day with zero tokens

Streak resets, makeup-drill offer shown once.

TC-03

Freeze active but user practices anyway

Token refunded to balance.

TC-04

3 missed days, 1 token available

Only first day protected, streak breaks after.

 

PDG-US-02: Confidence Score Methodology Transparency & Dispute

STATUS: Proposed   PRIORITY: Medium   ACTOR: Learner

Intent: To let users understand how the top-line Confidence Score (PDG-US-10) is calculated and flag a specific session's contribution to it if it seems wrong, building trust in the platform's central metric.

Happy Path Steps

1. Info Access: User taps an info icon next to the Confidence Score on the dashboard.

2. Explanation: System displays a plain-language breakdown of contributing factors (fluency, vocabulary use, pronunciation, session consistency).

3. Session Drill-down: User can tap into a specific past session to see its individual contribution to the current score.

4. Dispute Option: If a specific session's score looks wrong, user can flag it for review.

Acceptance Criteria

●       The Confidence Score explanation must list all contributing sub-metrics in plain language, not just a single number.

●       Flagging a session for review must not immediately alter the score; it must route to a review process.

Exception Handling

●       E-01: Session Flagged as Inaccurate. User disputes a specific session's contribution. RESOLUTION: Log the dispute with the session ID for review; notify the user once resolved, consistent with a standard score-dispute flow.

●       E-02: Score Drops After a Strong Session. User feels their score should have risen but it fell. RESOLUTION: Explanation panel highlights which specific sub-metric dropped and why (e.g., "Vocabulary variety was lower than your recent average").

●       E-03: Insufficient Data for Explanation. User has completed only 1 session, too little to break down meaningfully. RESOLUTION: Display: "We need a few more sessions to show your full score breakdown" rather than an empty or misleading chart.

●       E-04: Repeated Disputes Across Many Sessions. User disputes several sessions in a short time. RESOLUTION: Rate-limit disputes per day (mirrors dispute-abuse handling in other modules) and surface remaining allowance.

Validation Test Cases

TC-02

TC-03

Flag a session as inaccurate

Dispute logged, user notified once reviewed.

New user with 1 session

Intent: To let users see the complete set of achievable badges (streaks, practice-time milestones, vocabulary milestones) — including locked ones — so they have visible long-term goals beyond the next single milestone.

Happy Path Steps

1. Navigation: User taps "Trophy Case" (referenced in PDG-US-15) from the dashboard.

2. Catalog Display: System shows all badges across categories (Streaks, Practice Time, Vocabulary, Special Events), each marked Earned or Locked.

3. Locked Preview: Locked badges show a silhouette/greyed icon with the requirement needed to unlock (e.g., "Reach a 30-day streak").

4. Progress Indicator: Each locked badge shows current progress toward it (e.g., "18/30 days").

Acceptance Criteria

●       All defined badge types across every gamification mechanic (streaks, practice time, vocabulary) must appear in a single unified catalog view.

●       Locked badges must show the specific unlock requirement, not just a generic "locked" label.

Exception Handling

●       E-01: New Badge Type Added Post-Launch. Product team introduces a new badge category after users already have history. RESOLUTION: Retroactively evaluate existing user data against the new badge's criteria and auto-award if already qualified, with a "newly unlocked" notice.

●       E-02: Badge Requirement Changed. A milestone threshold is adjusted (e.g., 50 hours badge changed to 40 hours). RESOLUTION: Grandfather users already past the old threshold; do not revoke previously earned badges.

●       E-03: Catalog Load Failure. Badge metadata fails to load from the backend. RESOLUTION: Show cached last-known badge state with a subtle sync warning, consistent with dashboard sync-failure handling (PDG-US-10 E-01).

●       E-04: Duplicate Badge Award Attempt. A sync glitch tries to award the same badge twice. RESOLUTION: System enforces badge uniqueness per user per badge ID; duplicate award attempts are silently ignored.

Exception Handling

●       E-02: Export Generation Failure. PDF rendering fails server-side. RESOLUTION: Notify the user the export failed and offer a retry, without losing their selected range/settings.

●       E-03: Large Data Range Causes Timeout. User selects "All Time" after 2+ years of daily use. RESOLUTION: Generate a summarized/aggregated version (monthly rollups) rather than every individual session, to keep the report readable and generation fast.

●       E-04: Sensitive Data in Shared Report. User shares the report externally. RESOLUTION: Exclude raw audio/voice data and any account credentials from the export; include only aggregate scores and badges.

PDG-US-05: Streak Restore Appeal (Manual Support Correction)

STATUS: Proposed   PRIORITY: Low   ACTOR: Learner

Intent: To give users a path to request manual restoration of a streak broken due to a confirmed platform-side error (e.g., sync bug, outage), separate from the automatic timezone/UTC handling already in place (PDG-US-10 E-04, PDG-US-13 E-02).

Happy Path Steps

1. Detection: User notices their streak broke despite believing they completed the Daily Challenge.

2. Appeal Request: User taps "Report an Issue" next to their streak counter and submits a short description.

3. Internal Review: Support/automated system checks server logs for evidence of a completed-but-unsynced session around the relevant time.

4. Resolution: If confirmed, streak is manually restored and the user is notified; if not, a clear explanation is given.

Acceptance Criteria

●       Appeal submission must capture the approximate date/time of the disputed break to speed up log lookup.

●       System must never auto-restore a streak without server-side evidence of a genuinely completed session.

Exception Handling

●       E-01: No Server Evidence Found. Logs show no completed session around the claimed time. RESOLUTION: Politely decline the restoration with an explanation, and suggest starting a fresh streak.

●       E-02: Evidence Found (Confirmed Platform Bug). Logs confirm a completed session that failed to sync. RESOLUTION: Restore the streak and back-fill the missing day, and log the sync bug for engineering follow-up.

●       E-03: Repeated Appeals from Same User. User submits 5+ restoration appeals in a month. RESOLUTION: Flag account for manual review to distinguish recurring platform issues from attempted abuse.

●       E-04: Appeal Submitted Long After the Fact. User appeals a streak break from 3 months ago. RESOLUTION: Apply a reasonable appeal window (e.g., 14 days) beyond which logs may have rolled off; inform user of the window.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-01

Appeal with confirmed sync bug

Streak restored, missing day back-filled.

TC-02

Appeal with no supporting evidence

Appeal declined with explanation.

TC-03

Appeal submitted after 14-day window

User informed the window has passed.

TC-04

5+ appeals in a month

Account flagged for manual review.

 

PDG-US-06: Historical Data Retention & Long-Range Chart Performance

STATUS: Proposed   PRIORITY: Low   ACTOR: Learner

Intent: To keep dashboard trend charts (PDG-US-10, PDG-US-14) fast and readable for long-tenured users with years of daily session history, mirroring the pagination approach already used for the Vocabulary word list (PDG-US-12 E-04).

Happy Path Steps

1. Long History: A user with 2+ years of daily sessions opens their Progress Dashboard.

2. Range Selector: User selects a time range (Week, Month, Year, All Time) for the trend chart.

3. Aggregation: For longer ranges, the system automatically aggregates data points (e.g., weekly averages for "Year", monthly averages for "All Time") instead of plotting every single session.

4. Render: Chart renders smoothly regardless of underlying data volume.

Acceptance Criteria

●       Chart rendering time must remain consistent regardless of total historical session count.

●       Aggregation level must be clearly labeled on the chart (e.g., "Weekly Average") so users don't mistake it for per-session data.

Exception Handling

●       E-01: User Wants Per-Session Detail on a Long Range. User wants to drill into a specific day within an aggregated "Year" view. RESOLUTION: Allow tapping an aggregated data point to expand into the underlying daily sessions for that period.

●       E-02: Data Gaps in Long History. User had a multi-month gap in usage within their "All Time" view. RESOLUTION: Render the gap as a flat/empty segment on the chart rather than interpolating a misleading trend line across it.

●       E-03: Aggregation Causes Outlier Masking. A single exceptional session gets averaged away in a monthly rollup. RESOLUTION: Preserve and separately mark true outlier peaks (best single session) even within aggregated views.

●       E-04: Export Conflicts with Aggregation. Report Export (GAP-04) requests full granularity from an aggregated range. RESOLUTION: Export pulls raw underlying data regardless of the dashboard's current display aggregation level.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-01

Open dashboard with 2+ years history

Chart renders quickly with clear aggregation label.

TC-02

Tap an aggregated data point

Expands to show underlying daily sessions.

TC-03

Multi-month gap in history

Chart shows flat/empty segment, not a misleading interpolation.

TC-04

Export during aggregated view

Export contains full raw data, not the aggregated view.

 

PDG-US-07: Anti-Gaming Detection for Daily Challenge Completion

STATUS: Proposed   PRIORITY: High   ACTOR: Learner

Intent: To detect when a user is technically meeting the Daily Challenge's time/turn requirement (PDG-US-11) without genuine engagement — e.g., filler noise, repeated single words, or silence padded with background audio — protecting the integrity of streaks and Confidence Score.

Happy Path Steps

1. Session Monitoring: During the 5-minute session, system continuously evaluates speech content quality, not just duration/turn count.

2. Genuine Engagement Check: AI confirms the audio contains substantive, varied conversational content meeting a minimum quality bar.

3. Qualification: If content quality bar is met alongside duration/turns, the streak increments normally.

4. Low-Quality Flag: If duration is met but content quality is clearly filler, system does not increment the streak.

Acceptance Criteria

●       Streak increment must require both minimum duration/turns (existing) AND a minimum content-quality signal (new).

●       The quality bar must be lenient enough not to penalize genuine beginners struggling with fluency.

Exception Handling

●       E-01: Genuine Beginner Struggles Naturally. A real learner speaks slowly with pauses and simple vocabulary. RESOLUTION: Quality bar must be calibrated to accept halting-but-genuine speech; only flag clear filler/repetition patterns, not low skill level.

●       E-02: Repeated Filler Words/Noise Detected. User repeats the same word or hums to pad time. RESOLUTION: Session logs as "Incomplete — Low Engagement" and streak does not increment; user is shown a supportive nudge to try again, not a punitive message.

●       E-03: False Positive on Quality Check. A legitimate but very short, simple response is misflagged as filler. RESOLUTION: Allow the user to flag the session for review (ties to GAP-02 dispute pattern); if confirmed genuine, streak is retroactively credited.

●       E-04: Background TV/Media Used as Filler. User plays a video/podcast near the mic to simulate conversation. RESOLUTION: Voice-isolation and speaker-consistency checks detect non-interactive audio patterns and reject the session.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-01

Genuine halting beginner speech

Session qualifies, streak increments normally.

TC-02

Repeated filler word padding

Session marked low-engagement, streak withheld.

TC-03

False positive disputed by user

Review confirms genuine effort, streak retroactively credited.

TC-04

Background media used as filler

Session rejected as non-interactive audio.

 

PDG-US-08: Notification Frequency Controls & Quiet Hours

STATUS: Proposed   PRIORITY: Medium   ACTOR: Learner

Intent: To let users control how often and when they receive gamification-related push notifications (streak reminders, milestone celebrations), preventing notification fatigue from an otherwise well-intentioned engagement engine (PDG-US-13).

Happy Path Steps

1. Settings Access: User navigates to Notification Preferences.

2. Quiet Hours: User sets a do-not-disturb window (e.g., 10 PM – 8 AM local time).

3. Frequency Choice: User selects a reminder cadence (e.g., "Only if I haven't practiced by 6 PM" vs "Off entirely").

4. Respect: System honors these preferences for all future streak/milestone notifications.

Acceptance Criteria

●       Quiet hours must apply across all gamification notification types, not just the daily streak reminder.

●       Turning reminders off must not affect the user's ability to earn streaks/badges — only the proactive nudges are disabled.

Exception Handling

●       E-01: Quiet Hours Span Midnight. User sets quiet hours from 10 PM to 8 AM, crossing the day boundary. RESOLUTION: System correctly handles the overnight range without misfiring notifications inside the window.

●       E-02: User Disables All Reminders Then Loses Streak. User with reminders off breaks a long streak without warning. RESOLUTION: On streak break, show an in-app (not push) summary next open explaining the miss, since proactive nudging was explicitly declined.

●       E-03: Milestone Reached During Quiet Hours. User crosses a badge milestone at 11 PM within their quiet window. RESOLUTION: Defer the celebratory push to the start of the next allowed window, but still display the in-app celebration immediately if the user is actively in the session.

●       E-04: Conflicting Preferences Across Devices. User sets different quiet hours on phone vs web. RESOLUTION: Sync preferences at the account level so the most recently set preference applies across all devices.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-01

Set overnight quiet hours

No notifications fire during the window.

TC-02

Reminders off, streak breaks

In-app summary shown next open, no push sent.

TC-03

Milestone hit during quiet hours

Push deferred to next window; in-app celebration still shows live.

TC-04

Different settings on two devices

Most recent preference applies account-wide.

 

PDG-US-09: Healthy Engagement Safeguard (Overuse Nudge)

STATUS: Proposed   PRIORITY: Low   ACTOR: Learner

Intent: To gently flag unusually excessive usage patterns (e.g., many hours of back-to-back sessions in one sitting) and encourage a healthy practice rhythm, rather than the gamification system inadvertently reinforcing compulsive use.

Happy Path Steps

1. Usage Monitoring: System tracks continuous session time within a single sitting.

2. Threshold Reached: User crosses a high continuous-use threshold (e.g., 2+ hours without a break).

3. Gentle Nudge: App displays a friendly, non-blocking message suggesting a short break, without shaming or restricting access.

4. Continued Choice: User can dismiss the nudge and continue practicing if they choose.

Acceptance Criteria

●       The nudge must be non-blocking and dismissible; the system must never lock a user out of practicing.

●       Nudge copy must be neutral and encouraging, never framed as a penalty or warning.

Exception Handling

●       E-01: User Dismisses and Continues Well Past Threshold. User keeps practicing for 4+ hours after dismissing the nudge. RESOLUTION: Show at most one follow-up nudge after a further extended interval; do not repeatedly interrupt the session.

●       E-02: Legitimate Extended Study Session. A user is intentionally doing a long prep session ahead of an interview. RESOLUTION: Nudge remains purely informational and dismiss-and-continue must always be a single tap, respecting user autonomy.

●       E-03: Threshold Reached via Multiple Short Sessions. User completes several short sessions that sum to a high daily total but no single long sitting. RESOLUTION: Do not trigger the continuous-use nudge for this pattern; it targets unbroken sitting duration, not total daily practice.

●       E-04: Nudge Coincides with Milestone Celebration. A practice-time milestone is crossed at the same moment the overuse threshold is hit. RESOLUTION: Show the milestone celebration first; present the wellbeing nudge as a separate, secondary message afterward.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-01

Continuous 2+ hour session

Non-blocking break nudge shown.

TC-02

Nudge dismissed, session continues

At most one follow-up nudge shown later, no lockout.

TC-03

Several short sessions, high daily total

No continuous-use nudge triggered.

TC-04

Milestone and overuse threshold coincide

Milestone celebration shown first, nudge shown separately after.

PDG-US-11: Daily Challenge & Streak Gamification

STATUS: In Development PRIORITY: High ACTOR: Learner

Intent: To complete a 5-minute daily conversation to build a consistent practice habit and earn milestone rewards.

Happy Path Steps

Prompt: User opens the app and is greeted with the "Daily Challenge" prompt.

Engagement: User initiates a 5-minute casual conversation session.

Completion: System logs the completion of the 5-minute requirement.

Reward: System updates the user's daily streak counter and displays a shareable progress card/badge showing their confidence score growth.

Acceptance Criteria

Session must last exactly 5 minutes (or user must engage in a minimum number of conversational turns) to qualify.

Streak must increment by 1 upon successful completion.

System must award milestone badges at 7-day and 30-day intervals.

Exception Handling

E-02: Timezone Boundary Crossing. User starts the challenge at 11:58 PM and finishes at 12:03 AM. RESOLUTION: System honors the start time of the session and applies the streak to the previous day.

E-03: Multiple Completions in One Day. User attempts to do the Daily Challenge three times to boost their streak. RESOLUTION: Cap streak increment at +1 per calendar day; additional sessions log as standard practice time without incrementing the streak multiplier.

E-04: Network Failure on Completion. App fails to log the completion event to the server. RESOLUTION: Cache the completion timestamp locally and sync to update the streak upon the next active connection.

PDG-US-13: Daily Challenge Push Notification Engine

STATUS: In Development PRIORITY: High ACTOR: System / Learner

Intent: To automatically remind users to complete their 5-minute Daily Challenge, maximizing daily active users (DAU) and preserving engagement streaks.

Happy Path Steps

Trigger Condition: User has not opened the app by 6:00 PM local time.

Execution: System dispatches a localized push notification (e.g., "Don't lose your 4-day streak! 5 minutes of practice is all it takes.").

Action: User taps the notification.

Routing: App opens and deep-links the user directly into the "Daily Challenge" initiation screen.

Completion: User finishes the challenge and the streak increments safely.

Acceptance Criteria

Notifications must respect the user's local timezone.

The push copy must dynamically inject the user's current streak number for personalization.

Exception Handling

E-01: Notifications Disabled at OS Level. User has blocked Speeky-AI from sending push notifications. RESOLUTION: System detects the blocked permission and falls back to a visually prominent "Streak Warning" banner upon the user's next organic app launch.

E-02: Timezone Change Mid-Day. User travels across the world, jumping ahead 12 hours. RESOLUTION: Notification engine uses UTC anchoring to calculate the 24-hour cycle, preventing premature "Streak Lost" alerts.

E-03: Already Completed. User completes the challenge at 5:45 PM, but the 6:00 PM batch notification is already queued. RESOLUTION: Pre-dispatch validation checks the database at 5:59 PM and drops the notification if the user's daily status is "Complete".

E-04: Multi-Device Sync. User completes the challenge on their iPad, but their iPhone is scheduled to receive the push. RESOLUTION: Cross-device state syncing ensures the iPhone push is cancelled upon iPad completion.

Validation Test Cases

Expected Result

 TC-0 05

PDG-US-15: Progress Dashboard - Practice Time Milestones

STATUS: In Development PRIORITY: Low ACTOR: Learner

Intent: To track total cumulative "Practice Time" and unlock visual milestone badges to maintain long-term motivation beyond just daily streaks.

Happy Path Steps

Completion: User completes a 5-minute Scenario-Based Learning session.

Data Sync: The backend adds the 5 minutes to the user's lifetime total practice time.

Milestone Trigger: The user's total time crosses a threshold (e.g., 10 hours of speaking).

Celebration UI: A full-screen celebration modal appears: "You've spoken English for 10 Hours!"

Dashboard Update: The new milestone badge is permanently added to the user's Progress Dashboard "Trophy Case".

Acceptance Criteria

Time tracking must only count active speaking/chatting time, not idle time spent navigating menus.

Milestones should be spaced logarithmically (e.g., 1 hour, 5 hours, 10 hours, 50 hours) to keep goals achievable.

Exception Handling

E-01: App Crash Mid-Session. User is 4 minutes into a session when their phone dies. RESOLUTION: The system relies on incremental server pings (every 60 seconds) to ensure at least partial time is credited to their lifetime total.

E-02: Simultaneous Cross-Device Sessions. User tries to run a session on their phone and web browser simultaneously to farm hours. RESOLUTION:

Backend detects concurrent active sessions for the same user ID and only logs the time of the primary/first session.

E-03: Zero-Input Time Logging. User starts a 5-minute session but remains completely silent, letting the timer run out. RESOLUTION: System logs the session as "Incomplete" and credits 0 minutes to the total lifetime practice time.

Validation Test Cases

 Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

 TC-0 01

Complete valid session

5 minutes accurately added to lifetime dashboard total.

 TC-0 02

Cross a milestone

App displays celebration UI and unlocks trophy badge.

 TC-0 03

Concurrent session farming

System rejects duplicate time logging from a second device.

 TC-0 04

Silent session timeout

System rejects time credit for sessions with zero audio/text input.

 TC-0 05

App crash recovery

Partial time (up to the last 60s ping) is successfully logged.

LPM-US-05: Learning Path Management

STATUS: In Development PRIORITY: High ACTOR: Administrator

Intent: To create, sequence, and manage structured learning journeys so users receive content logically rather than randomly.

Happy Path Steps

Dashboard Access: Admin logs into the portal and navigates to "Learning Paths".

Creation: Admin clicks "Create New Path" (e.g., "Interview Prep Mastery").

Sequencing: Admin drags and drops existing modules and scenarios into a logical sequence (Step 1, Step 2, etc.).

Publication: Admin saves and publishes the path.

User View: Learners immediately see the newly structured path available on their dashboard.

Acceptance Criteria

Admins must be able to lock sequential modules (User cannot do Step 2 until Step 1 is done).

The system must allow paths to be updated dynamically without requiring an app store update.

Exception Handling

E-01: Empty Path Publication. Admin attempts to publish a path with zero modules attached. RESOLUTION: UI disables the "Publish" button and highlights an error: "A path must contain at least one module."

E-02: Deletion of Active Module. Admin tries to delete a scenario that is currently part of an active Learning Path. RESOLUTION: System blocks deletion and warns: "This module is active in 'Interview Prep Mastery'. Remove it from the path first."

E-03: Circular Dependency. Admin accidentally sets Module A to require Module B, and Module B to require Module A. RESOLUTION: Logic validation blocks the save action and highlights the conflicting rules.

E-04: Concurrent Admin Editing. Two admins try to edit the same learning path simultaneously. RESOLUTION: Implement record locking; second admin sees a "Locked for editing by [Name]" badge.

LPM-US-06: Learning Path Progress Persistence (Pause & Resume)

STATUS: In Development PRIORITY: Medium ACTOR: Learner

Intent: To pause a scenario or learning module mid-way (due to interruption) and resume exactly where they left off, ensuring progress is not lost.

Happy Path Steps

Active Session: User is 3 minutes into a 10-minute Mock Interview.

Interruption: User receives a phone call or closes the app manually.

State Save: System captures the current context window, question index, and uploaded audio buffers, saving them to the backend database.

Return: User opens the app 2 hours later. Dashboard displays a "Resume Interview" banner.

Restoration: User clicks resume; AI acknowledges the return (e.g., "Welcome back, we were discussing your background") and asks the next question.

Acceptance Criteria

Session state must be saved server-side, not just cached locally, to allow resuming on a different device.

The AI must retain the memory/context of the conversation prior to the interruption.

Exception Handling

E-01: Abandoned Session Expiration. User pauses an interview but does not return for 7 days. RESOLUTION: System clears the active state cache to save server resources and resets the module to the beginning.

E-02: Audio Processing During Close. User force-closes the app exactly while an audio snippet is uploading to the AI. RESOLUTION: Upon resume, the AI prompts: "I didn't quite catch your last answer before you left. Could you repeat it?"

E-03: Admin Deletes Module Mid-Pause. An admin deletes or completely overwrites a scenario while the user has it paused. RESOLUTION: System catches the version mismatch upon resume, displays "This scenario has been updated," and restarts the module with the new content.

 TC-0 02

Pause and resume device)

(cross- User starts on mobile, closes app, resumes exact state on web.

State is cleared; user must restart the module from scratch.

AI prompts the user to repeat the interrupted answer.

Exception Handling

E-02: Admin Edits Live Path Sequence. User is on Module 2, but an Admin inserts a new "Module 1.5" into the path. RESOLUTION: The new module appears in the path, but the user is "grandfathered" in and maintains access to Module 2 without being forced backward.

E-03: Enterprise Override. A manager wants an employee to skip directly to Module 5. RESOLUTION: Admins can manually click "Unlock All" for specific users within the Enterprise Learning Dashboard.

LPM-US-08: End-to-End Learning Path Completion & Certification

Intent: To complete the final module of a structured Learning Path and receive a conclusive summary of their journey, proving they have mastered the assigned skill (e.g., "Workplace Communication Mastery").

Acceptance Criteria

The system must validate that 100% of the modules in the path are marked "Complete" before triggering the end-state celebration.

The Summary Card must be exportable/shareable to drive viral acquisition and validate the user's effort.

Exception Handling

The dashboard redirects the user to the missing module with a prompt: "You're almost there! Complete Module 4 to finish your path."

E-02: Path Updated Mid-Journey. An admin added a new module to the path just as the user finished what used to be the final module. RESOLUTION: The user is grandfathered in. They receive the completion celebration for the version of the path they started. The new module appears as an optional "Bonus Challenge."

E-03: Share API Failure. User attempts to share their Summary Card to LinkedIn, but the OS native sharing sheet fails to load. RESOLUTION: App automatically saves the Summary Card image to the device's local photo gallery as a fallback, showing a "Saved to Camera Roll" toast.

CM-US-03: Content Management - Target Vocabulary Builder

STATUS: In Development PRIORITY: Medium ACTOR: Administrator

Intent: To define, update, and manage the specific lists of expected vocabulary tied to different scenarios (e.g., Airport, Restaurant) so content remains relevant and challenging.

Happy Path Steps

206. Navigation: Admin opens the Content Management dashboard and selects an existing Scenario template.

208. Save Action: Admin clicks "Save and Deploy".

209. Result: The updated vocabulary list is instantly pushed to the mobile application for all subsequent learner sessions in that scenario.

Acceptance Criteria

•             Admin must be able to assign 5-15 target words per scenario.

•             The system must validate that the entered words are spelled correctly before saving.

Exception Handling

•             E-01: Empty Vocabulary List. Admin tries to save a scenario without defining any target words. RESOLUTION: System prevents saving and shows an error: "Scenario-based learning requires at least 3 target vocabulary words."

•             E-02: Duplicate Words Entered. Admin accidentally types "customs, baggage, customs". RESOLUTION: System auto-deduplicates the list upon save and displays a minor toast notification: "Duplicate words removed."

•             E-03: Profanity in Target List. Admin maliciously or accidentally enters a profanity into the target word list. RESOLUTION: Backend profanity filter blocks the save and flags the word with a severe UI warning.

•             E-04: Exceeding Word Limit. Admin tries to add 50 words to a single 5-minute scenario. RESOLUTION: UI restricts input at 15 words to prevent overwhelming the learner and the evaluation prompt.

CM-US-04: Content Management - Scenario Versioning & Rollback

STATUS: In Development PRIORITY: Medium ACTOR: Administrator

Intent: To safely update conversation templates and scenarios without disrupting users who are actively practicing in those scenarios.

Happy Path Steps

227. Navigation: Admin opens Content Management and edits an existing scenario (e.g., "Restaurant").

228. Version Creation: Admin adds new expected vocabulary and saves the changes.

229. Deployment: System increments the scenario version from v1.0 to v1.1.

230. Seamless Routing: Users starting a new session are routed to v1.1. Users currently mid-conversation in v1.0 complete their session without interruption.

Acceptance Criteria

•             Scenario updates must not force a mobile app update via the App Store/Play Store.

•             The system must maintain older versions of a scenario in the database for active session completion.

Exception Handling

•             E-01: Critical Scenario Bug. Admin deploys a broken prompt that causes the AI to respond in gibberish. RESOLUTION: Admin clicks "Rollback," which instantly reverts new traffic to the previous stable version while flagging the broken version for review.

•             E-02: Outdated Client App. User's mobile app is 6 months out of date and cannot parse the new scenario JSON structure. RESOLUTION: API detects the app version and serves the legacy v1.0 scenario to prevent app crashes.

•             E-03: Deleting an Active Scenario. Admin attempts to completely delete a scenario that 50 users are currently utilizing. RESOLUTION: System changes status to "Archived" rather than hard-deleting, removing it from the UI but keeping the database record intact for active users.

•             E-04: Concurrent Template Editing. Two admins try to overwrite the same "Restaurant" template at the exact same time. RESOLUTION: Last-write-wins logic applies, but the system stores version histories so the overwritten data can be restored if needed.

Platform Analytics Dashboard (Admin)

PAD-US-01: Role-Based Access Control & Data Scoping for the Analytics Dashboard

STATUS: Proposed   PRIORITY: High   ACTOR: Super Admin / Platform Owner

Intent: To restrict analytics dashboard modules (e.g., Revenue, Cohort detail) based on an admin's assigned role, so support/junior admins cannot view sensitive financial or user-level data they are not authorized to see.

Happy Path Steps

Role Assignment: Super Admin assigns a role (e.g., "Support Admin", "Growth Admin", "Finance Admin") to a new admin account.

Login: Admin logs into the Analytics Dashboard.

Scoped Rendering: System renders only the modules/tabs permitted for that role (e.g., a Support Admin sees Drop-off Funnel but not Revenue).

Restricted Attempt: Admin attempts to navigate directly to a restricted module via URL.

Enforcement: System blocks the request and redirects to an authorized default view.

Acceptance Criteria

Dashboard must dynamically hide or disable UI modules based on a role-permission matrix, not just visually collapse them.

Backend API endpoints must independently enforce the same role restrictions, so client-side hiding is never the only safeguard.

Exception Handling

E-01: Direct URL/API Access Attempt. An admin without Revenue permission manually navigates to the Revenue endpoint. RESOLUTION: Server returns a 403, and the UI redirects to the permitted default dashboard with a "You don't have access to this section" notice.

E-02: Role Changed Mid-Session. A Super Admin downgrades an admin's role while that admin has the dashboard open. RESOLUTION: The next API call re-validates permissions and forces a UI refresh (or logout) if the admin is no longer authorized for the open view.

E-03: Conflicting Role Grants. Two assigned roles grant contradictory permissions (allow vs. deny) for the same module. RESOLUTION: System applies a "most restrictive wins" rule by default.

E-04: Orphaned Admin Account. The role assigned to an admin account is deleted from the system. RESOLUTION: The account automatically falls back to a "No Access" default state, and the Super Admin is notified to reassign a role.

E-05: Last Super Admin Lockout. An attempt is made to deactivate or downgrade the only remaining Super Admin account. RESOLUTION: System blocks the action, requiring at least one active Super Admin at all times.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-01

Support Admin views dashboard

Only permitted modules render; Revenue tab is absent.

TC-02

Direct navigation to restricted module

Request is rejected server-side (403) and UI redirects with a notice.

TC-03

Role downgraded mid-session

Open session loses access to now-restricted modules on next action.

TC-04

Conflicting role permissions

Most restrictive permission is applied.

TC-05

Attempt to deactivate last Super Admin

Action is blocked with an explanatory error.

PAD-US-02: PII Protection & Data Anonymization in Analytics Views

STATUS: Proposed   PRIORITY: High   ACTOR: Administrator / Compliance

Intent: To ensure analytics views display aggregated, anonymized data by default so no admin can casually browse an individual user's private conversation content or personal identifiers, protecting user privacy and supporting regulatory compliance.

Happy Path Steps

Default View: Admin opens the Feature Usage or Retention module.

Aggregation: System displays only aggregate counts/percentages, never individual names, emails, or transcripts.

Escalation Request: Admin needs to investigate a specific support ticket and requests elevated access to a single user's record.

Secondary Approval: System requires a documented reason and secondary admin approval before revealing identifiable data.

Logging: The elevated access event is recorded to the audit trail.

Acceptance Criteria

All default dashboard views must aggregate data to a minimum cohort size (e.g., 5+ users) and must never reveal a breakdown that could indirectly identify a single user.

Access to an individual user-level record must require a documented justification and secondary authorization before being granted.

Exception Handling

E-01: Small-Cohort De-Anonymization Risk. A filter combination returns only one or two matching users. RESOLUTION: System suppresses the exact breakdown and displays "Result set too small to display" instead of exact counts.

E-02: Unauthorized Drill-Down Attempt. An admin without elevated clearance tries to open an individual user's conversation transcript from analytics. RESOLUTION: The action is blocked, the attempt is logged, and the admin is prompted to submit an elevated-access request.

E-03: PII Leakage in Export. A CSV export inadvertently includes user emails or account IDs. RESOLUTION: The export pipeline strips or hashes identifiable fields unless the exporting admin holds explicit PII-export permission.

E-04: Cross-Border Data Residency Conflict. An admin in one region requests data on users whose records must legally remain in another jurisdiction. RESOLUTION: System serves only pre-aggregated, region-compliant summaries; raw records are withheld.

E-05: Approval Timeout. The secondary approver does not respond to an elevated-access request within SLA. RESOLUTION: The request auto-expires after 24 hours and the requesting admin must resubmit.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-01

View default retention module

Only aggregated, non-identifiable data is shown.

TC-02

Filter returns 1-2 users

UI suppresses the count and shows a "too small to display" message.

TC-03

Unauthorized drill-down attempt

Action blocked and logged; access-request prompt shown.

TC-04

CSV export by non-PII-permitted admin

Identifiable fields are stripped or hashed in the file.

TC-05

Elevated access approval expires

Request auto-expires after 24 hours and must be resubmitted.

PAD-US-03: Automated Anomaly Detection & Proactive Alerting

STATUS: Proposed   PRIORITY: High   ACTOR: Administrator / Growth Team

Intent: To automatically detect abnormal shifts in key metrics (churn spike, signup drop, revenue dip) and proactively notify relevant admins, rather than relying solely on manual dashboard checks.

Happy Path Steps

Monitoring: System continuously compares live metrics against historical baselines.

Threshold Breach: A metric (e.g., Day-1 retention) drops beyond a configured threshold versus its rolling average.

Alert Trigger: System sends an alert (email/push/Slack) to designated admins.

Deep Link: Admin opens the alert, which links directly to the dashboard view pre-filtered to the anomalous window.

Acknowledgement: Admin reviews the anomaly and marks the alert "Reviewed."

Acceptance Criteria

Anomaly-detection thresholds must be configurable per metric by an authorized admin.

Every alert must deep link directly to the relevant filtered dashboard view rather than the generic dashboard homepage.

Exception Handling

E-01: Alert Storm. A single upstream outage triggers many simultaneous anomaly alerts across unrelated metrics. RESOLUTION: System groups related alerts into one digest notification (e.g., "5 metrics affected by a suspected outage at 14:02 UTC") instead of flooding admins with separate alerts.

E-02: False Positive from Seasonal Pattern. An expected weekend dip in usage is flagged as an anomaly. RESOLUTION: The detection model accounts for day-of-week and seasonal baselines, and admins can mark an alert "False Positive" to retrain the thresholds.

E-03: Notification Channel Failure. The configured Slack webhook is broken or unreachable. RESOLUTION: System falls back to email delivery and logs the channel failure for Super Admin review.

E-04: No Owner Configured. An anomaly triggers but no recipient is assigned for that metric. RESOLUTION: The alert is still logged in an in-app "Unassigned Alerts" queue, and the Super Admin is notified to assign ownership.

E-05: Persistent Ongoing Anomaly. The same anomaly continues across multiple checking intervals. RESOLUTION: System suppresses repeat alerts for the same ongoing incident and sends a single resolution notice once the metric normalizes.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-01

Metric breaches configured threshold

Alert is generated and delivered to configured admins.

TC-02

Multiple metrics breach simultaneously

Alerts are grouped into a single digest notification.

TC-03

Expected weekend dip occurs

No false anomaly alert is triggered.

TC-04

Slack webhook unreachable

Alert falls back to email and failure is logged.

TC-05

Same anomaly persists 3 checks in a row

Only one alert plus one resolution notice are sent, not repeats.

PAD-US-04: Scheduled Report Generation & Distribution

STATUS: Proposed   PRIORITY: Medium   ACTOR: Administrator

Intent: To let admins configure recurring analytics report packages that are automatically generated and emailed to stakeholders, removing the need for manual dashboard exports on a routine cadence.

Happy Path Steps

Template Setup: Admin configures a report template: chosen metrics, date-range type (e.g., "last 7 days"), and a recipient list.

Recurrence: Admin sets a recurrence schedule (e.g., every Monday 9 AM).

Generation: System auto-generates the report (PDF/CSV) at the scheduled time.

Distribution: Report is emailed to the configured recipients.

History: Admin can view a history of previously sent reports.

Acceptance Criteria

Scheduled reports must be rendered from the same live data pipeline as the interactive dashboard, so figures never diverge from what the dashboard would show.

The recipient list must support both internal admin accounts and external stakeholder email addresses.

Exception Handling

E-01: Report Generation Failure. A data-pipeline error prevents the report from rendering at the scheduled time. RESOLUTION: System retries generation twice, then sends a "Report generation failed — view the dashboard directly" notice to the report owner instead of failing silently.

E-02: Recipient Email Bounce. A stakeholder's email address is invalid or bounces. RESOLUTION: The failed delivery is flagged in the report history log and the admin owner is notified, without blocking delivery to the other valid recipients.

E-03: Schedule Edited Mid-Run. An admin edits the recurrence schedule while a report is mid-generation. RESOLUTION: The edit is queued and applied only after the in-progress run completes.

E-04: Sensitive Data Sent Externally. A report configured to include Revenue data is addressed to an external, non-employee domain. RESOLUTION: System shows a confirmation warning before allowing financial data to be distributed outside the organization.

E-05: Time Zone Misalignment. An admin configuring a "9 AM" schedule is unaware of a mismatch between server time and their local time zone. RESOLUTION: The schedule UI explicitly displays and lets the admin select the time zone the schedule runs in.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-01

Weekly report runs on schedule

Report generates and is emailed to all recipients at the configured time.

TC-02

Data pipeline error during generation

System retries, then notifies the owner of failure without a silent miss.

TC-03

One recipient email bounces

Failure is logged; other recipients still receive the report.

TC-04

External recipient added to Revenue report

Admin sees a confirmation warning before send.

TC-05

Schedule edited while report is generating

Change is applied only after current run finishes.

PAD-US-05: Regional / Locale-Based Segmentation Analytics

STATUS: Proposed   PRIORITY: Medium   ACTOR: Administrator

Intent: To segment platform metrics by country, language variant, or subscription tier, enabling admins to compare engagement and retention across markets.

Happy Path Steps

Segment Selection: Admin opens the Analytics Dashboard and selects "Segment by Region."

Rollup: System groups core metrics (retention, revenue, feature usage) by country/locale.

Comparison: Admin compares two regions side by side (e.g., retention curves).

Drill-down: Admin drills into a single region to see localized feature adoption.

Acceptance Criteria

Segmentation must use precomputed regional rollups rather than re-querying raw data per region, to keep the view responsive.

Comparative views must clearly label each region/segment in chart legends and axis labels.

Exception Handling

E-01: Low-Volume Region. A region has fewer users than the minimum reporting threshold. RESOLUTION: The individual regional breakdown is suppressed ("Insufficient data for this region") and rolled into an "Other Regions" bucket instead.

E-02: Missing Locale Data. A user's region/locale field is null due to a signup bug. RESOLUTION: These users are bucketed under "Unknown Region" rather than silently dropped from totals.

E-03: Suspected Location Spoofing. An abnormal share of users shows a mismatch between IP-inferred location and declared locale. RESOLUTION: The affected regional data is flagged with a confidence caveat rather than presented as fully reliable.

E-04: Currency Mismatch Across Regions. Revenue segmented by region shows in inconsistent local currencies. RESOLUTION: All figures are normalized to a base currency before regional comparison charts render.
