PAD-US-06: Period-over-Period Comparative Analysis (WoW / MoM / YoY)

STATUS: Proposed   PRIORITY: Medium   ACTOR: Administrator

Intent: To show percentage-change indicators comparing the current reporting period against a prior equivalent period, so admins can judge trend direction without manually cross-referencing two date ranges.

Happy Path Steps

Metric View: Admin views a core metric card (e.g., Active Users).

Toggle Comparison: Admin enables "Compare to previous period."

Delta Display: System shows the current value alongside a delta indicator (e.g., "+12% vs. last 30 days").

Basis Switch: Admin switches the comparison basis between WoW, MoM, and YoY.

Acceptance Criteria

Delta indicators must show both direction and magnitude using an icon plus numeric value, not color alone, to remain accessible.

The comparison period length must always match the primary period length exactly (e.g., 30 days vs. the prior 30 days).

Exception Handling

E-01: Insufficient Historical Data. The platform launched only 20 days ago and a YoY comparison is requested. RESOLUTION: Unavailable comparison options are disabled and the UI displays "Not enough historical data" instead of a misleading delta.

E-02: Comparison Period Includes a Known Outage. The historical baseline period had a data-collection gap. RESOLUTION: The comparison is flagged with a footnote noting the affected dates so the delta is not misread as a genuine trend.

E-03: Month-Length Mismatch. A MoM comparison spans February (28 days) against a 31-day month. RESOLUTION: System normalizes by comparable day-counts, or clearly labels the day-count mismatch rather than presenting a false percentage.

E-04: Divide-by-Zero on Prior Period. The prior period's value was zero (e.g., a new feature had 0 sessions before launch). RESOLUTION: System displays a "New" indicator rather than an undefined or broken percentage calculation.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-01

Toggle WoW comparison on Active Users

Correct delta percentage and direction icon render.

TC-02

YoY requested with <1 year of data

Option is disabled with an explanatory message.

TC-03

Baseline period includes an outage

Comparison card shows a data-gap footnote.

TC-04

Prior period value is zero

"New" indicator shown instead of a broken percentage.

PAD-US-07: Admin Action Audit Trail for Analytics Access & Data Exports

STATUS: Proposed   PRIORITY: High   ACTOR: Super Admin / Compliance Officer

Intent: To maintain a tamper-evident audit log of who viewed sensitive analytics data, applied filters, or exported reports, supporting internal compliance and post-incident investigation.

Happy Path Steps

Sensitive Action: An admin views a restricted module (e.g., Revenue) or performs a CSV export.

Silent Logging: System records the actor, timestamp, module/filters used, and action type to an audit log.

Review: A Compliance Officer or Super Admin opens the "Audit Log" view.

Investigation: Officer filters the log by admin, date, or action type to investigate an incident.

Acceptance Criteria

Audit log entries must be immutable and append-only, not editable or deletable by any admin — including Super Admins — through the standard UI.

Every data-export action must capture the exact data scope exported (filters, date range, module) alongside the actor and timestamp.

Exception Handling

E-01: Audit Logging Service Failure. The logging service is temporarily unavailable when an admin performs a sensitive export. RESOLUTION: System blocks the export action itself until logging succeeds, so no untracked export can occur ("fail closed").

E-02: Excessive Log Volume. High-frequency, trivial filter changes by an admin threaten to bloat the audit log. RESOLUTION: System debounces and batches routine view-only filter changes, logging only meaningful actions (exports, restricted-module access) in full detail.

E-03: Attempted Log Tampering. A direct database-level attempt is made to alter an existing audit entry. RESOLUTION: Log storage uses write-once, hash-chained records so any tampering is detectable.

E-04: Unauthorized Audit Log Access. A non-compliance admin attempts to open the audit log view. RESOLUTION: Audit log viewing is restricted to a dedicated Compliance/Super Admin role only.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-01

Admin exports Revenue data

Audit entry records actor, timestamp, and exact filters/scope exported.

TC-02

Logging service is down during export attempt

Export is blocked until logging succeeds.

TC-03

Attempt to edit an existing audit entry

Edit is rejected; tampering is detectable via hash chain.

TC-04

Non-compliance admin opens audit log

Access is denied per role restriction.

PAD-US-08: Custom Dashboard Layout & Saved Views

STATUS: Proposed   PRIORITY: Low   ACTOR: Administrator

Intent: To let individual admins pin frequently used widgets and save custom filter combinations as reusable views, reducing repetitive setup for recurring analysis tasks.

Happy Path Steps

Arrange: Admin arranges dashboard widgets and applies a specific filter set.

Save: Admin clicks "Save View" and names it (e.g., "Weekly Growth Review").

Reuse: The saved view appears in a personal dropdown for quick reload.

Restore: Admin reopens the dashboard later and selects the saved view; layout and filters restore instantly.

Acceptance Criteria

Saved views must be personal and private by default, visible only to the creating admin unless explicitly shared.

Restoring a saved view must reapply both the widget layout and all active filters exactly as they were saved.

Exception Handling

E-01: Widget Deprecated After Save. A saved view references a metric/widget that has since been removed from the platform. RESOLUTION: On load, the system shows a placeholder ("This widget is no longer available") and lets the admin remove it without breaking the rest of the view.

E-02: Saved Filter References Deleted Segment. A saved filter targets a region or cohort tag that was later deleted. RESOLUTION: System falls back to "All" for that filter dimension and notifies the admin that the original segment no longer exists.

E-03: Shared View Permission Mismatch. Admin A shares a view with Admin B, but Admin B's role lacks permission to see one of the included modules (e.g., Revenue). RESOLUTION: The restricted widget is hidden for Admin B according to their role, rather than implicitly granting elevated access.

E-04: Naming Collision. Admin tries to save a view under a name that already exists in their personal list. RESOLUTION: System prompts the admin to overwrite the existing view or choose a new name.

Validation Test Cases

Expected Result

TC-02

Placeholder shown; rest of view loads normally.

TC-03

Restricted widgets are hidden per role, no elevated access granted.

TC-04

PAD-US-09: Cross-Source Data Reconciliation (Analytics Engine vs. Payment Provider)

STATUS: Proposed   PRIORITY: High   ACTOR: Administrator / Finance

Intent: To detect and surface discrepancies between the platform's internal analytics counts (subscriptions, active payers) and the payment provider's reported figures, preventing silent financial reporting errors.

Happy Path Steps

Nightly Job: A reconciliation job compares internal subscription/revenue counts against Stripe/Apple/Google reported totals.

Match: Figures match within an acceptable tolerance (e.g., under 1% variance due to timing).

Status Badge: Dashboard displays a green "Reconciled" status badge on the Revenue module.

Detail View: Admin can open the reconciliation detail log on demand.

Acceptance Criteria

Reconciliation must run automatically at least once daily and compare each payment provider (Stripe, Apple, Google) separately.

Any variance beyond the configured tolerance must be visibly flagged on the dashboard itself, not only recorded in a background log.

Exception Handling

E-01: Variance Exceeds Tolerance. The internal count shows 500 active subscribers while the provider reports 470. RESOLUTION: The Revenue module displays a "Data Discrepancy Detected" warning badge linking to the detailed line-item comparison, and finance admins are notified.

E-02: Provider API Unavailable. The payment provider's API is temporarily unreachable during the reconciliation run. RESOLUTION: The job retries on a backoff schedule and the dashboard shows "Reconciliation pending" rather than a false "Reconciled" or "Discrepancy" status.

E-03: Timing-Window Mismatch. A subscription that renews just before the internal daily cutoff is recorded by the provider a few minutes later. RESOLUTION: The reconciliation window includes a rolling grace buffer before flagging timing-only mismatches as true discrepancies.

E-04: Unsynced Refund/Chargeback. The provider reports a refund that has not yet synced to internal churn metrics. RESOLUTION: System queues a targeted re-sync for the affected user record rather than requiring a full data reload.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-01

Nightly reconciliation within tolerance

Dashboard shows a green "Reconciled" badge.

TC-02

Variance exceeds tolerance

Warning badge appears with a link to the detailed comparison.

TC-03

Payment provider API down during job

Dashboard shows "Reconciliation pending", job retries on backoff.

TC-04

Refund not yet synced internally

Targeted re-sync corrects the affected record without a full reload.

Enterprise Administration & Team Management



ENT-US-01: Sub-Admin / Role-Based Access Control (Department Manager Role)

STATUS: Proposed (Gap)   PRIORITY: High   ACTOR: Organization Owner / Admin

Intent: To create and manage secondary admin roles (e.g., "Department Manager") with scoped, permissioned access limited to their own team's data, rather than granting full organization-wide visibility to every admin account.

Happy Path Steps

1.        Owner navigates to "Admin Roles & Permissions" in Enterprise settings.

2.        Owner clicks "Add Admin" and selects a role type: Full Admin, Department Manager, or Read-Only Viewer.

3.        Owner assigns the new admin to one or more specific teams/departments.

4.        New admin receives an invite email; upon login, the dashboard is scoped only to assigned teams.

5.        Owner can modify or revoke the admin's permissions at any time.

Acceptance Criteria

●       Admin roles must enforce strict data scoping (a Manager cannot view other departments' employees).

●       Only the Full Admin/Owner role can create or modify other admin accounts.

●       Permission changes must take effect immediately, without requiring the affected admin to re-login.

Exception Handling

E-01: Privilege Escalation Attempt. A Department Manager tries to access org-wide settings via direct URL manipulation. RESOLUTION: 403 Forbidden; redirect to the scoped dashboard.

E-02: Orphaned Team. Owner removes the only admin assigned to a department. RESOLUTION: Department is flagged "Unmanaged"; Owner is prompted to assign a new manager.

E-03: Conflicting Scope Assignment. An admin is assigned to overlapping teams (e.g., Team A and Team A-East). RESOLUTION: System merges the permission set; access defaults to the broadest scope granted.

E-04: Last Owner Removal. An attempt is made to demote or remove the sole remaining Full Admin/Owner. RESOLUTION: Action is blocked; at least one Full Admin/Owner must exist at all times.

E-05: Role Downgrade Mid-Session. Owner downgrades a Manager to Read-Only while that Manager is actively assigning a path. RESOLUTION: The current session completes read actions only; write actions are blocked with a "Permissions changed - refresh to continue" notice.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-01

Assign Manager role scoped to Team A

Manager dashboard displays only Team A data.

TC-02

Manager attempts cross-team URL access

403 Forbidden is returned and access is blocked.

TC-03

Remove the last Full Admin

System blocks removal and displays a warning.

TC-04

Downgrade admin mid-session

Active write actions are blocked; read-only access persists.

TC-05

Owner edits a Manager's team scope

Manager's dashboard updates without requiring re-login.

 

ENT-US-02: SSO / SCIM-Based Identity Provisioning

STATUS: Proposed (Gap)   PRIORITY: High   ACTOR: Organization Admin / IT Department

Intent: To integrate with corporate identity providers (Okta, Azure AD, Google Workspace) so employee accounts are automatically provisioned and deprovisioned based on HR system status, removing reliance on manual CSV uploads for onboarding and offboarding.

Happy Path Steps

1.        Admin/IT navigates to "Integrations" and selects an SSO/SCIM provider.

2.        Admin authenticates and links the Enterprise org to the identity provider (IdP) tenant.

3.        The IdP pushes the user list via SCIM; matching employees are auto-provisioned with Enterprise access.

4.        When an employee is removed or disabled in the IdP, the system auto-revokes their Speeky-AI license within a defined sync window.

5.        Admin views a sync status log confirming provisioning and deprovisioning events.

Acceptance Criteria

●       SSO login must be enforceable org-wide when enabled, disabling direct email/password login for members.

●       Deprovisioning via SCIM must trigger the same license-release flow as a manual revocation.

●       Sync failures must be visibly logged with retry capability, never silently dropped.

Exception Handling

E-01: SCIM Sync Failure. The IdP push fails due to a malformed payload. RESOLUTION: The failed record is logged in a Sync Error report; the admin is notified by email while other records continue processing.

E-02: Duplicate Identity. An employee exists both via manual invite and SCIM push. RESOLUTION: System matches on verified email and merges to a single account, preserving practice history.

E-03: IdP Outage. The identity provider is unreachable during a scheduled sync. RESOLUTION: System retains the last-known-good state, retries with exponential backoff, and displays a "Sync Delayed" banner on the dashboard.

E-04: Seat Limit Exceeded via Auto-Provision. A SCIM push adds more users than available licenses. RESOLUTION: Extra users are provisioned to a "Pending Activation" queue; admin is prompted to purchase additional seats.

E-05: SSO Lockout. Admin enables SSO enforcement, but IdP misconfiguration locks out all users, including the Admin. RESOLUTION: A time-limited emergency break-glass admin login, delivered via a separate secure channel, remains available.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-01

Link an Okta tenant

Employees are auto-provisioned matching the Okta group.

TC-02

Disable an employee in the IdP

Speeky-AI license is auto-revoked within the sync window.

TC-03

Submit a malformed SCIM payload

Error is logged; other users remain unaffected.

TC-04

Exceed seats via SCIM push

New users are queued as Pending; admin is notified.

TC-05

IdP outage during a scheduled sync

Dashboard shows "Sync Delayed"; auto-retry succeeds once restored.

 

ENT-US-03: Organizational Structure - Department & Team Hierarchy Management

STATUS: Proposed (Gap)   PRIORITY: High   ACTOR: Organization Admin

Intent: To create, edit, and manage the team/department hierarchy referenced throughout the Enterprise dashboard (e.g., "Team A"), since no existing story defines how these groupings are actually created or maintained.

Happy Path Steps

1.        Admin navigates to "Org Structure" within the Manage Team section.

2.        Admin creates a new department/team (e.g., "Sales - APAC") and optionally assigns a sub-manager.

3.        Admin bulk-assigns or drags-and-drops employees into the new team.

4.        Each employee belongs to exactly one primary team, with optional secondary tags for cross-functional reporting.

5.        Dashboard metrics, leaderboards, and reports automatically re-aggregate along the updated hierarchy.

Acceptance Criteria

●       Teams must support a nested structure (Department > Sub-team) up to a defined depth limit.

●       Reassigning an employee to a new team must not erase their historical practice data.

●       Deleting a team must require reassignment or archiving of its members first.

Exception Handling

E-01: Deleting a Non-Empty Team. Admin attempts to delete a team with active employees. RESOLUTION: Deletion is blocked; admin is prompted to bulk-reassign members or archive the team instead.

E-02: Circular Hierarchy. Admin attempts to nest a department under its own sub-team. RESOLUTION: System validates hierarchy depth and rejects circular references with an inline error.

E-03: Bulk Reassignment Conflict. A CSV re-import assigns an employee to a team that has since been renamed or deleted. RESOLUTION: Unmatched rows are flagged in an "Unresolved Assignments" report for manual correction.

E-04: Duplicate Team Names. Admin creates a second team with an identical name. RESOLUTION: System appends a disambiguator (e.g., "Sales (2)") and warns the admin.

E-05: Historical Reporting Integrity. An employee moves from Team A to Team B mid-quarter. RESOLUTION: Historical ROI/completion data prior to the move stays attributed to Team A; only future data rolls up to Team B, preserving audit accuracy.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-01

Create a nested department

Hierarchy saves and displays correctly.

TC-02

Delete a team with active members

Deletion is blocked; reassignment prompt is shown.

TC-03

Create a circular nesting relationship

Request is rejected with a validation error.

TC-04

Move an employee mid-quarter

Past data stays with the original team; future data rolls to the new team.

TC-05

Create a team with a duplicate name

Name is auto-disambiguated on save.

 

ENT-US-04: Admin Audit Log & Activity History

STATUS: Proposed (Gap)   PRIORITY: Medium   ACTOR: Organization Admin / Compliance Officer

Intent: To maintain a tamper-evident log of all administrative actions (license revocations, path assignments, permission changes) for internal compliance and dispute resolution, since no existing story tracks admin-side actions.

Happy Path Steps

1.        Admin/Compliance Officer navigates to "Audit Log" in Enterprise settings.

2.        System displays a chronological, filterable list of admin actions (actor, action type, target, timestamp).

3.        Officer filters the log by date range, action type, or specific admin.

4.        Officer exports the log as a CSV for compliance records.

Acceptance Criteria

●       Every license, permission, and assignment change must generate an immutable log entry.

●       Log entries must capture actor identity, action, target employee/team, and a UTC timestamp.

●       Only the Full Admin/Owner or a designated Compliance role may view or export the audit log.

Exception Handling

E-01: Log Tampering Attempt. A request attempts to directly modify or delete a log entry via the API. RESOLUTION: Write access to audit records is disabled entirely after creation; the request is rejected at the database layer.

E-02: High-Volume Export. Compliance Officer exports two years of logs for a 5,000-seat org. RESOLUTION: Export is processed as a background job with a secure download link, matching the pattern used for ROI reporting.

E-03: Deleted Employee Reference. A log entry references an employee whose account was later deleted. RESOLUTION: The log retains an anonymized employee ID reference so the action history stays complete without exposing deleted PII.

E-04: Unauthorized Viewer. A Department Manager (non-Owner) attempts to view the org-wide audit log. RESOLUTION: Access is restricted to their own team's action history only, or fully blocked if the role lacks audit permission.

E-05: Clock Skew / Timestamp Dispute. Two near-simultaneous admin actions from different sessions appear out of order. RESOLUTION: The server-side timestamp, not the client's, is authoritative and logged with millisecond precision to preserve accurate sequencing.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-01

View the audit log

Chronological list of all admin actions is displayed.

TC-02

Filter by admin and date range

Results are correctly scoped to the filter.

TC-03

Export a 2-year log for a large org

Background job completes; secure link is emailed.

TC-04

Manager attempts an org-wide view

View is restricted to own team or fully blocked.

TC-05

Attempt to modify a log entry via API

Request is rejected; log remains immutable.

 

ENT-US-05: Multi-Admin Ownership & Account Transfer

STATUS: Proposed (Gap)   PRIORITY: Medium   ACTOR: Organization Owner / Admin

Intent: To allow an organization to add multiple full admins and transfer primary ownership when an HR/admin lead departs the company, preventing account lockout risk for the entire organization.

Happy Path Steps

1.        Owner navigates to "Admin Management" and selects "Add Full Admin."

2.        Owner enters a colleague's email; the colleague receives an invite and accepts Full Admin rights.

3.        Prior to departure, the outgoing Owner selects "Transfer Primary Ownership" and designates a successor.

4.        The successor receives a confirmation email and accepts the ownership transfer.

5.        Billing, license, and audit-log permissions move to the new Owner; the prior Owner is optionally demoted or removed.

Acceptance Criteria

●       An organization must always have at least one active Owner-level admin.

●       Ownership transfer must require confirmation from both the outgoing and incoming parties.

●       Billing/payment-method access transfers only upon successful completion of the transfer.

Exception Handling

E-01: Sole Owner Departs Without Transfer. The Owner's account is deactivated (e.g., offboarded by IT) before designating a successor. RESOLUTION: System auto-escalates the next most senior Full Admin to Owner, or flags the account for manual support-assisted recovery if none exists.

E-02: Incoming Party Declines. The successor does not accept the ownership transfer within 7 days. RESOLUTION: The transfer request expires and the outgoing Owner is prompted to select a different successor.

E-03: Simultaneous Transfer Requests. Owner initiates two competing transfer requests to different colleagues. RESOLUTION: Only the first accepted request is honored; the second is auto-invalidated with a notice.

E-04: Billing Dispute During Transfer. A payment fails mid-transfer. RESOLUTION: Ownership transfer is paused until billing is resolved; access roles remain unchanged in the interim.

E-05: Demoted Former Owner Retains Access. The former Owner is demoted to Manager post-transfer but still has stale team-wide permissions cached. RESOLUTION: All active sessions for the demoted account are force-invalidated at the moment the transfer completes.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-01

Add a second Full Admin

Colleague gains full admin rights upon acceptance.

TC-02

Transfer ownership to a successor

Successor confirms; billing/audit access moves accordingly.

TC-03

Successor ignores the request for 7+ days

Request expires; outgoing owner is re-prompted.

TC-04

Payment fails mid-transfer

Transfer is paused; roles stay unchanged until resolved.

TC-05

Demote former owner after transfer

Active sessions for that account are invalidated immediately.

 

ENT-US-06: Data Subject Deletion Request (GDPR / CCPA Compliance)

STATUS: Proposed (Gap)   PRIORITY: High   ACTOR: Organization Admin / Employee / Compliance Officer

Intent: To let an employee or Admin submit a full data-deletion request under privacy regulations (GDPR/CCPA), distinct from the account-deletion anonymization defined elsewhere in the dashboard, which only anonymizes but never truly erases underlying records.

Happy Path Steps

1.        Employee (or Admin on their behalf) submits a "Delete My Data" request via account settings.

2.        System routes the request to Org Admin/Compliance for review within the regulatory window.

3.        Admin approves the request.

4.        System permanently purges the employee's session recordings, transcripts, and identifiable records from all systems and backups within the compliance window.

5.        Confirmation of erasure is emailed to the requester and logged in the Audit Log.

Acceptance Criteria

●       Full deletion must remove data from primary databases and backups within the regulatory timeframe.

●       Aggregate/org-level ROI statistics must be recalculated to exclude the deleted employee's contribution, or retained only in fully anonymized form per applicable law.

●       The request and its resolution must be recorded in the immutable Audit Log.

Exception Handling

E-01: Conflicting Legal Hold. The employee is under an active litigation hold requiring data retention. RESOLUTION: Deletion is deferred; the requester is notified of the legal basis for the delay.

E-02: Admin Ignores the Request. Admin does not act within the regulatory review window. RESOLUTION: System auto-escalates and processes the deletion automatically once the deadline passes.

E-03: Partial Backup Purge Failure. A cold-storage backup fails to purge during the automated sweep. RESOLUTION: Failure is logged, retried on the next backup cycle, and the compliance officer is alerted if unresolved past the deadline.

E-04: Re-Invitation After Deletion. The employee is re-invited to the same org after their data was fully purged. RESOLUTION: The account is treated as brand-new, with no historical linkage restored.

E-05: Aggregate Metric Distortion. Removing an employee's data would measurably skew an already-published ROI report. RESOLUTION: Published historical reports remain intact as an immutable point-in-time record, with a footnote noting a subsequent deletion; only forward-looking aggregates exclude the deleted data.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-01

Submit a data deletion request

Request is routed to Admin/Compliance for review.

TC-02

Approve a deletion request

Data is purged within the compliance window; confirmation is sent.

TC-03

Legal hold is active on the employee

Deletion is deferred with a notice explaining why.

TC-04

Admin misses the review deadline

Deletion is auto-escalated and processed.

TC-05

A backup purge fails

Failure is logged, retried, and escalated if unresolved.

 

ENT-US-07: Enterprise Report & Communication Branding Configuration

STATUS: Proposed (Gap)   PRIORITY: Low   ACTOR: Organization Admin

Intent: To let an Admin configure the organization's logo, color scheme, and sender details used across exported ROI reports and employee-facing notification emails, since branding is referenced as an output elsewhere but is never actually configured.

Happy Path Steps

1.        Admin navigates to "Branding" under Enterprise settings.

2.        Admin uploads a company logo and selects a primary brand color.

3.        Admin sets a custom "From" display name for employee notification emails (e.g., "Acme Corp Learning Team").

4.        Admin saves the settings; all future ROI report exports and notification emails apply the new branding.

5.        Admin previews a sample report/email before publishing the changes org-wide.

Acceptance Criteria

●       Branding changes must apply to all newly generated exports/emails without requiring regeneration of historical reports.

●       Logo uploads must be validated for file type/size and must render correctly across PDF and email formats.

●       The preview must accurately reflect production output before the Admin commits changes.

Exception Handling

E-01: Invalid Logo Format. Admin uploads an unsupported file type or an oversized image. RESOLUTION: The upload is rejected with an inline error specifying accepted formats and size limits.

E-02: Low-Tier Restriction. A standard-tier org attempts to access custom branding, a Premium Enterprise feature. RESOLUTION: An upgrade/paywall modal is displayed, consistent with the existing tier-restriction pattern used for advanced ROI reporting.

E-03: Branding Change Mid-Export. Admin changes the logo while a scheduled bulk ROI export is already processing. RESOLUTION: The in-flight export completes using the branding active at export start time; only subsequent exports use the new branding.

E-04: Sender Domain Not Verified. Admin sets a custom "From" email domain that has not completed DNS/SPF verification. RESOLUTION: System falls back to the default sender address and flags a "Domain not verified" warning until DNS records are confirmed.

E-05: Accessibility Contrast Failure. Admin selects a brand color combination that fails WCAG contrast requirements for report text. RESOLUTION: System warns the admin and suggests a compliant alternative, but allows override with explicit acknowledgment.

Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-01

Upload a logo and set a brand color

Branding is applied to new exports and emails.

TC-02

Standard-tier org attempts branding access

Upgrade modal is shown.

TC-03

Change branding while an export is in-flight

In-flight export is unaffected; the next export uses new branding.

TC-04

Set an unverified sender domain

System falls back to default sender with a warning.

TC-05

Select a low-contrast color combination

Warning is shown; admin may override with acknowledgment.

Must ensure strict data separation (Org A cannot see Org B's data).

Exception Handling

E-02: Unassigned Employees. An employee is part of the org but has not been assigned a learning path. RESOLUTION: Highlight user in an "Unassigned" bucket on the dashboard with a prompt for the Admin to assign a path.

E-03: Data Rollup Latency. High volume of employee sessions causes the aggregated team score to lag. RESOLUTION: Display a "Data updated as of [Timestamp]" note to clarify potential latency.

E-04: Employee Account Deletion. An employee leaves the company and deletes their Speeky-AI account. RESOLUTION: Anonymize the historical data to preserve the Org's overall ROI metrics, but remove identifying information.

RESOLUTION: System batches the assignments in groups of 50 in the background and displays a "Processing assignments..." loader.

Exception Handling

E-02: Exceeding Seat Limits. Admin revokes 1 user but tries to invite 5 new users via CSV. RESOLUTION: System provisions the 1 available seat and queues the other 4 as "Pending," prompting the Admin to purchase more seats.

ENT-US-17: Enterprise Dashboard - Employee Course Completion Tracking

STATUS: In Development PRIORITY: High ACTOR: Organization Admin

Admin intervention (reminders) must be executed seamlessly within the platform.

RESOLUTION: The dashboard relies on real-time WebSockets or a manual refresh state to update the progress bar to 100% and mark the user as "Completed."

Privacy & Data Management



PRIV-US-01: User Data Export (GDPR/CCPA)

STATUS: In Development    PRIORITY: High    ACTOR: Learner

Intent: Export all personal data in a machine-readable format.

Happy Path Steps

1. Open Privacy Settings.

2. Select Export Data.

3. Verify identity.

4. System prepares encrypted archive.

5. Download link delivered.

Acceptance Criteria

Export contains profile, sessions, scores, transcripts and preferences.

Download link expires after 24 hours.

Identity verification mandatory.

Exception Handling

E-01: Identity Verification Failure

Trigger: User enters an incorrect OTP or fails identity verification before requesting a data export.

Resolution: The system immediately blocks the export request, logs the failed verification attempt for security auditing, and prompts the user to retry identity verification.



E-02: Export Generation Failure

Trigger: The backend fails while generating the downloadable archive due to a temporary processing error.

Resolution: The export request is placed in a retry queue, the user is notified that the export is being processed, and a notification is sent once the archive is ready.



E-03: Expired Download Link

Trigger: The user attempts to download the exported archive after the secure download link has expired.

Resolution: The expired link is invalidated and the user is provided with an option to generate a fresh secure download link.



E-04: Unauthorized Export Request

Trigger: A user attempts to export another user's data through a manipulated request.

Resolution: The request is rejected with an authorization error, the event is recorded in security logs, and suspicious activity monitoring is triggered.



E-05: Multiple Concurrent Export Requests

Trigger: The same user submits multiple export requests within a short period.

Resolution: Only the latest valid request is processed while previous duplicate requests are cancelled to reduce unnecessary processing.



Validation Test Cases

Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-001

Valid export

Archive generated.

TC-002

Wrong OTP

Export denied.

TC-003

Expired link

New link required.

TC-004

Retry export

Single archive created.

TC-005

Audit log

Event recorded.

PRIV-US-02: Consent Management

STATUS: In Development    PRIORITY: High    ACTOR: Learner

Intent: Manage consent for analytics, AI training and marketing.

Happy Path Steps

1. Open Consent Center.

2. Modify preferences.

3. Confirm.

4. System stores consent version.

5. Changes applied immediately.

Acceptance Criteria

Consent versioned.

Withdrawal effective immediately.

Legal consents retained.

Exception Handling

• E-01: Session Expired

Trigger: The user changes consent preferences after the login session has expired.

Resolution: The system redirects the user to sign in again before saving any privacy preferences.



E-02: Database Timeout

Trigger: The consent record cannot be stored due to a temporary database timeout.

Resolution: The system retries automatically and informs the user if manual retry is required.



E-03: Policy Version Conflict

Trigger: The privacy policy has been updated while the user is editing preferences.

Resolution: The latest policy is displayed and the user is asked to review and confirm the updated version.



E-04: Offline Update

Trigger: The device loses internet connectivity while consent preferences are being updated.

Resolution: The changes are stored locally and synchronized automatically after connectivity is restored.

PRIV-US-03: Account Deletion & Right to be Forgotten

STATUS: In Development    PRIORITY: High    ACTOR: Learner

Intent: Permanently delete account.

Happy Path Steps

1. Request deletion.

2. Verify identity.

3. Review consequences.

4. Grace period starts.

5. Data deleted after expiry.

Acceptance Criteria

Grace period supported.

Legal records excluded where required.

Deletion irreversible after expiry.

Exception Handling

•E-01: Active Subscription

Trigger: The user requests account deletion while an active subscription exists.

Resolution: The system informs the user about the subscription status and requests cancellation before permanent deletion.



E-02: Identity Verification Failure

Trigger: The entered password or verification code is incorrect.

Resolution: The deletion request is rejected until identity verification succeeds.



E-03: Grace Period Recovery

Trigger: The user changes their mind during the grace period.

Resolution: The deletion request is cancelled and the account is fully restored.



E-04: Data Purge Failure

Trigger: Some user records cannot be deleted because of a temporary backend failure.

Resolution: The system retries the deletion process automatically and alerts administrators if manual intervention is required.



E-05: Compliance Hold

Trigger: Certain financial or legal records must be retained due to regulatory requirements.

Resolution: Only legally required records are retained while all remaining personal information is permanently deleted.

Scenario

Expected Result

TC-002

Cancel request

Account restored.

TC-003

Grace expires

Data deleted.

TC-004

Enterprise account

Admin workflow.

Audit

Deletion logged.

PRIV-US-06: Privacy & Audio Data Deletion Request

STATUS: In Development PRIORITY: High ACTOR: Learner

Intent: To manage their personal privacy by requesting the permanent deletion of their recorded voice and video data from the platform's servers.

Happy Path Steps

Navigation: User navigates to Settings ➔ Privacy & Data.

Action: User taps "Delete My Audio/Video Recordings".

Confirmation: System displays a high-friction confirmation modal explaining that deleting recordings will disable the ability to replay past sessions or track historical waveform data.

Execution: User types "DELETE" to confirm.

Processing: System scrubs all raw .wav/.mp4 files from the cloud storage buckets but retains the anonymized numerical scores (Confidence, Fluency) to preserve overall progress tracking.

Acceptance Criteria

The deletion must physically remove the media files from S3/cloud storage, not just hide them in the UI.

The user's historical metadata and text transcripts must be retained to maintain their Progress Dashboard metrics.

Exception Handling

E-01: Active Processing Conflict. User requests deletion exactly while a background video upload is currently being processed by the AI. RESOLUTION:

System queues the deletion request, allows the processing to finish, logs the score, and immediately scrubs the file.

E-02: Enterprise Data Retention Policy. An Enterprise employee attempts to delete their recordings, but their company has a strict 90-day retention policy for ROI auditing. RESOLUTION: System blocks manual deletion and displays: "Your organization manages your data retention settings. Please contact your administrator."

E-03: Complete Account Deletion. User selects "Delete Entire Account" rather than just recordings. RESOLUTION: System permanently drops the user row, anonymizes all scores, and scrubs all media files within 72 hours per GDPR/CCPA compliance.

Validation Test Cases

 Case ID

Scenario

Expected Result

 TC-0 01

Valid audio deletion request

Media files removed from server; historical scores remain visible.

 TC-0 02

Confirmation modal

UI requires explicit text confirmation before deleting.

 TC-0 03

Attempt playback post- deletion

Waveform and playback buttons are disabled on past scorecards.

 TC-0 04

Enterprise policy block

System prevents manual deletion if corporate policy overrides.

 TC-0 05

Complete account deletion

All PII, media, and identifiable metadata are purged within SLA.
